A custom stripped-down collector configuration (`OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE`) containing only the OTLP HTTP receiver and AWS X-Ray exporter reduces the Extension's memory footprint from ~50MB to ~35MB, freeing headroom within the 512MB allocation.
- **(Round 7)** Why `BatchSpanProcessor` instead of `SimpleSpanProcessor` for the SSE Lambda? `SimpleSpanProcessor` exports each span synchronously — every DynamoDB query span blocks on an OTLP HTTP POST to localhost before the next query executes, adding per-span latency to the streaming response. `BatchSpanProcessor` buffers spans and exports asynchronously every 1000ms (per FR-073; default is 5000ms — corrected from original 200ms assumption, see FR-084), requiring `force_flush()` at stream end (FR-055). For latency-sensitive streaming, `BatchSpanProcessor` is the correct choice — the 1000ms batch interval is negligible relative to the 15-second streaming lifecycle, and async export prevents span creation from blocking the response.
- **(Round 7)** What happens when `TracerProvider` is mistakenly created per invocation instead of as a module-level singleton? Each `TracerProvider()` instantiation spawns a new `BatchSpanProcessor` daemon thread and opens a new OTLP HTTP connection to ADOT. Previous instances are not garbage-collected (daemon threads hold references). After N warm invocations, the execution environment has N orphaned threads consuming ~N MB of memory. Eventually, Lambda hits its 512MB memory limit and OOM-terminates the environment. This is why FR-065 clarifies that FR-059's per-invocation requirement applies ONLY to `propagate.extract()`, not to infrastructure objects.
- **(Round 7)** What happens with the ADOT Extension + RESPONSE_STREAM lifecycle interaction? In RESPONSE_STREAM mode, the Lambda invocation is "complete" only when the generator is exhausted and the response stream closes — NOT when the handler returns the generator. The ADOT Extension receives the INVOKE completion notification after streaming finishes. The `force_flush()` in the generator `finally` block (FR-055) pushes the final spans to ADOT's OTLP receiver before INVOKE completion. The Extension then has time to export to X-Ray in the post-INVOKE processing window before environment freeze. This lifecycle is compatible because ADOT is designed for Lambda — it waits for the INVOKE response before starting its post-processing.
- **(Round 7)** What is the distinction between the ADOT Python SDK layer and the ADOT collector-only layer? Two layer types exist: (1) `aws-otel-python-amd64-*` includes both the OTel Collector binary AND Python auto-instrumentation wrapper (`/opt/otel-instrument`) — ~80MB unzipped, (2) `aws-otel-collector-amd64-*` includes only the OTel Collector binary — ~35MB unzipped. For sidecar-only mode (FR-046: no `AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER`), the collector-only layer is correct. Using the Python SDK layer wastes ~45MB and includes unused auto-instrumentation code that could be accidentally activated. Source: ADOT Lambda Layer ARN repository — separate per-region ARN mappings for each layer type.
- **(Round 8)** What happens when FR-062/FR-063 specify Lambda Layers for a container-based Lambda? Lambda container images CANNOT use Lambda Layers — the `layers` attribute is only valid for ZIP deployments. Terraform will either error (if using `aws_lambda_function` with `image_uri` and `layers` simultaneously) or silently ignore the layer configuration. The SSE Lambda (`python:3.13-slim` + custom bootstrap), Analysis Lambda (`public.ecr.aws/lambda/python:3.13`), and Dashboard Lambda (`public.ecr.aws/lambda/python:3.13`) are ALL container-based. ADOT deployment for the SSE Lambda requires embedding the collector binary in the Docker image. Source: AWS Lambda Container Image docs — "You cannot add Lambda layers to container images."
- **(Round 8)** What happens when `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME` is not set on the SSE Lambda? The `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` populates `cloud.*` and `faas.*` attributes but does NOT set `service.name`. The OTel SDK defaults `service.name` to `unknown_service`. The ADOT X-Ray exporter uses `service.name` as the node name in the X-Ray service map. All SSE Lambda invocations appear under a single `unknown_service` node — indistinguishable from any other unconfigured Lambda. SC-028 becomes unachievable. Operators cannot identify the SSE Lambda in the service map without searching by trace ID. Source: `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws` — `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` implementation; AWS X-Ray OTLP integration docs.
- **(Round 8)** What happens when `BatchSpanProcessor` uses default configuration (`schedule_delay_millis=5000`) on the SSE Lambda? The background worker thread wakes every 5 seconds to check for pending spans. During a 15-second streaming session producing ~50-200 spans, the worker exports approximately 3 batches (at 5s, 10s, 15s). With `force_flush()` in the generator `finally` block, the remaining spans are drained synchronously. Functionally correct, but the 5-second delay means a mid-stream crash loses up to 5 seconds of spans (vs 1 second with tuned configuration). The 2048-entry queue buffer also wastes ~200KB of memory unnecessarily. For Lambda, smaller/faster is better.
- **(Round 9)** What happens when the ADOT Extension's collector context is canceled before HTTP exports to X-Ray complete? This is a KNOWN issue (GitHub aws-otel-lambda#886, opentelemetry-lambda#224) with measured ~30% span drop rate in worst-case scenarios. The root cause: the collector's internal context is canceled when the Lambda Extension calls Next API, but the X-Ray HTTP exporter may still have in-flight requests. Error pattern: `"context canceled"` during export followed by `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."` The decouple processor (Lambda-specific batch processor in ADOT) mitigates this by decoupling span reception from export — it holds the Extension from calling Next until all queued data is exported. However, under high concurrency or when `span.end()` is the very last operation before function exit, a race exists between the collector's shutdown and the HTTP export completion. The spec's `force_flush()` (FR-055) handles the SDK→Extension hop (fast, localhost). The Extension→X-Ray backend hop is the vulnerable path. The canary (FR-019/FR-036) provides aggregate detection. Per-invocation detection is NOT possible because the span loss occurs in the Extension process, not the SDK. Source: https://github.com/aws-observability/aws-otel-lambda/issues/886
- **(Round 9)** What happens when `TracerProvider` is created with the default `shutdown_on_exit=True`? Python's `atexit` module registers a handler that calls `TracerProvider.shutdown()`. In Lambda, the interpreter does not exit between warm invocations, so `atexit` does not fire between invocations. However, when the execution environment is recycled (idle timeout), the interpreter finalization sequence runs, triggering `atexit` handlers. In Python 3.13+, `ConcurrentMultiSpanProcessor.shutdown()` shuts down the thread pool executor. If the shutdown races with a pending export (e.g., a span was queued just before recycling), a `RuntimeError: cannot schedule new futures after shutdown` is raised (opentelemetry-python#4461). The `shutdown_on_exit=False` parameter prevents this race by skipping the `atexit` registration. Since the Lambda runtime calls `force_flush()` per FR-055, the `atexit` handler is redundant. Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-python/issues/4461
- **(Round 9)** What happens when OTel `BotocoreInstrumentor().instrument()` is called on the SSE Lambda alongside Powertools Tracer (even with `auto_patch=False`)? `BotocoreInstrumentor` patches `botocore.client.BaseClient._make_api_call` with OTel span creation. Powertools Tracer's `@tracer.capture_method` also creates X-Ray subsegments around handler-phase AWS SDK calls. During the handler phase, each AWS SDK call would produce BOTH an OTel span (via BotocoreInstrumentor) AND an X-Ray subsegment (via capture_method). During the streaming phase, only OTel spans are created (correct). The BotocoreInstrumentor does NOT auto-activate in sidecar-only mode — it must be explicitly called. FR-060 prohibits `auto_patch` but does not prohibit `BotocoreInstrumentor`. Without explicit prohibition, a future implementer could import and call it thinking it's the "OTel way" to instrument AWS SDK calls.
- **(Round 9)** What happens when the X-Ray canary queries BatchGetTraces before the trace is indexed? The X-Ray API cannot distinguish "not yet indexed" from "trace does not exist." Both scenarios result in the trace ID appearing in `UnprocessedTraceIds` or being absent from the `Traces` response array. A single query at 30 seconds will produce false negatives under load. The canary must retry with backoff (query at 30s, retry at 60s) to account for eventual consistency. Two consecutive failures across canary intervals remains the alarm threshold. Source: https://aws.amazon.com/xray/faqs/ — "Trace data sent to X-Ray is generally available for retrieval and filtering within 30 seconds"
- **(Round 9)** What happens when CloudWatch `put_metric_data` fails with an IAM error (AccessDeniedException) vs a transient error (ThrottlingException)? The canary (FR-049) currently treats all failures uniformly. IAM/credential errors (AccessDeniedException, NotAuthorized, InvalidClientTokenId) indicate a permanent permission change — the exact failure mode FR-051's separate IAM role is designed to detect — and require immediate out-of-band escalation. Transient errors (ThrottlingException, InternalFailure, ServiceUnavailable) should be retried with exponential backoff before escalating. Without this classification, an IAM revocation is silently retried for multiple canary intervals before escalating, losing critical response time. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/APIReference/API_PutMetricData.html
- **(Round 9)** What happens when the SSE Lambda server ignores the `Last-Event-ID` request header on reconnection? FR-033 specifies client-side `Last-Event-ID` propagation for stream resumption, but if the server does not check this header and resume from the corresponding position, the client receives a fresh stream from the beginning. This causes duplicate events (already-processed events re-sent) and missed events (events emitted between disconnect and reconnect start if server resets). The client must handle idempotently (deduplicate by event ID). Without server-side support, the "stream resumption" guarantee in FR-033 is hollow.
- **(Round 9)** What happens when the frontend needs to read the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` response header for FR-048's `previous_trace_id` capture? Per the CORS specification, browsers can only read response headers listed in `Access-Control-Expose-Headers`. The SSE Lambda Function URL's CORS configuration currently does not include `x-amzn-trace-id` in `ExposeHeaders`. Without it, the browser JavaScript cannot read the response trace ID, making FR-048's reconnection trace correlation impossible. This is a hard prerequisite, not optional.
- **(Round 9)** What happens when Safari processes small SSE frames from a fetch()+ReadableStream connection? Safari may buffer small streaming responses differently than Chrome/Firefox, potentially batching multiple small SSE frames before delivering them to the ReadableStream reader. This causes perceived latency spikes where events arrive in bursts rather than individually. Workaround: server sends padding bytes or explicit flush signals. Source: sveltejs/kit#10315
- **(Round 9)** What is the canonical way to distinguish graceful server close from network error in a fetch()+ReadableStream SSE connection? `ReadableStreamDefaultReader.read()` returns `{done: true}` on graceful close and throws `TypeError` on network error. The `reader.closed` Promise fulfills on graceful close and rejects on error. FR-033's reconnection logic should use `retry:` value (from SSE protocol) or short fixed delay for graceful close (expected Lambda timeout), and exponential backoff with jitter for network errors. Uniform backoff on all close types unnecessarily delays reconnection after expected server-initiated closes. Source: WHATWG Streams Standard — ReadableStreamDefaultReader.closed
- **(Round 9)** What happens if AWS Account-level Transaction Search is enabled? If the account migrates to CloudWatch-native tracing, traces stored in `/aws/spans` are NOT queryable via X-Ray's `BatchGetTraces` API — only traces stored via `PutTraceSegments` to the legacy X-Ray segment store are retrievable. The canary's trace verification (FR-019) uses `BatchGetTraces`. An account-level settings change could break the canary without any code change. The canary should verify that its test traces are retrievable via the API it uses, not assume the storage backend. Source: https://repost.aws/questions/QUUl7bopxdQii5vVCNZ3FtPg
- **(Round 10)** What happens when the SSE Lambda continues streaming after the client disconnects? AWS docs confirm: "Streamed responses are not interrupted or stopped when the invoking client connection is broken. Customers are billed for the full function duration." The SSE Lambda continues DynamoDB polling, CloudWatch metric emission, and OTel span creation after client disconnects. `force_flush()` runs in the `finally` block for a phantom stream. Python custom runtimes have NO standard mechanism to detect client disconnect (unlike Node.js `StreamifyResponse` which provides `metadata.onAbort`). The only signal is `BrokenPipeError` raised when the generator attempts to write to the closed response stream. Spans created after disconnect annotate "successful" streaming with no client receiving the data. The canary should account for elevated "successful but undelivered" traces in its health assessment. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/configuration-response-streaming.html
- **(Round 10)** What happens when `BatchSpanProcessor` queue fills during high-throughput SSE streaming? `BatchSpanProcessor.emit()` uses `queue.put_nowait()` which raises `queue.Full` exception, silently caught and logged as a WARNING. Spans are DROPPED, not queued or retried. At FR-073's original `max_queue_size=512`, a 15-second streaming Lambda producing ~15 DynamoDB polls/second with ~3 spans per poll generates ~675 spans per invocation. This EXCEEDS the 512 queue capacity. If `force_flush()` (which drains the queue synchronously) does not keep pace with span production between batch intervals, ~163 spans are silently lost. The drop is only visible as a WARNING log line — no metric, no exception, no span attribute. Source: OTel Python SDK source code — `BatchSpanProcessor.on_end()` method.
- **(Round 10)** What happens when custom ADOT collector config omits the decouple processor? The ADOT Lambda Layer's default configuration automatically includes the decouple processor when the batch processor is used. However, this auto-configuration ONLY applies to Lambda Layer deployments — NOT to container-based deployments with custom collector YAML (FR-064/FR-069). If the custom collector config defines a pipeline without explicitly listing `decouple` in the processors chain, span drops revert to the known ~30% rate (aws-otel-lambda#886) because the collector context is canceled before HTTP exports complete. Cross-reference: FR-075 (decouple processor requirement), FR-064 (container-based deployment), FR-069 (custom config). Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda/blob/main/collector/processor/decoupleprocessor/README.md
- **(Round 10)** What happens when Active Tracing is accidentally disabled on a Lambda function? `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator` reads `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` environment variable, which is ALWAYS set by the Lambda runtime regardless of Active Tracing status. With Active Tracing disabled, the trace ID still populates but with `Sampled=0`. The propagator extracts this context (open issue opentelemetry-lambda#1782 — the propagator does not distinguish between "legitimately unsampled" and "tracing disabled"). The `parentbased_always_on` sampler honors the parent's `Sampled=0` flag and suppresses ALL span creation. Result: zero spans emitted, zero errors logged, complete silent tracing failure. Cross-reference: FR-052 (Active Tracing requirement). Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda/issues/1782
- **(Round 10)** What happens when X-Ray subsegment count exceeds 100 per segment (Powertools Tracer)? The X-Ray SDK has a default subsegment streaming threshold of 100. When exceeded, completed subsegments are automatically sent to the X-Ray daemon out of band. For non-streaming Lambdas with many boto3 calls, this is benign. For the SSE Lambda handler phase (before streaming begins), the count should be well under 100. However, if `auto_patch=True` were accidentally re-enabled (violating FR-060), streaming-phase boto3 calls would create X-Ray subsegments via the X-Ray daemon (unreliable after handler returns), counting against the 100-subsegment threshold and triggering automatic streaming of partially-complete subsegments. This reinforces the criticality of FR-060 (`auto_patch=False`). Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/xray/latest/devguide/xray-troubleshooting.html
- **(Round 10)** What happens when X-Ray centralized sampling rules are temporarily unavailable? The OTel X-Ray remote sampler falls back to a `TraceIDRatioBased` sampler with reservoir borrowing (1 trace per second). In dev/preprod environments where 100% sampling is required (FR-034/FR-035), this fallback silently drops to 1 request/second sampling during X-Ray service degradation. The fallback is a safety mechanism (not a bug), but the drop from 100% to ~0.01% (at 10K req/s) is dramatic and invisible without explicit monitoring. No metric or alarm fires for the sampling mode change. Source: https://aws-otel.github.io/docs/getting-started/remote-sampling/
- **(Round 11)** What happens when the SSE Lambda hits its timeout limit during streaming? Lambda does NOT send SIGTERM to the custom runtime's bootstrap process. The process is killed directly. Python's `finally` blocks do NOT execute when the process is SIGKILL'd. `GeneratorExit` is NOT raised. FR-055's `force_flush()` does NOT run. Un-flushed `BatchSpanProcessor` spans (up to 1000ms worth per FR-073's batch interval) are permanently lost. The ADOT Extension receives a Shutdown event with `shutdownReason: "TIMEOUT"` and has a 2000ms grace period to export already-received spans. Spans that never left the SDK (still in BSP queue) cannot be recovered. Mitigation: proactive flush when remaining time < threshold (see FR-093). Source: AWS Lambda Runtime Environment Lifecycle — Extensions receive Shutdown with reason TIMEOUT; runtime process is killed.
- **(Round 11)** What happens when the SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap does NOT set `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` from the `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` response header between warm invocations? The Lambda service sets `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` in the process environment at cold start (INIT phase). On warm invocations, the Lambda Runtime API returns an updated `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` header with the new invocation's trace context, but the process environment variable is NOT automatically updated by the Lambda service. The custom bootstrap MUST explicitly set `os.environ['_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID']` from this header before calling the handler. Without this, `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator.extract()` reads stale context from the FIRST invocation on EVERY subsequent warm invocation. The X-Ray SDK's `LambdaContext._refresh_context()` reads the same env var. This is a SILENT failure — no error, no warning, just wrong trace IDs on every warm invocation span. Source: AWS Lambda Custom Runtime Contract — bootstrap must set `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` from `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` header.
- **(Round 11)** What happens when a malicious client sends `Sampled=1` in `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` to a Lambda Function URL? The Lambda service honors the incoming sampling decision. Unlike API Gateway (which makes its own sampling decision when tracing is enabled), Function URLs have no intermediary tracing layer. The client forces 100% sampling on the SSE Lambda. At 1000 concurrent connections with 15-second sessions (4 invocations/minute/connection), this produces ~172M traces/month at ~$860/month. Mitigation for API Gateway paths: API Gateway's own tracing integration makes independent decisions. Mitigation for Function URL paths: application-level sampling logic, WAF rate limiting, or placing API Gateway in front. CloudFront would strip the header (it treats `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` as restricted) but is not in the current architecture.
- **(Round 11)** What happens when the ADOT Extension's custom collector config file exists at `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml` but `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` is not set? The Extension ignores the file and uses its compiled-in embedded default configuration. The embedded default includes: OTLP HTTP receiver on 4318, AWS X-Ray exporter, decouple processor. However, it also includes unnecessary components (gRPC receiver on 4317, potentially metrics pipeline) that consume ~15MB of extra memory. The custom config (with stripped-down components per FR-064) is effectively dead code. The file's presence in the container image provides no benefit without the env var. Source: ADOT Lambda Extension — config file path is only read from `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` env var.
- **(Round 11)** What happens when `TextDecoder` processes a ReadableStream chunk that ends in the middle of a multi-byte UTF-8 character? Without `TextDecoder({stream: true})`, the decoder treats each chunk independently. An incomplete byte sequence at the chunk boundary (e.g., the first 2 bytes of a 3-byte UTF-8 character) is replaced with U+FFFD (replacement character). On the next chunk, the remaining byte(s) are also invalid (starting mid-sequence) and produce another U+FFFD. The original character is permanently lost, replaced by 2 replacement characters. For SSE event data containing sentiment analysis results with non-ASCII characters (article titles, international content), this silently corrupts the data. `TextDecoder({stream: true})` retains incomplete sequences across decode calls, correctly reconstructing multi-byte characters split across chunks. Source: WHATWG Encoding Standard — TextDecoder `stream` option.
- **(Round 12)** What happens when the SSE Lambda's generator terminates after the proactive flush (FR-093/FR-100) but before the Lambda timeout? The Lambda handler returns normally (not a timeout), so the ADOT Extension receives a NORMAL Shutdown event with `shutdownReason: "spindown"` (not `"timeout"`). The Extension gets the standard 2000ms grace period to flush buffered spans to X-Ray. This is strictly MORE reliable than waiting for timeout, because normal Shutdown has no SIGKILL risk for the Extension process. FR-100's graceful termination converts what would be a crash into a clean exit, improving span export reliability from "best-effort Extension Shutdown after runtime SIGKILL" to "guaranteed Extension Shutdown after normal completion."
- **(Round 12)** What happens when OTel core packages are at different versions in the Docker image? The `opentelemetry-sdk` package hard-pins `opentelemetry-api==<exact-version>`. `pip install` fails with `ResolutionImpossible` error, preventing the Docker build from succeeding. This means version mismatch is a build-time failure, not a runtime failure — but without explicit `==` pins in `requirements.txt`, different `pip install` runs on different dates could resolve to different lockstep versions, making builds non-reproducible. FR-101 makes this constraint explicit.
- **(Round 12)** What happens when the bootstrap provides the deadline but the handler doesn't use it? FR-093 becomes unimplementable. The generator streams until Lambda timeout, the runtime is SIGKILL'd, the `finally` block doesn't run, and spans from the final BSP batch interval (~1000ms per FR-073) are permanently lost. FR-103 is a hard prerequisite for FR-093.
- **(Round 12)** What happens when Lambda memory is increased to 1024MB but ADOT + application code consumes more than expected? The 85% memory alarm (FR-104) fires at ~870MB, giving operators advance warning before OOM. Lambda OOM-terminates the execution environment at 1024MB. The Lambda `REPORT` log line includes `Max Memory Used` for post-incident analysis. Without FR-104, the first indication of memory pressure is an OOM kill with no advance warning.
- **(Round 12)** What happens when the ADOT Extension log message format changes in a future version? FR-105's substring match pattern (`"Exporting failed" "Dropping data"`) is resilient to minor format changes (field reordering, additional fields) but would miss a completely rewritten message. Version pinning (FR-070 digest pin) prevents silent ADOT upgrades. When upgrading ADOT, the metric filter pattern must be verified against the new version's log output. The log messages originate from upstream OTel Collector `exporterhelper` package and have been stable since v0.67 (2022). Source: `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-collector` — `exporter/exporterhelper/internal/retry_sender.go`.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when remediation tasks are deployed out of phase order — specifically, when the canary (Task 11) is deployed before any instrumentation task (Tasks 2-5)? The canary submits its OWN test traces and queries for them. If no application instrumentation is deployed, the canary's self-generated test traces are found successfully, so it reports healthy. But application traces don't exist — the canary validates itself, not the system. This is a false-green scenario where the canary says "tracing works" but zero real application traces exist. FR-107's Phase 6 ordering prevents this by requiring instrumentation deployment before canary deployment.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` is accidentally set to `true` in production? All OTel tracing silently stops. The `TracerProvider` returns no-op tracers — zero spans created, zero export errors, zero log entries from the OTel SDK. The ADOT Extension process continues running (consuming ~50MB memory) but receives no spans on its OTLP receiver. The canary (FR-019) detects absence of application traces within 2 canary intervals (10 minutes per FR-048 at 5-minute interval). The Lambda continues functioning normally — `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` affects ONLY observability, not application logic. This is by design: the kill switch trades observability for stability during incidents where tracing is suspected of causing problems. Rollback: set `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=false` via Terraform and apply.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when a rollback from ADOT is needed but no pre-ADOT container image exists in ECR? The team must modify the Dockerfile to remove ADOT components, rebuild the container image, push to ECR, update Terraform `image_uri`, and apply. This takes 15-30 minutes during an active incident, requiring CI/CD pipeline access and Docker build infrastructure availability. FR-110's pre-ADOT baseline image reduces rollback to a single Terraform variable change (~2 minutes), eliminating CI/CD dependency during incidents.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when X-Ray Groups are created without `insights_enabled = true`? The Groups function correctly as query-time filters in the X-Ray console — operators can search and view filtered trace lists. However, the Groups do NOT emit CloudWatch metrics. SC-013's requirement ("X-Ray Group with error/fault filter generates CloudWatch metrics") fails silently — no error, no warning, no indication that metrics are not being emitted. Alarms configured against Group-derived CloudWatch metrics never fire because the underlying metrics never exist. The `insights_enabled` attribute defaults to `false` in both the AWS API and Terraform, making this an opt-in configuration that is easy to miss.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when the EventBridge rule for the canary fires before `aws_lambda_permission` is created during initial `terraform apply`? EventBridge attempts to invoke the Lambda and receives `AccessDeniedException`. EventBridge retries with exponential backoff (built-in retry policy). The `aws_lambda_permission` resource is typically created within seconds by Terraform, so the first retry succeeds. However, the initial failure creates noise: an error entry in EventBridge's dead-letter queue (if configured) or a silently lost invocation (if no DLQ). More critically, operators monitoring the initial deployment may see a "canary failed" alert that self-resolves, creating false urgency. FR-112's `depends_on` eliminates this entirely.
- **(Round 13)** What happens when trace completeness drops below 95% but individual traces are not marked IsPartial? This indicates systemic trace loss where entire traces — not just segments within a trace — are being dropped. Possible causes: (a) ADOT Extension process crash during streaming (all spans from that invocation are lost), (b) X-Ray `PutTraceSegments` throttling at the 2,600 segments/sec region limit, (c) BSP queue overflow (mitigated by FR-086's 1500 queue size), (d) Extension→X-Ray backend race (aws-otel-lambda#886 at ~30% worst-case). The per-trace IsPartial check (FR-087) catches incomplete traces but NOT missing traces (a trace that never arrives has no IsPartial flag to check). FR-113's completeness ratio metric catches both incomplete and missing traces by comparing submission count to retrieval count.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when the ADOT Extension process crashes during `force_flush()`? The OTel OTLP HTTP exporter's `DEFAULT_TIMEOUT` is 10 seconds with up to 6 retries per HTTP POST. With ceil(1500/64)=24 batches at worst-case, each blocking for up to 60s on timeout, total potential block is ~24 minutes. Since `force_flush()` timeout parameter is NOT enforced (OTel issue #4568), the call blocks indefinitely. FR-093's 3000ms pre-deadline flush becomes a multi-minute block. The Lambda is SIGKILL'd while `force_flush()` is still processing. Mitigation: `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT=2` caps per-request timeout, limiting worst-case to ~15 seconds. Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor._export()` loop; OTLP HTTP exporter timeout; issue #4568.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when the BSP's internal export fails silently during `force_flush()`? Spans are popped from the deque BEFORE being passed to `self._exporter.export(batch)`. If export raises an exception, it is caught by `except Exception` and the loop continues. Failed batch spans are PERMANENTLY destroyed — already removed from queue. `force_flush()` returns `True` regardless, indicating "queue drained" not "export succeeded." Against localhost ADOT, export failure is extremely unlikely, but during Extension crash/hang recovery, this behavior means proactive flush can drain the queue while zero spans reach ADOT. Source: OTel Python SDK `_shared_internal/__init__.py` lines 180-195.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when an OTel span on the SSE Lambda has more than 50 attributes that map to X-Ray annotations? X-Ray silently drops annotations beyond the 50-per-segment limit with `log.warning()`. With FR-006 (~6 annotations), FR-007 (~5), FR-008 (~3), FR-009 (~4), plus OTel semantic conventions (~5-10), total is ~23-28 per span — within the 50 limit. However, ad-hoc debugging annotations during incident investigation could exceed 50, and the silent drop creates a debugging trap. Source: AWS X-Ray API — PutTraceSegments annotation limit; SDK warning behavior.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when the browser's CORS preflight cache expires for X-Amzn-Trace-Id? After `Access-Control-Max-Age` expiry (Chrome: 7200s, Firefox: 86400s, Safari: 600s), the next fetch() with X-Amzn-Trace-Id triggers a preflight OPTIONS request (50-200ms). For SSE connections (15s+), negligible. For Dashboard Lambda API calls, first request after expiry pays the cost. Safari's 10-minute max means Safari users experience frequent preflights. Source: MDN Access-Control-Max-Age; Fetch Living Standard.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when a ReadableStream SSE connection terminates with `done: true` but the server did NOT send a sentinel `event: done` first? The client cannot distinguish server-intentional close from clean network drop (TCP FIN). Both produce `{ done: true, value: undefined }`. Without sentinel: treating all `done: true` as graceful masks network issues; treating as error adds unnecessary backoff to graceful closes. Sentinel resolves ambiguity: presence of `event: done` in buffer before `done: true` = graceful; absence = abnormal. Source: WHATWG Fetch Standard; Streams Standard §4.2.3.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when `treat_missing_data = "notBreaching"` is set on the canary health alarm and the canary Lambda dies? The canary stops emitting health metrics. `notBreaching` treats missing data as within threshold — alarm resolves to OK. The "watcher of the watcher" is dead and the alarm says "healthy." `treat_missing_data = "breaching"` is the ONLY correct setting for canary alarms: absence of heartbeat IS the failure. Source: AWS CloudWatch Developer Guide — treat_missing_data.
- **(Round 14)** What happens when ADOT collector config is syntactically valid YAML but references an unsupported component? The collector fails at config validation phase with `Error: failed to get config: unknown receiver type`. ADOT Extension logs error and exits. Lambda invocation proceeds without telemetry (Extension is sidecar — failure doesn't crash Lambda). All subsequent invocations on this execution environment also lack telemetry. Only canary detects trace absence (~10 minutes). CI validation with `validate` subcommand catches this before deployment. Source: OTel Collector config loading; ADOT Extension failure behavior.
- **(Round 14)** What happens during dual-emit when X-Ray SDK and OTel SDK produce traces for the same request? X-Ray SDK produces native segment documents with `subsegment` nesting. ADOT-converted OTel spans produce flat segments with `parent_id` references. X-Ray service map correctly links both (shared trace ID). Console visualization differs (nesting depth varies). FR-109 verification gates must use SEMANTIC comparison (same operations, annotations, error flags) not structural comparison (byte-identical documents). Source: X-Ray segment document format; ADOT X-Ray exporter output.
- **Cascading false-green during CloudWatch regional degradation** (Round 15): put_metric_data fails → custom metrics stop → alarms with treat_missing_data=notBreaching resolve to OK → dashboard shows all-green while system is failing. Mitigation: canary heartbeat with treat_missing_data=breaching + Logs metric filter backup.
- **Canary heartbeat through different code path** (Round 15): If canary uses a separate CloudWatch client or separate put_metric_data call, it proves CloudWatch API reachability but NOT that the application's metric emission pipeline is healthy. Canary MUST piggyback on same call.
- **Silent failure metric emission itself failing** (Round 15): Adding put_metric_data to catch blocks creates a second failure point — the metric emission for the silent failure can itself fail silently. Defense: structured log fallback with metric_fallback=true marker for Logs metric filter.
- **Percentage-based error alarm at low traffic** (Round 15): If Lambda runs 2 invocations in 5 minutes and 1 fails, that's 50% error rate — alarm fires. At 1000 invocations, 5 errors = 0.5% — alarm does not fire. Need minimum invocation count guard: IF(invocations > 10, error_rate, 0).
- **SendGrid python_http_client call chain** (Round 15): sendgrid → python_http_client.Client._make_request() → urllib.request.urlopen() → http.client.HTTPSConnection. X-Ray patch_all() patches httplib which IS http.client — so it DOES capture SendGrid calls, but only as generic "http.client" subsegments without SendGrid-specific metadata.
- **Composite alarm INSUFFICIENT_DATA suppression** (Round 15): If underlying alarms use treat_missing_data=notBreaching, they never enter INSUFFICIENT_DATA — composite alarm for "all metrics missing" never fires. Underlying alarms MUST use treat_missing_data=missing.
- **Work order implementer scope blindness** (Round 15): Developer implementing Task 5 from fix-sse-subsegments.md sees 16 FRs. HL doc assigns 52 FRs (including 2 CRITICAL: FR-092 warm-invocation trace ID, FR-093 deadline-aware flush). 36 FRs silently omitted, including corrections that invalidate earlier FRs' assumptions.
- **Alarm widget showing stale count** (Round 15): Dashboard alarm widget configured with static alarm list — new alarms added by Terraform not automatically included. Widget must use alarm name prefix pattern, not explicit ARN list.
- **CloudWatch RUM initialization race** (Round 16): If application code calls `fetch()` before RUM's web client completes initialization (INIT phase), the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header is NOT injected. The SSE connection is typically established early in the page lifecycle. Mitigation: SSE connection establishment MUST wait for RUM readiness (e.g., `window.cwr_ready` or a RUM initialization callback) before calling `fetch()`.
- **SNS rawMessageDelivery breaks trace propagation** (Round 16): If any subscription on the Ingestion→Analysis SNS topic has `rawMessageDelivery: true`, the `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute is stripped and cross-Lambda trace propagation silently breaks. The SNS subscription appears healthy — messages deliver — but traces are disconnected. FR-137's verification gate catches this.
- **Cross-region SNS IAM specificity** (Round 16): The canary's execution role for FR-136 needs `sns:Publish` for the cross-region topic ARN. A wildcard region in the policy (`arn:aws:sns:*:*:canary-alert`) creates unnecessarily broad permissions. The policy MUST pin to the specific backup region ARN.
- **Hung vs. crashed ADOT Extension** (Round 16): TCP connect to a crashed Extension fails in <100ms (ECONNREFUSED). TCP connect to a hung Extension succeeds but reads block until per-request timeout (FR-114, 2s). FR-139's thread wrapper handles both: crashed Extension completes fast (~2s for all 22 batch connect failures); hung Extension triggers the 2,500ms hard timeout. Without FR-139, only the crashed case is bounded.
- **ADOT Extension OOM** (Round 16): If the Extension process is OOM-killed by the Lambda sandbox (Extension shares Lambda's memory allocation per FR-102), the OTLP exporter sees ECONNREFUSED (not hung). force_flush() fails fast per SC-064. But the OOM signal indicates insufficient memory headroom — FR-104's memory alarm at 85% should fire BEFORE Extension OOM. If it doesn't, the 1024MB allocation (FR-102) needs re-evaluation.
- **API Gateway IntegrationLatency includes cold start** (Round 16): During deployments (new container image rollout), Lambda cold starts spike temporarily. FR-138's `IntegrationLatency` P99 alarm must tolerate deployment-time spikes: 2 evaluation periods × 5 minutes = 10-minute window prevents single-period false alarms during rolling deployment.
- **X-Ray annotation requirement for session chain queries** (Round 16): FR-141's X-Ray filter `annotation.session_id = "{value}"` requires `session_id` to be an X-Ray ANNOTATION (indexed), not metadata (non-indexed). FR-008 specifies it as an annotation, so this works. But if future FR amendments move it to metadata for space savings (FR-120 annotation budget), session queries break.
- **Audit trail DLQ for compliance** (Round 16, OUT OF SCOPE): FR-124 adds alerting for audit trail persistence failures, but alerting alone doesn't solve the compliance gap — failed audit events are permanently lost. A DLQ or retry mechanism for audit writes is outside X-Ray tracing scope but flagged as a dependent feature requirement. The X-Ray trace subsegment (SC-004 item 3) provides forensic evidence of the failure but not data recovery.
- **OTel SpanKind service map distortion** (Round 17): Manual OTel spans on SSE Lambda must use correct SpanKind — `SpanKind.CLIENT` for outbound calls (DynamoDB, CloudWatch), `SpanKind.INTERNAL` for internal processing (poll cycle, event formatting). ADOT X-Ray exporter maps `SpanKind.CLIENT` to remote subsegment (appears as separate node in service map), `SpanKind.INTERNAL` to local subsegment (appears within the Lambda node). Using `SpanKind.CLIENT` for internal processing creates phantom nodes in the X-Ray service map. Using `SpanKind.INTERNAL` for DynamoDB calls hides them from the service map's dependency view, violating SC-028. Source: ADOT X-Ray Exporter `segment.go` — `MakeSegment()` SpanKind routing.
- **Canary dual-mode operation** (Round 17): The canary Lambda has a unique architectural constraint: it must be INSTRUMENTED (per FR-029/FR-146) for operator visibility when X-Ray is healthy, AND RESILIENT (per FR-145) when X-Ray is down. No other Lambda in the system has this dual requirement. If FR-145's error handling catches too broadly, the canary might mask legitimate bugs in its own code. If too narrowly, it might crash on unexpected X-Ray failure modes. The error handling MUST be scoped to initialization only (TracerProvider setup, ADOT Extension connection) — runtime exceptions in canary business logic (API calls, metric emission) should propagate normally per FR-018.
- **record_exception() without set_status(ERROR) invisibility** (Round 17): The OTel `span.record_exception(exception)` API adds an exception event to the span with type, message, and stacktrace attributes. However, the ADOT X-Ray exporter's `makeCause()` function — which converts exception events to X-Ray's `cause` field — is GATED on `StatusCode.ERROR`. Calling `record_exception()` without `set_status(StatusCode.ERROR)` means the exception event EXISTS on the OTel span but is NEVER translated to the X-Ray segment document. The segment has `fault: false`, `cause: null`. The exception is permanently invisible in X-Ray, including to Group filters, console search, and CloudWatch metrics derived from Groups. This is the most insidious failure mode because the developer believes they handled the error (they recorded it) but X-Ray sees a healthy span. Source: ADOT X-Ray Exporter `cause.go`.
- **RUM initialization race on cold page load** (Round 18): CloudWatch RUM's FetchPlugin patches `window.fetch` synchronously once the AwsRum client constructor completes, but the constructor itself may be loaded asynchronously via a CDN snippet (`<script>` with `async` or `defer`). On a cold page load, application JavaScript can call `fetch()` before the AwsRum constructor fires, resulting in an unpatched `window.fetch` that sends NO `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. The SSE connection established in this window has no frontend-to-backend trace correlation. This is distinct from FR-135's deployment gate (which tests in a controlled Playwright environment where page load order is deterministic) — production users with cold caches experience non-deterministic script loading order. Mitigation: application code MUST NOT call fetch() until RUM is confirmed initialized (FR-148).
- **Post-flush span creation window** (Round 18): Between the proactive flush (FR-093 at 3000ms remaining, FR-139 at 2500ms hard timeout) and the generator's final `event: deadline` yield + return (FR-100), there is a window where new spans MAY be created (e.g., exception handling spans, cleanup operation spans). These spans are enqueued in the BSP AFTER the flush has drained the queue. No second flush occurs. The BSP's schedule_delay_millis=1000ms (FR-073) means these post-flush spans wait for the next scheduled export — but the Lambda may be killed (SIGKILL) or frozen before that export fires. These spans are silently lost. The window is small (~100ms for generator cleanup) but during error scenarios (exception handling creates diagnostic spans) it can be meaningful.
- **Canary TracerProvider state on warm invocation after cold-start failure** (Round 18): If TracerProvider initialization fails at module level during a cold start (e.g., ADOT Extension not running), the canary continues per FR-145 but module-level code does NOT re-execute on subsequent warm invocations. The TracerProvider remains in its failed/uninitialized state for ALL warm invocations until the execution environment is recycled. This means a transient ADOT Extension hiccup during cold start permanently disables canary tracing for the lifetime of that execution environment — potentially hours. The canary's alerting functions continue (FR-145) but its own trace visibility (FR-146) is lost without any re-initialization attempt.
- **FR-093 timing cascade margin analysis** (Round 18): FR-093 triggers proactive flush at 3000ms remaining. FR-139 wraps flush in a 2500ms hard timeout. If flush completes at 2500ms (worst case), 500ms remains for generator cleanup (yield `event: deadline`, return). Generator cleanup is lightweight (~10ms: one SSE event format + yield). The 500ms margin is sufficient but depends on FR-139's timeout being strictly enforced. If the thread-based timeout has jitter (thread scheduling latency under high CPU contention), the margin shrinks. At extreme contention (100ms thread scheduling delay), effective margin is 400ms — still sufficient for generator cleanup but worth documenting as a boundary condition.
- **BSP deadlock + FR-139 thread wrapper interaction** (Round 20): When BSP deadlocks (opentelemetry-python#3886), `force_flush()` hangs on the BSP's internal condition variable lock. FR-139's thread wrapper terminates the flush call after 2500ms — identical behavior to Extension hang. But the SPAN FATE differs: in Extension hang, spans were dequeued from BSP and held by the exporter (lost in exporter memory). In BSP deadlock, spans remain in the BSP deque but the lock is never released — they cannot be exported, retried, or even counted. The diagnostic log (FR-156) helps operators differentiate, but the practical outcome (span loss) is the same. A BSP deadlock also blocks all subsequent `on_end()` calls (new spans cannot be enqueued), meaning the deadlock's impact extends beyond the current flush to all future spans until the Lambda execution environment is recycled.
- **ADOT cold start exceeds customer experience threshold** (Round 20): SSE Lambda with embedded ADOT Extension at 1024MB may have cold starts exceeding 2000ms. For the SSE endpoint, cold start directly adds to the time before the first SSE event is delivered to the user. If cold start is 2500ms and first DynamoDB poll takes 200ms, the user waits 2700ms for the first stock price update — potentially exceeding acceptable UX thresholds. Mitigation options include provisioned concurrency (cost — ~$15/month per provisioned instance), larger memory (diminishing returns above 1769MB which allocates a full vCPU per AWS Lambda pricing), or ADOT version optimization. FR-158 mandates measurement to replace this assumption with data.
- **ADOT Extension invoke phase end during streaming** (Round 20): AWS Lambda Extensions API defines three lifecycle phases: INIT, INVOKE, SHUTDOWN. For buffered responses, the INVOKE phase ends when the runtime sends the response. For streaming responses, the "response" is continuous — the initial HTTP 200 headers are sent immediately, then the body streams over 15+ seconds. If the Extension's invoke phase ends when the initial response headers are sent (before streaming begins), the Extension may enter a pre-Shutdown state where it prioritizes flushing existing data over accepting new spans. This would manifest as intermittent span loss concentrated in the LATER seconds of streaming — observable in X-Ray as traces with early spans present but late spans missing. FR-160's verification gate detects this pattern by checking span retention across the full streaming duration.
- **Function URL burst traffic X-Ray cost spike** (Round 20): A traffic burst creating 10 million Function URL invocations in a single day at 100% sampling (parentbased_always_on with no parent context) costs $50 in X-Ray traces — exceeding FR-038's monthly $50 cost guard in a single day. At 100 million invocations (possible during a viral event or DDoS), the cost is $500/day. FR-161's daily anomaly alarm detects this, but the alarm evaluates at 5-minute intervals with a 6-hour rolling window — up to 6 hours of uncapped cost accumulation before the alarm fires. The X-Ray centralized sampling rule change (via console) takes effect within 5 minutes. The gap between cost accumulation start and alarm fire is the residual cost risk.
- **X-Ray trace archival at scale rate limits** (Round 20): The `BatchGetTraces` API has a limit of 5 traces per request with a rate limit of 5 requests/sec. For an incident affecting 100,000 traces, archival takes: 100,000 ÷ 5 ÷ 5 = 4,000 seconds (≈67 minutes). For 1 million traces, archival takes ~11 hours and may exceed the remaining 30-day retention window if the incident is discovered late. Operators must estimate trace volume via `GetTraceSummaries` count BEFORE starting archival and prioritize the most critical time windows.
- **ADOT Extension unauthenticated OTLP endpoint** (Round 20): The ADOT Extension accepts OTLP trace data on localhost:4318 without authentication (confirmed by ADOT documentation). Lambda's execution environment provides network isolation at the sandbox level — only code within the same Lambda invocation can reach the endpoint. However, a compromised third-party dependency (e.g., supply chain attack on a pip package) running within the Lambda could inject arbitrary trace data into X-Ray, creating misleading service map topology, false error annotations, or even PII violations (bypassing FR-155). The practical risk is LOW (requires compromised dependency with network access) but should be considered in the threat model.
- **Silent IAM permission degradation for centralized sampling** (Round 20): If `xray:GetSamplingRules` permission is removed from the Lambda execution role (e.g., during an IAM policy update), the ADOT Extension's awsproxy fails silently and the OTel sampler degrades from centralized sampling to `TraceIDRatioBased` at 1 trace/sec. This produces dramatically fewer traces in X-Ray but NO error in Lambda logs, NO CloudWatch alarm, and NO canary detection (the canary's own test traces still succeed because the canary uses Powertools Tracer, not OTel SDK). The degradation is invisible until an operator notices reduced trace volume. FR-159 prevents this by enumerating all required actions, but IAM drift after initial deployment remains a risk.
- **(Round 22)** Sampling rate change during active invocation — sampling decision is made at span creation, not at export. Spans created before rate change keep their original sampling decision. No mid-invocation effect.
- **(Round 22)** Kill switch activated during active SSE streaming session — `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` only takes effect on next cold start (env var read at SDK initialization). In-flight sessions continue with active tracing until sandbox recycles.
- **(Round 22)** PII in auto-captured exception stack traces — OTel automatically records exception attributes (`exception.message`, `exception.stacktrace`) which may contain user data embedded in error messages. FR-184's allow-list MUST include exception attribute handling.
- **(Round 22)** Canary annotation not set due to instrumentation error — canary traces without `synthetic=true` pollute production X-Ray Group. FR-185's implementation MUST set annotation in a fail-safe wrapper.
- **(Round 22)** 51st annotation attempted on a trace — OTel SDK's `BoundedAttributes` silently drops attributes beyond the limit (default 128 for span attributes, but X-Ray's 50-annotation limit is enforced at the X-Ray service, not SDK). X-Ray silently ignores excess annotations — no error response.
- **(Round 22)** Deployment version skew persists through sandbox recycling — old sandboxes retain old `DEPLOYMENT_VERSION` until recycled (~5-15 min idle). Skew detection must tolerate a window during rolling updates.
- **(Round 22)** `update-function-configuration` called with empty Variables map — deletes ALL environment variables including `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`, `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`, etc. Lambda becomes non-functional. FR-181's capture-first procedure prevents this.
- **(Round 22)** GetTraceSummaries `Sampling=true` during archival — returns statistical subset, not all traces. FR-174's archival procedure loses traces. Must use `Sampling=false`.
- **(Round 23)** `set_attribute()` call in third-party library code (e.g., `BotocoreInstrumentor`, `RequestsInstrumentor`) — these instrumentors call `span.set_attribute()` internally, bypassing FR-191's CI static analysis gate (which only scans project source files). Attributes injected by auto-instrumentors (e.g., `http.request.method`, `db.system`, `db.statement`) are NOT covered by the project allow-list. Defense: FR-191's runtime audit SpanProcessor catches ALL attribute violations regardless of source. The CI gate is defense-in-depth for project code only.
- **(Round 23)** Exception attributes containing PII — `span.record_exception(exception)` captures `exception.message` which may contain user data embedded in error messages (e.g., `"User john@example.com not found"`). FR-191's allow-list covers standard attribute keys but exception message CONTENT is not filterable by key-based allow-listing. Defense: FR-184's attribute allow-list blocks non-listed keys, but `exception.message` IS a listed key (required for X-Ray cause rendering). PII in exception messages requires code-level discipline (never interpolate user data into exception strings) plus FR-155's regex scanning as a catch-all.
- **(Round 23)** SpanProcessor ordering violated by future processor additions — if a new SpanProcessor is registered between the allow-list processor and BSP (e.g., a sampling processor, a debugging processor), it sees unfiltered attributes on `on_start()` if it reads attributes set by preceding processors. Defense: FR-192 documents the ordering contract with code comments. Any new processor addition requires reviewing its position in the chain.
- **(Round 23)** SDK upgrade changes `BoundedAttributes` eviction policy — OTel SDK currently uses FIFO eviction (oldest attribute dropped). A future SDK version could change to LRU, random, or priority-based eviction. If the eviction policy changes, FR-193's annotation priority assumptions become invalid. Defense: FR-194's SDK upgrade runbook includes `BoundedAttributes` eviction policy verification as gate (2).
- **(Round 23)** Powertools `auto_patch` behavior regression — a Powertools version upgrade could change `auto_patch=False` behavior (e.g., patching libraries at import time regardless of the flag). This would re-enable X-Ray SDK patching on the SSE Lambda, violating FR-060. Defense: FR-195's version pinning prevents silent upgrades. Integration test verifies zero X-Ray SDK subsegments during streaming phase.
- ~~**(Round 23)** ADOT Extension recovered panic in exporter goroutine — Extension process stays alive (passes Runtime API health checks) but the OTLP-to-X-Ray exporter goroutine is dead. Spans accepted on :4318 are buffered but never exported. Over time, the buffer fills and spans are silently dropped. The canary detects this as "traces submitted but not retrievable" — same symptom as ADOT drop race (FR-074) but with 100% loss rate instead of ~30%. Defense: FR-196 extends canary verification to detect sustained 100% trace loss as distinct from intermittent drop race.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 24**: OTel Collector does NOT use `recover()` in pipeline goroutines — panics crash the entire Extension process. The "recovered panic" scenario is architecturally impossible. See FR-200. The edge case is REPLACED by: ADOT exporter backend error degraded state (persistent 429/500 from X-Ray API causes retry exhaustion and span drops with Extension alive). See FR-201.
- **(Round 24)** What happens when X-Ray PutTraceSegments API returns persistent 429 (rate limit) to ADOT Extension? ADOT exporter retries per `exporterhelper` `retry_on_failure` configuration with exponential backoff. If rate limiting persists beyond `max_elapsed_time`, spans are dropped silently. Extension stays alive. Canary detects trace loss. Distinguished from ADOT crash (vector #3) by Extension process survival and from drop race (vector #1) by sustained near-100% loss rate.
- **(Round 24)** What happens when `force_flush()` execution exceeds the Lambda platform's 2-second extension shutdown window? Lambda platform sends SIGKILL to the Extension process after 2 seconds. Any spans still in the OTLP export pipeline (in-flight HTTP request to X-Ray backend) are lost. The BSP's `force_flush()` timeout parameter (FR-062) only controls the SDK-side wait; the Lambda platform's SIGKILL overrides it.
- **(Round 24)** What happens when requirements checklist backfill discovers FRs that were superseded or amended in later rounds? Superseded FRs should be tracked with `[SUPERSEDED by FR-NNN]` status in the checklist, preserving traceability. The original FR text remains in the spec; only the checklist status changes.
- **(Round 24)** What happens when ADOT exporter enters persistent retry loop during the streaming phase of a long-running SSE Lambda? Spans accumulate in BSP queue while exporter is blocked retrying. If queue fills (default 2048 spans), new spans are dropped via `deque` FIFO eviction. `dropped` counter increments but no alarm fires because BSP drop detection is external (span count comparison). SSE sessions lasting minutes could lose significant trace data during X-Ray backend degradation.
- **(Round 24)** What happens when an operator adds a new SpanProcessor to the TracerProvider without consulting FR-192's ordering contract? The new processor may execute before the allow-list processor (receiving unfiltered attributes) or after the audit processor (receiving already-audited spans). Defense: FR-192 documents the ordering contract and unit test (SC-136) fails on ordering violation. But runtime additions (via custom initialization code) bypass the unit test.
- **(Round 23)** Canary alarm fires for brief outage that already ended — canary detects failure at T+10min, alarm fires, operator investigates but X-Ray recovered at T+8min. The operator sees a healthy system and dismisses the alarm as false positive. Defense: FR-197 documents this as expected behavior with runbook guidance to check X-Ray service health dashboard and recent canary metrics trend (not just current state).

## Requirements *(mandatory)*

### Functional Requirements

**Backend Lambda X-Ray Subsegments**

- **FR-001**: System MUST add X-Ray tracing to all SSE Streaming Lambda operations: global stream handling, config stream handling, DynamoDB polling, connection acquisition, connection release, and event dispatch. Because the SSE Lambda uses `RESPONSE_STREAM` invoke mode, the Lambda runtime's auto-created segment closes before streaming begins. Tracing during streaming MUST use a mechanism with an independent lifecycle that does not depend on the Lambda runtime's X-Ray segment being open (see FR-026 revised).
- **FR-002**: System MUST add X-Ray subsegments to all 7 silent failure paths: (1) circuit breaker load, (2) circuit breaker save, (3) audit trail persistence, (4) downstream notification SNS publish, (5) time-series fanout batch write, (6) self-healing item fetch, (7) parallel fetcher error aggregation.
- **FR-003**: All service calls made by the Metrics Lambda (DynamoDB queries, CloudWatch API calls) MUST appear as auto-instrumented subsegments in X-Ray traces. Currently, the Metrics Lambda has zero X-Ray SDK integration despite Active tracing being enabled at the infrastructure level.
- **FR-004**: System MUST add explicit X-Ray subsegments to the Metrics Lambda for DynamoDB queries and CloudWatch `put_metric_data` calls.
- **FR-005**: System MUST mark X-Ray subsegments as error/fault when the wrapped operation catches an exception, including the exception type and message as metadata.

**X-Ray Annotations and Metadata**

- **FR-006**: System MUST replace custom structured latency logging in `latency_logger.py` with X-Ray subsegment annotations containing: `event_type`, `latency_ms`, `is_cold_start`, `is_clock_skew`, `connection_count`.
- **FR-007**: System MUST replace custom structured cache logging in `cache_logger.py` with X-Ray subsegment annotations containing: `cache_hit_rate`, `cache_entry_count`, `cache_max_entries`, `trigger`, `is_cold_start`. Each poll-cycle subsegment (already created per FR-006's span-per-poll convention) MUST include a `cache_hit` boolean annotation (`true`/`false`) to enable per-request trace filtering (e.g., `annotation.cache_hit = false`) for debugging emergent cache issues. The `cache_hit` annotation is added to the existing poll-cycle subsegment — NOT as a separate subsegment — to avoid creating ~180 additional subsegments per SSE invocation (900s / 5s poll interval) that would drown out meaningful subsegments in the X-Ray waterfall. The aggregate `cache_hit_rate` is retained on the parent span for at-a-glance health; the per-poll `cache_hit` enables drill-down.
- **FR-008**: System MUST include X-Ray annotations on connection lifecycle subsegments: `connection_id`, `current_count`, `max_connections`.
- **FR-009**: System MUST include X-Ray annotations on DynamoDB polling subsegments: `item_count`, `changed_count`, `poll_duration_ms`, `sentiment_type`.

**Correlation ID Consolidation**

- **FR-010**: System MUST replace the custom `get_correlation_id()` function with X-Ray trace ID retrieval from the active segment.
- **FR-011**: System MUST replace the custom `generate_correlation_id()` function with X-Ray trace ID retrieval.
- **FR-012**: System MUST include the X-Ray trace ID as a top-level field in all operational structured log entries (error logs, warning logs, info-level operational events) so CloudWatch Logs Insights queries can join log entries to X-Ray traces. Note: FR-022 and FR-023 remove tracing-specific structured logs; this requirement applies to the operational logs that remain.

**Cross-Service Trace Propagation**

- **FR-013**: System MUST verify that Active X-Ray tracing is enabled on both the Ingestion Lambda and the Analysis Lambda, and that the SNS subscription between them supports automatic trace context propagation via the `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute. The result is that both Lambda invocations appear under the same trace ID with zero manual MessageAttributes configuration.
- **FR-014**: System MUST propagate the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header from the frontend SSE proxy (Next.js API route) to the upstream SSE Lambda call when the header is present on the incoming request.
- **FR-015**: System MUST add `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` to the CORS `Access-Control-Allow-Headers` list for both API Gateway and Lambda Function URLs.
- **FR-016**: The frontend API client MUST include the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header on all outgoing requests when the browser has an active trace context. In test environments where RUM sampling is set to 100%, every API request from the browser MUST carry this header.

**Infrastructure Alignment**

- **FR-017**: All Lambda execution roles MUST have sufficient permissions to emit X-Ray trace segments and telemetry records. Currently, only 2 of 6 Lambda roles have explicit X-Ray write permissions; the remaining 4 (Ingestion, Analysis, Dashboard, Metrics) MUST be aligned.
- **FR-018**: X-Ray instrumentation errors MUST propagate to the Lambda runtime unhandled, resulting in Lambda invocation failure visible in standard error metrics. No error-suppression or fallback logic around tracing calls is permitted.

**X-Ray Canary (Watcher of the Watcher)**

- **FR-019**: System MUST implement a canary that periodically submits a batch of test traces to X-Ray and queries for their retrieval, reporting health via a non-X-Ray channel (CloudWatch metric). The canary MUST track both presence (did my test trace arrive?) and completeness (did all N of my test traces arrive?) to detect partial data loss from throttling.
- **FR-020**: System MUST configure the canary's health metric alarm with `treat_missing_data = breaching` so the alarm fires if the canary itself stops running.
- **FR-021**: The canary MUST be the sole non-X-Ray tracing and correlation mechanism in the system. All other custom tracing logs (latency_logger, cache_logger), custom correlation IDs, and custom log-based trace correlation MUST be consolidated onto X-Ray. Standard operational logging (error messages, audit records) and CloudWatch metrics (billing alarms, auto-scaling triggers, SLO dashboards) are not in scope and remain unchanged.

**Removal of Replaced Systems**

- **FR-022**: System MUST remove the custom latency structured logging from `latency_logger.py`. After X-Ray subsegment annotations replace its tracing function, the module and all its call sites MUST be deleted. No adapter or wrapper is permitted — the X-Ray annotations ARE the replacement.
- **FR-023**: System MUST remove the custom cache structured logging from `cache_logger.py`. After X-Ray annotations replace its tracing function, the module and all its call sites MUST be deleted.
- **FR-024**: System MUST remove the custom `get_correlation_id()` and `generate_correlation_id()` functions after X-Ray trace ID retrieval replaces them.

**SSE Streaming Trace Context (Round 2, revised in Round 3)**

- **FR-025** [Round 3 — Revised]: The SSE Lambda MUST preserve trace context across the async-to-sync bridge boundary. The system MUST rely on the default `threading.local()` context storage (which correctly propagates through `asyncio.new_event_loop().run_until_complete()` on the same thread). The system MUST NOT configure the X-Ray SDK's `AsyncContext`, which uses `TaskLocalStorage` that loses context across event loop boundaries (known bugs: aws-xray-sdk-python #164, #310, #446).
- **FR-026** [Round 3 — Replaced]: ~~During SSE streaming, the system MUST create independent X-Ray segments for each poll cycle.~~ **INVALIDATED**: `begin_segment()` is a no-op in Lambda (`LambdaContext.put_segment()` silently discards, `FacadeSegment` raises `FacadeSegmentMutationException`). **Replacement**: The SSE Lambda MUST use a tracing mechanism with an independent lifecycle for operations that execute during response streaming (after the handler returns the generator). This mechanism MUST: (a) create trace spans during active streaming, (b) link spans to the original invocation's trace ID for unified visualization, (c) export spans to X-Ray, (d) function independently of the Lambda runtime's facade segment lifecycle. The mechanism MUST run as a separate process (Lambda Extension) with its own INIT and SHUTDOWN phases, ensuring trace data is flushed even when the Lambda execution environment freezes.
- **FR-027** [Round 3 — Replaced]: ~~Auto-patched boto3 calls during streaming MUST execute within independently created segments.~~ **Replacement**: All service calls during SSE response streaming (DynamoDB queries, CloudWatch metric emission) MUST be captured within traced spans. These calls occur after the Lambda handler returns, when the X-Ray SDK's facade segment is closed. The independent lifecycle tracing mechanism from FR-026 MUST capture these calls so they appear in X-Ray as part of the connection's trace.

**SendGrid Explicit Instrumentation (Round 2 — Emergent)**

- **FR-028**: The SendGrid email sending operation in the Notification Lambda MUST be wrapped in an explicit X-Ray subsegment. The SendGrid SDK uses `urllib`/`python-http-client` for HTTP transport, which is NOT auto-patched by the X-Ray SDK. The subsegment MUST capture: HTTP status code, request duration, and error details on failure.

**Tracer Standardization (Round 2, updated in Round 3)**

- **FR-029** [Round 3 — Updated]: All non-streaming Lambda functions (Ingestion, Analysis, Dashboard, Notification, Metrics) MUST use a consistent X-Ray instrumentation approach that automatically captures exceptions as subsegment errors. The SSE Streaming Lambda MUST use the independent lifecycle tracing mechanism from FR-026, which has different instrumentation requirements due to the RESPONSE_STREAM segment lifecycle constraint. Both approaches MUST produce traces that appear in the same X-Ray console with unified trace IDs.
- **FR-030**: The system MUST eliminate double-patching of HTTP/AWS SDK clients. Currently, the Dashboard Lambda calls both explicit `patch_all()` and initializes a Tracer with `auto_patch=True` (the default), causing boto3 and requests to be patched twice. After standardization, each Lambda MUST have exactly one patching mechanism.

**Async Generator Tracing Safety (Round 3 — New)**

- **FR-031**: The system MUST NOT apply `@tracer.capture_method` or any equivalent function-wrapping decorator to async generator functions. The Powertools Tracer dispatcher does not check `inspect.isasyncgenfunction()` and silently routes async generators to the synchronous wrapper, which captures only generator creation time (near-zero) rather than iteration time. All async generator tracing MUST use manual subsegment or span context managers within the generator body. Source: `aws_lambda_powertools/tracing/tracer.py` — `isasyncgenfunction()` is never called in the dispatch chain.

**Frontend SSE Trace Propagation (Round 3 — New)**

- **FR-032**: The frontend SSE client MUST use `fetch()` with `ReadableStream` consumption instead of the `EventSource` API for connections that require trace header propagation. The `EventSource` API does not support custom HTTP headers per the WHATWG HTML Living Standard (Section 9.2). Using `fetch()` enables CloudWatch RUM's automatic `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header injection (when `addXRayTraceIdHeader: true` is configured in the RUM http telemetry) and provides a mechanism for manual header attachment.
- **FR-033**: Since the `EventSource` API's built-in auto-reconnection is lost when switching to `fetch()` + `ReadableStream` (FR-032), the frontend SSE client MUST implement equivalent reconnection logic: exponential backoff with jitter on connection failure, `Last-Event-ID` header propagation for stream resumption, and connection state management matching the reliability guarantees of the replaced `EventSource`.

**Sampling Strategy (Round 3 — New)**

- **FR-034**: The system MUST configure X-Ray sampling rules per environment: 100% sampling (reservoir=1, fixed_rate=1.0) in dev/preprod for complete debuggability, and a documented production rate that balances cost with trace availability. The system MUST configure an X-Ray Group with filter expression `fault = true OR error = true` that automatically generates CloudWatch metrics (ApproximateErrorCount, FaultCount, latency percentiles) from errored traces, enabling error rate monitoring and alarming directly from trace data.
- **FR-035**: The system MUST configure server-side X-Ray sampling rules at the API Gateway and Lambda level that make independent sampling decisions, regardless of client-supplied `Sampled=1` in the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. A malicious client MUST NOT be able to force 100% sampling and inflate X-Ray costs. The server-side sampling configuration is the authoritative source of truth for sampling decisions.

**Trace Data Integrity (Round 3 — New)**

- **FR-036**: The X-Ray canary (FR-019) MUST additionally track the ratio of submitted test traces to successfully retrieved test traces across consecutive intervals. When the retrieval ratio drops below a configured threshold (indicating systematic data loss from throttling, daemon failure, or SDK errors), the canary MUST emit a dedicated `trace_data_loss` CloudWatch metric that triggers an alarm.
- **FR-037**: The system MUST NOT manually configure the X-Ray SDK's `AsyncContext` on any Lambda function. The default `threading.local()` context storage correctly propagates through `asyncio.new_event_loop().run_until_complete()` calls on the same thread. Manually configuring `AsyncContext` uses `TaskLocalStorage`, which stores context on `asyncio.Task` objects — new tasks in a new event loop have no inherited context, breaking the async-to-sync bridge pattern used by the SSE Lambda. Known open issues: aws-xray-sdk-python #164 (concurrent async subsegments cause `AlreadyEndedException`), #310 (concurrent asyncio tasks + X-Ray in Lambda), #446 (context not propagated with `run_in_executor`).

**Cost Guard (Round 3 — New)**

- **FR-038**: The system MUST have CloudWatch billing alarms for X-Ray costs at thresholds of $10, $25, and $50 per month. At 100% sampling, X-Ray costs scale linearly at $5 per million traces recorded plus $0.50 per million traces retrieved/scanned. The free tier covers 100,000 traces recorded and 1,000,000 retrieved per month.

**Scope Clarification (Round 4 — New)**

- **FR-039**: "X-Ray exclusive" applies to **tracing** — the mechanism for distributed request tracing, latency analysis, and dependency visualization. CloudWatch alarms on Lambda built-in metrics (Errors, Duration, Throttles) and custom application metrics are a separate, complementary system for operational alerting. Alarms tell operators "something is wrong"; X-Ray traces tell operators "what went wrong and where." Both systems are required for complete observability. CloudWatch alarms are NOT duplicative with X-Ray and MUST NOT be removed as part of the X-Ray consolidation effort. Standard operational logging (error messages, audit records) also remains unchanged per FR-021.

**Operational Alarm Coverage (Round 4 — New)**

- **FR-040**: All 6 Lambda functions MUST have CloudWatch error alarms on the `AWS/Lambda` `Errors` metric. Currently, SSE Streaming Lambda and Metrics Lambda have zero error alarms (audit Section 4.3).
- **FR-041**: All 6 Lambda functions MUST have CloudWatch latency alarms on the `AWS/Lambda` `Duration` metric at the p95 statistic. Currently, Ingestion Lambda, Notification Lambda, SSE Streaming Lambda, and Metrics Lambda are missing latency alarms (audit Section 9.3).
- **FR-042**: The following custom metrics currently emitted without alarms MUST each have a CloudWatch alarm configured: `StuckItems` (items stuck in "pending" >5min), `ConnectionAcquireFailures` (SSE connection pool exhaustion), `EventLatencyMs` (SSE live update latency p95 > 3000ms SLO), `MetricsLambdaErrors` (monitoring system errors), `HighLatencyAlert` (ingestion latency >30s), `PollDurationMs` (DynamoDB poll duration), `AnalysisErrors` (analysis processing errors). Source: audit Section 4.2.
- **FR-043**: The 7 silent failure paths identified in audit Section 8 MUST emit dedicated CloudWatch metrics in addition to X-Ray subsegments (FR-002, FR-005). X-Ray subsegments provide trace context for debugging; CloudWatch metrics provide 100% occurrence capture for alarming regardless of X-Ray sampling configuration. The required metrics are: `CircuitBreakerPersistenceFailure` (paths 1-2), `AuditEventPersistenceFailure` (path 3), `DownstreamNotificationFailure` (path 4), `TimeseriesFanoutPartialFailure` (path 5), `SelfHealingItemFetchFailure` (path 6), `ParallelFetcherErrors` (path 7).
- **FR-044**: The CloudWatch dashboard alarm status widget MUST display ALL configured alarms. The audit identified that the current widget shows only 6 of 30+ alarms (audit Section 6.3), giving operators a false sense of "all green" when non-displayed alarms may be firing.
- **FR-045**: All CloudWatch alarms monitoring metrics where absence indicates failure (heartbeat metrics, canary metrics, pipeline throughput metrics such as `NewItemsIngested`) MUST use `treat_missing_data = breaching`. Alarms monitoring error count metrics where zero data points means "no errors occurred" MUST use `treat_missing_data = notBreaching`. The configuration MUST be audited and corrected for all existing alarms.

**ADOT Coexistence Constraints (Round 4 — New)**

- **FR-046**: The SSE Lambda MUST NOT enable ADOT auto-instrumentation via the `AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER=/opt/otel-handler` environment variable. ADOT MUST function solely as an OTLP receiver sidecar (Lambda Extension) that accepts spans on `localhost:4318` and exports them to X-Ray. ADOT auto-instrumentation wraps the handler entry point (conflicting with Powertools `@tracer.capture_lambda_handler` from FR-029) and patches botocore (conflicting with X-Ray SDK patching from Powertools `auto_patch=True`), causing duplicate handler wrapping and duplicate spans for every boto3 call.
- **FR-047**: The OTel `service.name` resource attribute configured for ADOT span export on the SSE Lambda MUST match the `POWERTOOLS_SERVICE_NAME` environment variable used by Powertools Tracer. X-Ray service map aggregates nodes by service name. Mismatched names cause the same Lambda to appear as two disconnected nodes in the service map — one for handler-phase subsegments and one for streaming-phase spans.

**SSE Reconnection Trace Correlation (Round 4 — New)**

- **FR-048**: All SSE connection traces MUST include a stable `session_id` annotation that persists across reconnections, enabling operators to query X-Ray by `session_id` to find all traces for a logical SSE session. On reconnection (new trace ID due to new `fetch()` call), the trace MUST additionally include a `previous_trace_id` annotation referencing the prior connection's X-Ray trace ID and a `connection_sequence` annotation (incrementing integer starting at 1). X-Ray does not support native span links (OpenTelemetry link data stored in segment metadata is not queryable via X-Ray console or API), so annotation-based correlation is the required pattern.

**Meta-Observability (Round 4 — New)**

- **FR-049**: The observability canary (extending FR-019) MUST additionally verify CloudWatch metric emission health on each canary interval. The canary emits a known test metric via `put_metric_data`, waits for the CloudWatch ingestion delay (typically 60-120 seconds), and then queries for it via `get_metric_statistics`. If the test metric is not retrievable within the expected window, the canary reports CloudWatch metric pipeline failure. This check is in addition to the X-Ray trace submission/retrieval check from FR-019.
- **FR-050**: The canary MUST report CloudWatch metric pipeline failure via a channel independent of CloudWatch alarms. If CloudWatch is degraded, a CloudWatch alarm on the canary's own metric may also fail to fire. The canary MUST use an out-of-band alerting mechanism (e.g., SNS direct publish to email/SMS, external monitoring API) for meta-observability failures. Source: AWS Well-Architected Operational Excellence Pillar — "never alert on failure using the same system that failed."
- **FR-051**: The canary Lambda MUST use a separate IAM role from all application Lambdas. If an IAM policy change revokes X-Ray or CloudWatch permissions from application Lambda roles, the canary MUST retain its permissions to detect and report the failure. This isolation ensures the canary is not affected by the same failure mode it is designed to detect.

**OTel-to-X-Ray Trace Context Bridging (Round 5 — New)**

- **FR-052**: The SSE Lambda's OTel SDK MUST be configured with the `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator` (from `opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray`) as the global text map propagator. This propagator reads the `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` Lambda environment variable (updated by the Lambda runtime on each invocation) and extracts the trace ID, parent span ID, and sampling decision into the OTel context. Without this propagator, streaming-phase OTel spans carry auto-generated trace IDs that differ from the Lambda runtime's X-Ray facade segment, creating disconnected traces that violate SC-010 and SC-023.
