The propagator MUST be configured before any OTel spans are created during the streaming phase. Source: `opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray` package — `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator.extract()` reads `os.environ.get("_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID")`.
- **FR-053**: The SSE Lambda's OTel `TracerProvider` MUST be configured with `AwsXRayIdGenerator` (from `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws`). This ID generator embeds the current unix timestamp in the first 4 bytes of generated trace IDs, matching X-Ray's trace ID format requirement (`1-{unix_epoch_hex}-{unique_hex}`). The default OTel `RandomIdGenerator` produces random bytes in the epoch field, causing X-Ray to misindex traces by time window. Note: when linking to an existing Lambda trace via FR-052, the trace ID comes from `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` (already valid). `AwsXRayIdGenerator` matters for any new root spans (e.g., canary test traces) and is a safety net for correct X-Ray interoperability.
- **FR-054**: The SSE Lambda MUST configure the OTel OTLP exporter to send spans to the ADOT Extension's local HTTP endpoint (`http://localhost:4318/v1/traces`). This MUST be configured via the `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT=http://localhost:4318` environment variable in Terraform or programmatically via the exporter constructor. The HTTP/protobuf exporter (`opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http`) is required — the gRPC exporter adds unnecessary binary dependency overhead in Lambda.

**OTel Span Lifecycle Management (Round 5 — New)**

- **FR-055**: The SSE Lambda's streaming generator MUST call `TracerProvider.force_flush()` in a `finally` block at the end of iteration, with a timeout of at least 5 seconds. The OTel `BatchSpanProcessor` buffers spans in memory and exports them to the ADOT Extension in batches (default batch timeout: 200ms). When the Lambda execution environment freezes after streaming completes, any spans buffered in the final batch interval are suspended in memory. Without `force_flush()`, these spans survive the freeze and are exported on the NEXT invocation — carrying stale trace IDs from the previous invocation, confusing operators and polluting traces. The `force_flush()` target is the local ADOT Extension OTLP receiver (localhost, sub-millisecond latency), not the remote X-Ray API.
- **FR-056**: The SSE Lambda's OTel `TracerProvider` MUST use the `parentbased_always_on` sampler (the OTel SDK default). This sampler reads the sampling decision from the parent context extracted by FR-052's propagator. When the Lambda runtime sets `Sampled=0` in `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID`, the sampler suppresses span creation and export, preventing orphaned traces in X-Ray. When `Sampled=1`, all streaming-phase spans are created and exported normally. The system MUST NOT override the sampler to `always_on`, which would ignore the parent's sampling decision and create spans for unsampled invocations.

**OTel SDK Dependencies (Round 5 — New)**

- **FR-057**: The SSE Lambda's deployment package MUST include the following OTel Python packages for the streaming-phase instrumentation: (1) `opentelemetry-sdk` — core SDK including `TracerProvider`, `BatchSpanProcessor`, (2) `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws` — `AwsXRayIdGenerator` for X-Ray-compatible trace ID generation, (3) `opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray` — `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator` for reading `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID`, (4) `opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http` — OTLP HTTP exporter for sending spans to the ADOT Extension. These packages are ONLY required on the SSE Lambda — non-streaming Lambdas use Powertools Tracer (FR-029) which has no OTel dependency.

**Segment Document Size Guard (Round 5 — New)**

- **FR-058**: All X-Ray subsegment metadata payloads (both X-Ray SDK and OTel span attributes exported via ADOT) MUST be bounded to prevent exceeding the 64KB `PutTraceSegments` document size limit. Error messages MUST be truncated to 2,048 characters. HTTP response bodies MUST NOT be attached as metadata. Stack traces MUST be truncated to the first 10 frames. Documents exceeding 64KB are silently rejected by the X-Ray API (appearing in `UnprocessedTraceSegments` with no SDK-level error), causing permanent trace data loss with no alarm.

**Warm Invocation Trace Context Safety (Round 6 — New)**

- **FR-059**: The SSE Lambda's OTel trace context MUST be extracted from `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` at the start of each handler invocation, NOT at module level. On warm invocations, the Lambda runtime updates `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` to reflect the new invocation's trace ID, but module-level code executes only once (on cold start). Module-level `propagate.extract()` captures the first invocation's trace context and reuses it for ALL subsequent warm invocations, linking every streaming-phase OTel span to the wrong trace ID. The per-invocation extraction MUST occur inside the handler function, before any OTel spans are created. Source: AWS Lambda execution model — environment variables are updated by the runtime between invocations; module-level code runs only on INIT.

**SSE Lambda Auto-Patching Constraint (Round 6 — New)**

- **FR-060**: The SSE Lambda MUST initialize Powertools Tracer with `auto_patch=False` to prevent Powertools' global boto3/botocore patching from creating duplicate X-Ray subsegments alongside OTel spans during the streaming phase. With `auto_patch=True` (the default), Powertools patches `botocore.client.BaseClient._make_api_call` at import time. These patches persist globally and intercept ALL boto3 calls — including those made during the streaming phase after the handler returns. During streaming, each DynamoDB query and CloudWatch `put_metric_data` call creates BOTH an X-Ray subsegment (via the auto-patch, sent to the X-Ray daemon whose lifecycle during RESPONSE_STREAM is undocumented) AND an OTel span (via manual instrumentation, sent to ADOT). This dual-emission produces duplicate entries in X-Ray. Handler-phase AWS SDK calls MUST be traced via explicit `@tracer.capture_method` decorators rather than auto-patching.

**Alarm Threshold Calibration (Round 6 — New)**

- **FR-061**: Task 17 (alarm coverage) MUST review ALL existing CloudWatch alarm thresholds and align them with the 80-90% of timeout threshold standard applied to new alarms. The audit (Section 6.1) identified `analysis_latency_high` at 25s (42% of the Analysis Lambda's 60s timeout) as too generous — this threshold would not fire until nearly half the timeout is consumed, leaving insufficient margin for investigation and remediation before timeout failures begin. Existing alarms MUST be recalibrated to match the threshold methodology applied to new alarms. This review covers all pre-existing alarms, not only the one explicitly called out in the audit.

**ADOT Extension Operational Lifecycle (Round 7 — New)**

- **FR-062**: ~~The SSE Lambda's ADOT Lambda Extension MUST use the collector-only layer distribution.~~ **REWRITTEN in Round 8**: The SSE Lambda is container-based (ECR image with `python:3.13-slim` + custom bootstrap) — Lambda container images CANNOT use Lambda Layers. The ADOT collector MUST be embedded in the SSE Lambda's Dockerfile via multi-stage build using the collector-only container image from `public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/aws-otel-lambda-extension-amd64`. The collector-only image contains the OTel Collector binary that runs the OTLP receiver and X-Ray exporter pipeline, without bundled Python auto-instrumentation code (~35MB vs ~80MB). The Dockerfile MUST copy the collector binary to `/opt/extensions/collector` and the default configuration to `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml`. See FR-069 for deployment details and FR-070 for version pinning. Source: AWS Lambda Container Image docs — "You cannot add Lambda layers to container images"; ADOT ECR Public Gallery — `public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/`.
- **FR-063**: ~~The ADOT Extension layer ARN in Terraform MUST be pinned to a specific version.~~ **REWRITTEN in Round 8**: The ADOT container image reference in the SSE Lambda's Dockerfile MUST be digest-pinned (not tag-referenced). See FR-070 for requirements. The digest determines the embedded OTel Collector binary version, which defines the collector configuration schema, available receivers/exporters, and wire protocol compatibility. An unpinned tag (`:latest` or `:v0.40.0`) could silently introduce breaking changes when the Docker image is rebuilt. Unlike Lambda Layer ARNs which are region-specific, container images from ECR Public Gallery are region-agnostic. Source: OCI Distribution Specification — content-addressable image references.
- **FR-064**: The SSE Lambda MUST verify that the ADOT Extension's collector pipeline includes: (1) an OTLP HTTP receiver on port 4318, and (2) an AWS X-Ray exporter. The ADOT Extension's default collector configuration for Lambda includes this pipeline. If the default configuration needs modification (e.g., to strip unnecessary components for reduced memory footprint, or to add custom processors for attribute filtering), a custom collector configuration MUST be provided via the `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` environment variable pointing to a configuration file in the Lambda deployment package. Unnecessary collector components (metrics pipelines, Prometheus receivers, zpages extensions) MUST be removed from custom configurations to minimize memory and CPU overhead within the 512MB allocation.

**TracerProvider Singleton Lifecycle (Round 7 — New)**

- **FR-065**: The SSE Lambda's OTel `TracerProvider` MUST be instantiated exactly once at module level (during Lambda INIT phase) and reused across all subsequent invocations on that execution environment. The `TracerProvider`, `BatchSpanProcessor`, and `OTLPSpanExporter` are invocation-independent infrastructure — they manage the export pipeline to the ADOT Extension. FR-059's per-invocation trace context extraction requirement applies ONLY to `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator.extract()` (reading the current `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` environment variable), NOT to `TracerProvider` instantiation. Creating a new `TracerProvider` per invocation spawns a new `BatchSpanProcessor` daemon thread (~1MB per thread) and OTLP HTTP connection, orphaning previous instances and causing monotonic memory growth that eventually triggers Lambda OOM termination on warm execution environments. Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor.__init__()` starts a daemon thread via `threading.Thread(daemon=True)`.

**OTel Export Failure Detection (Round 7 — New)**

- **FR-066**: The OTel Python SDK's `BatchSpanProcessor` silently catches all exporter exceptions (via `except Exception` in internal `_export()` method) and `force_flush()` returns `True` regardless of whether the underlying export succeeded or failed. This behavior is mandated by the OTel specification — exporters MUST NOT crash the application — and CANNOT be overridden via configuration. There is no built-in fail-fast mode. The SSE Lambda MUST NOT rely on `force_flush()` return value or exceptions to detect ADOT Extension failures. Instead, ADOT Extension health MUST be monitored via: (1) the X-Ray canary's end-to-end trace verification (FR-019/FR-036), which detects trace absence at aggregate level, and (2) Lambda Extension lifecycle logs (the runtime logs Extension registration and deregistration events, making Extension crashes visible in CloudWatch Logs). The practical mitigation is that the ADOT Extension runs on localhost with sub-millisecond latency — connection failures indicate the Extension process has crashed, not a transient network issue. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 — `BatchProcessor._export()` at `opentelemetry/sdk/_shared_internal/__init__.py`; OTel Specification, SDK Exporters section — "The SDK MUST NOT throw unhandled exceptions."

**OTel Span Semantic Conventions for X-Ray (Round 7 — New)**

- **FR-067**: Streaming-phase OTel spans MUST use semantic conventions that the ADOT X-Ray exporter maps to native X-Ray segment fields: (1) DynamoDB query spans MUST set `db.system = "dynamodb"` and `aws.dynamodb.table_names = ["{table_name}"]` attributes for X-Ray to render them as typed DynamoDB subsegments in the service map, (2) CloudWatch `put_metric_data` spans MUST set `rpc.service = "CloudWatch"` and `rpc.method = "PutMetricData"` for X-Ray to render them as typed CloudWatch subsegments, (3) error spans MUST record exceptions via the OTel span's `record_exception()` method (which sets `exception.type`, `exception.message`, and `exception.stacktrace` attributes per OTel semantic conventions), enabling X-Ray to populate the `cause` field with structured error data. Non-standard attribute names are stored as X-Ray metadata (non-indexed, non-searchable via X-Ray console or API filter expressions), rendering them invisible in default views and eliminating their value for operator debugging. Source: OTel Semantic Conventions for Database (https://opentelemetry.io/docs/specs/semconv/database/) and RPC (https://opentelemetry.io/docs/specs/semconv/rpc/); ADOT X-Ray exporter attribute mapping at `opentelemetry-collector-contrib/exporter/awsxrayexporter`.

**Propagator Configuration Hygiene (Round 7 — New)**

- **FR-068**: The SSE Lambda MUST NOT set the `OTEL_PROPAGATORS` environment variable in its Terraform configuration. The OTel Python SDK reads `OTEL_PROPAGATORS` at module import time and constructs the initial global propagator from it (default: `tracecontext,baggage` for W3C trace context). FR-052 requires `set_global_textmap(AwsXRayLambdaPropagator())` which unconditionally overwrites whatever `OTEL_PROPAGATORS` configured. Setting both creates misleading configuration — the environment variable appears active in Terraform/Lambda console but is silently overridden at runtime, causing operator confusion during debugging when the visible configuration does not match actual behavior. The `set_global_textmap()` call in application code is the single source of truth for propagator selection. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 — `opentelemetry/propagate/__init__.py`, module-level `environ.get(OTEL_PROPAGATORS)` parsing and `set_global_textmap()` override function.

**Container-Based ADOT Deployment (Round 8 — New)**

- **FR-069**: The SSE Lambda's Dockerfile MUST include the ADOT collector binary via multi-stage build from the official AWS ADOT Lambda Extension container image. The collector binary MUST be placed at `/opt/extensions/collector` and the default collector configuration at `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml`. Lambda discovers extensions by scanning `/opt/extensions/` during INIT — this is a Lambda service behavior independent of the runtime base image. The SSE Lambda uses `python:3.13-slim` with a custom bootstrap (not the AWS Lambda base image), which is fully compatible with Lambda Extensions. The multi-stage pattern `COPY --from=<adot-image> /opt/extensions/ /opt/extensions/` is the canonical approach for container-based Lambda Extensions. Source: AWS Lambda Container Image docs — "You cannot add Lambda layers to container images"; AWS Lambda Extensions API — extension discovery in `/opt/extensions/`.
- **FR-070**: The ADOT Lambda Extension container image reference in the SSE Lambda's Dockerfile MUST be digest-pinned (e.g., `public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/aws-otel-lambda-extension-amd64@sha256:{digest}`), NOT tag-referenced (`:latest` or `:v0.40.0`). Container image tags are mutable — the publisher can update the image behind a tag without notice. Digest pinning ensures reproducible builds and prevents silent introduction of breaking collector changes (schema changes, removed exporters) when the Docker image is rebuilt. Version updates MUST be explicit Dockerfile changes tracked in version control. Source: OCI Distribution Specification — content-addressable image references; Docker best practices for reproducible builds.

**OTel Resource Configuration (Round 8 — New)**

- **FR-071**: The SSE Lambda MUST set the `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME` environment variable in its Terraform configuration to a value matching `POWERTOOLS_SERVICE_NAME` (per FR-047). The OTel `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` does NOT set the `service.name` resource attribute. Without `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`, the OTel SDK defaults to `unknown_service`, causing the SSE Lambda to appear as an `unknown_service` node in the X-Ray service map — indistinguishable from any other unconfigured service. This breaks SC-028 (service map correctness). The `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME` env var is read by `Resource.create()` during `TracerProvider` initialization and does not require code changes. Source: OTel Python SDK — `opentelemetry.sdk.resources.Resource.create()` reads `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`; AWS X-Ray uses `service.name` for service map node naming.
- **FR-072**: The SSE Lambda's `TracerProvider` MUST be configured with `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` to populate resource attributes (`cloud.provider`, `cloud.region`, `faas.name`, `faas.version`, `faas.instance`, `faas.max_memory`) on all emitted spans. These attributes provide Lambda execution context in X-Ray trace metadata, enabling operators to identify which Lambda function, version, and execution environment produced each span. The resource configuration MUST merge `Resource.create()` (which reads `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`) with `AwsLambdaResourceDetector().detect()` to combine service identity with Lambda metadata. Source: `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws` package — `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` in `resource/_lambda.py`.

**BatchSpanProcessor Lambda Configuration (Round 8 — New)**

- **FR-073**: The SSE Lambda's `BatchSpanProcessor` MUST be configured with Lambda-tuned parameters: `schedule_delay_millis=1000` (1 second, down from default 5 seconds), `max_queue_size=256` (down from default 2048), `max_export_batch_size=64` (down from default 512). The defaults are designed for long-running server processes with high span throughput. The SSE Lambda produces a bounded number of spans per streaming session (~50-200 over 15 seconds). Reduced parameters consume less memory (smaller queue buffer), export more frequently (1s vs 5s), and reduce the span count at risk if `force_flush()` is not reached. Configuration MUST be via `OTEL_BSP_SCHEDULE_DELAY`, `OTEL_BSP_MAX_QUEUE_SIZE`, and `OTEL_BSP_MAX_EXPORT_BATCH_SIZE` environment variables in Terraform for visibility, or via constructor parameters in application code. Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor` defaults and `OTEL_BSP_*` environment variable support.

**Two-Hop Flush Architecture Acknowledgment (Round 9 — New)**

- **FR-074**: The spec acknowledges that span export from the SSE Lambda to X-Ray involves TWO asynchronous hops: (1) SDK → ADOT Extension via OTLP HTTP on localhost:4318 (fast, sub-millisecond, reliable — handled by FR-055's `force_flush()`), and (2) ADOT Extension → X-Ray backend via HTTPS (slow, measured in hundreds of milliseconds, subject to KNOWN race condition documented in aws-otel-lambda#886 and opentelemetry-lambda#224). The decouple processor in the ADOT Lambda collector mitigates the second hop by holding the Extension from signaling completion until queued data is exported. However, under worst-case timing (span.end() as the very last operation before function exit), the collector context may be canceled before HTTP exports complete, resulting in span loss with error pattern "context canceled" + "Exporting failed. Dropping data." Per-invocation detection of this loss is NOT possible because it occurs in the Extension process. The canary (FR-019/FR-036) provides aggregate detection. The system MUST NOT add fallback logic or retry mechanisms around this — per FR-018, the Extension's internal failures are the Extension's responsibility. The ADOT Extension's decouple processor is the accepted mitigation, not a fallback.
- **FR-075**: The ADOT Extension's collector configuration for the SSE Lambda MUST include the `decouple` processor in the pipeline to prevent the Lambda-specific span drop race condition. The decouple processor separates span reception from export, ensuring the Extension does not call the Next API until all queued spans are exported to the X-Ray backend. Without the decouple processor, the Extension signals invocation completion while HTTP exports are still in-flight, and the execution environment freezes before exports complete. The decouple processor is included in the ADOT Lambda Extension's default configuration — a custom `collector.yaml` MUST preserve it if FR-064's configuration modifications remove it. Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda/blob/main/collector/processor/decoupleprocessor/README.md

**OTel SDK Lambda Safety (Round 9 — New)**

- **FR-076**: The SSE Lambda MUST NOT call `BotocoreInstrumentor().instrument()` or any OTel auto-instrumentation for AWS SDK clients. The SSE Lambda's instrumentation architecture is: (a) handler-phase AWS SDK calls traced via explicit Powertools `@tracer.capture_method` decorators (per FR-060), (b) streaming-phase AWS SDK calls traced via manual OTel span creation with semantic conventions (per FR-067). Enabling `BotocoreInstrumentor` would patch `botocore.client.BaseClient._make_api_call` globally, creating OTel spans for EVERY AWS SDK call — including handler-phase calls that are already traced by Powertools, producing duplicate entries in X-Ray. The prohibition on `auto_patch=True` (FR-060) prevents Powertools' X-Ray SDK patching but does NOT prevent OTel botocore instrumentation, which is a separate mechanism. Both MUST be prohibited.
- **FR-077**: The SSE Lambda's `TracerProvider` MUST be instantiated with `shutdown_on_exit=False`. The default `shutdown_on_exit=True` registers a Python `atexit` handler that calls `TracerProvider.shutdown()` during interpreter finalization. In Lambda, `atexit` handlers fire during execution environment recycling (not between warm invocations). In Python 3.13+, the `ConcurrentMultiSpanProcessor.shutdown()` can race with a pending export, causing `RuntimeError: cannot schedule new futures after shutdown`. Since FR-055 mandates `force_flush()` at end of each streaming session, the `atexit` handler is redundant. Setting `shutdown_on_exit=False` eliminates the race with zero functional impact. Source: opentelemetry-python#4461 — `ConcurrentMultiSpanProcessor` shutdown race condition.

**Canary Robustness (Round 9 — New)**

- **FR-078**: The X-Ray canary (FR-019) MUST implement retry-with-backoff for trace retrieval. After submitting test traces, the canary queries `BatchGetTraces` at 30 seconds, then retries at 60 seconds if traces are not found. X-Ray's propagation delay is "generally 30 seconds" per the AWS FAQ but is NOT a deterministic SLA — under regional load, indexing may take longer. The `BatchGetTraces` API cannot distinguish "not yet indexed" from "trace permanently lost" — both result in the trace ID appearing in `UnprocessedTraceIds` or being absent from the `Traces` response array. The canary MUST treat these cases identically and only report failure after the final retry. The 2-consecutive-interval alarm threshold (FR-020) provides the outer detection boundary. Source: https://aws.amazon.com/xray/faqs/
- **FR-079**: The canary (FR-049) MUST classify CloudWatch `put_metric_data` errors into two categories and handle them differently: (a) **Transient errors** (`ThrottlingException`, `InternalFailure`, `ServiceUnavailable`, `InternalServiceError`) — retry with exponential backoff (max 3 retries), then report failure if all retries exhausted, (b) **Permanent IAM/credential errors** (`AccessDeniedException`, `NotAuthorized`, `InvalidClientTokenId`) — trigger IMMEDIATE out-of-band alert via FR-050 with zero retries. IAM revocation is the EXACT failure mode that FR-051's separate IAM role is designed to detect. Without error classification, an IAM revocation on application Lambda roles is silently retried for multiple canary intervals, losing critical response time. The canary's own metric emission uses its separate IAM role (FR-051) and is unaffected by application role changes — but the canary's CloudWatch HEALTH CHECK (which verifies application metrics are flowing) must detect when application roles lose permissions. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/APIReference/API_PutMetricData.html
- **FR-080**: The canary SHOULD support a secondary out-of-band alerting channel (external webhook endpoint such as PagerDuty or Opsgenie HTTPS API) in addition to SNS direct publish (FR-050). During simultaneous AWS regional failures affecting both CloudWatch AND SNS, the canary has no alerting path with SNS alone. Industry best practice from AWS outage post-mortems (e.g., 2017 S3 outage) is to use at least two independent alerting channels. This is a SHOULD (not MUST) because simultaneous CloudWatch + SNS regional failure is a low-probability event, but production deployments handling critical workloads benefit from this redundancy.

**Frontend SSE Server-Side Requirements (Round 9 — New)**

- **FR-081**: The SSE Lambda server MUST check the `Last-Event-ID` request header on connection establishment and resume the event stream from the corresponding position. If the client sends `Last-Event-ID: {id}` (per FR-033's client-side requirement), the server MUST NOT replay events already delivered (events with id <= Last-Event-ID). Without server-side support, FR-033's client-side `Last-Event-ID` propagation is hollow — the client sends the header but the server ignores it, causing duplicate events on reconnection. If server-side stream resumption is not feasible for the current SSE Lambda architecture (e.g., events are ephemeral and not stored), the server MUST respond with a `X-SSE-Resume-Supported: false` header so the client can implement idempotent deduplication.
- **FR-082**: The SSE Lambda Function URL's CORS configuration MUST include `x-amzn-trace-id` in `Access-Control-Expose-Headers`. Per the CORS specification, browsers can only read response headers explicitly listed in `Access-Control-Expose-Headers`. FR-048 requires the client to capture the response `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header value as `previous_trace_id` for reconnection trace correlation. Without `ExposeHeaders` including this header, the browser JavaScript cannot access it, making FR-048's reconnection trace correlation impossible. This is a hard prerequisite for FR-048, not optional.
- **FR-083**: The frontend SSE client's reconnection logic (FR-033) MUST distinguish between graceful server close and network error using the `ReadableStreamDefaultReader.closed` Promise (fulfills on graceful close, rejects on error). On graceful server close (expected — e.g., Lambda timeout, stream complete): reconnect with the SSE `retry:` field value or a short fixed delay (1-3 seconds). On network error (unexpected — e.g., WiFi drop, server crash): reconnect with exponential backoff plus jitter per FR-033's existing specification. Uniform backoff on all close types unnecessarily delays reconnection after expected server-initiated closes, degrading user experience.

**BSP Default Correction (Round 9 — Assumption Fix)**

- **FR-084**: The spec's Round 5 assumption regarding "default batch timeout of 200ms" is INCORRECT and MUST be corrected. The actual `BatchSpanProcessor` `schedule_delay_millis` default is **5000ms** (5 seconds), confirmed by the OTel Python SDK source code and the OTel Specification. FR-073 correctly overrides this to 1000ms, so runtime behavior is unaffected. The incorrect 200ms figure in the assumption and edge case text (originally added in Round 5) caused downstream reasoning errors about the flush window size — the actual default means spans buffer 25x longer than documented. This FR corrects the assumption; no runtime change is required.

**Client Disconnect Handling (Round 10 — New)**

- **FR-085**: The SSE Lambda's streaming generator MUST catch `BrokenPipeError` (Python's signal that the client has disconnected mid-write) in its event dispatch loop and set the OTel span attribute `client.disconnected=true` on the active span before propagating the exception. Python custom runtimes have NO standard mechanism to detect client disconnect (unlike Node.js `StreamifyResponse` which provides `metadata.onAbort`). `BrokenPipeError` on `response.write()` is the ONLY available signal. When caught: (a) set `client.disconnected=true` annotation on the current streaming-phase span, (b) set span status to `OK` (not `ERROR` — client disconnect is expected behavior, not a server fault), (c) skip remaining DynamoDB polls, (d) proceed to `finally` block for `force_flush()`. Without this handling, post-disconnect spans report successful operations that no client received, inflating success metrics. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/configuration-response-streaming.html — "Streamed responses are not interrupted or stopped when the invoking client connection is broken."

**BSP Queue Size Correction (Round 10 — Amends FR-073)**

- **FR-086**: FR-073's `max_queue_size` MUST be recalculated based on expected span throughput per invocation and set to >= 2x the expected maximum. Calculation: 15-second streaming session × ~15 DynamoDB polls/second × ~3 spans per poll cycle (db query span + event dispatch span + metric emit span) = ~675 spans per invocation. 2x safety margin = 1,350 minimum. **FR-073 is hereby AMENDED**: `max_queue_size` changes from `512` to `1500`. The `max_export_batch_size` remains at `64` (unchanged) and `schedule_delay_millis` remains at `1000` (unchanged). The 2x margin accounts for: (a) variable poll frequency under load, (b) additional spans from error handling paths, (c) spans created between `force_flush()` calls during batch intervals. The silent drop behavior of `BatchSpanProcessor` (logs WARNING only, no metric, no exception) makes undersized queues particularly dangerous — span loss is invisible without explicit log monitoring. Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor.on_end()` uses `queue.put_nowait()`, catches `queue.Full`, logs warning.

**Canary IsPartial Trace Check (Round 10 — New)**

- **FR-087**: The X-Ray canary (FR-078) MUST check the `IsPartial` flag on `TraceSummary` objects returned by `GetTraceSummaries` or `BatchGetTraces` for its test traces. If `IsPartial=true` after the final retry attempt (per FR-078's retry-with-backoff): (a) emit a dedicated CloudWatch metric `canary.trace.partial` with value 1, (b) report the trace verification as **degraded** (not complete success AND not complete failure), (c) include `is_partial=true` in the canary's OTel span attributes. A trace with `IsPartial=true` means not all segments have been received by X-Ray — critical streaming-phase spans from ADOT may be missing while the trace "exists" from the canary's perspective. Without this check, the canary reports false-green when ADOT span export is failing but the Lambda runtime's facade segment arrived successfully. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/xray/latest/devguide/xray-concepts.html — "X-Ray tags traces as incomplete or partial."

**SSE Reconnection Control (Round 10 — New)**

- **FR-088**: The SSE Lambda MUST emit a `retry:` field in the initial SSE frame of each connection with a recommended reconnection interval in milliseconds (e.g., `retry: 3000\n`). The SSE specification (WHATWG HTML Living Standard, Section 9.2) defines this field as the server-controlled mechanism for client reconnection timing. Without it, clients use their own implementation-defined default (varies by browser/library). The `retry:` value MUST be: (a) emitted as the FIRST field in the SSE stream (before any `data:` events), (b) set to 3000ms (3 seconds) as default, (c) configurable via environment variable `SSE_RETRY_MS` for per-environment tuning. Note: since the frontend uses `fetch()+ReadableStream` (not `EventSource`), the `retry:` field is NOT auto-parsed — the frontend must explicitly parse it per FR-089. Source: https://html.spec.whatwg.org/multipage/server-sent-events.html — Section 9.2, "retry" field.
- **FR-089**: The frontend SSE client (FR-033/FR-083) MUST parse the `retry:` field from the server's SSE stream and use its value as the reconnection delay for graceful server closes (overriding FR-083's default 1-3 second range with the server-specified value). Since the frontend uses `fetch()+ReadableStream` (NOT `EventSource`), the SSE protocol fields (`retry:`, `id:`, `event:`, `data:`) are NOT automatically parsed. The client MUST implement SSE field parsing for at least `retry:` and `data:` fields. If no `retry:` field is received, fall back to FR-083's default behavior. This ensures server-controlled reconnection timing without requiring `EventSource` (which cannot send custom headers per FR-032's CORS requirements).

**Explicit Decouple Processor in Custom Config (Round 10 — Strengthens FR-075)**

- **FR-090**: The custom ADOT collector YAML (created per FR-069 for the container-based SSE Lambda) MUST explicitly include the `decouple` processor in the `service.pipelines.traces.processors` list. The ADOT Lambda Layer's automatic decouple processor injection (documented in the decouple processor README: "the OpenTelemetry Lambda Layer automatically configures the decouple processor when the batch processor is used") ONLY applies to Lambda Layer deployments. Container-based deployments with custom collector configurations (FR-064) receive NO automatic processor injection. Without explicit inclusion, the SSE Lambda's span export reverts to the known ~30% drop rate (aws-otel-lambda#886). This FR strengthens FR-075 by making the container-specific requirement explicit. The pipeline order MUST be: `processors: [decouple, batch]` (decouple before batch). Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda/blob/main/collector/processor/decoupleprocessor/README.md

**BSP Queue Overflow Observability (Round 10 — New)**

- **FR-091**: The SSE Lambda MUST configure Python logging to capture `BatchSpanProcessor` WARNING-level log messages and emit a structured log entry when span queue overflow occurs. The OTel SDK logs `"Queue is full, dropping span"` at WARNING level when `queue.put_nowait()` raises `Full`. This log line is the ONLY observable signal of span loss (no metric, no exception, no span attribute). The structured log entry MUST include: (a) `span_queue_overflow=true` field for CloudWatch Logs Insights filtering, (b) current queue size, (c) span name being dropped. A CloudWatch Logs metric filter on `span_queue_overflow=true` SHOULD be created to provide alarming on span loss. This is defense-in-depth — FR-086's queue sizing should prevent overflow, but silent data loss requires independent detection.

**Custom Bootstrap Trace Context Propagation (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-092**: The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap MUST read the `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` header from the `/runtime/invocation/next` Runtime API response and set `os.environ['_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID']` to its value BEFORE calling the handler function on EVERY invocation (cold and warm). Per the AWS Lambda custom runtime contract, the bootstrap is responsible for propagating trace context from the Runtime API to the function process. Without this, `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` retains the cold start value on warm invocations, and FR-059's `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator.extract()` reads stale trace context — silently linking all warm invocation OTel spans to the first invocation's trace ID. The X-Ray SDK's `LambdaContext._refresh_context()` also reads this env var, meaning BOTH the handler-phase (Powertools) and streaming-phase (OTel) traces are broken on warm invocations without this fix. This is a prerequisite for FR-052 and FR-059. Source: AWS Lambda Custom Runtime Contract — "Your function must set `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` to the value of the `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` header"; confirmed by code inspection that the current bootstrap at `src/lambdas/sse_streaming/bootstrap` (lines 39-51) reads `Lambda-Runtime-Aws-Request-Id` but omits `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id`.

**Deadline-Aware Proactive Span Flush (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-093**: The SSE Lambda's streaming generator MUST implement a deadline-aware flush mechanism that calls `TracerProvider.force_flush()` BEFORE the Lambda timeout kills the process. The Lambda Runtime API response includes a `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms` header containing the invocation deadline as a Unix epoch timestamp in milliseconds. The streaming generator MUST check remaining time on each poll cycle and trigger proactive flush when remaining time falls below a configurable threshold (default: 3000ms). This is REQUIRED because Lambda does NOT send SIGTERM to the custom runtime process on timeout — the process is killed directly (SIGKILL after Extension Shutdown phase). Python `finally` blocks do NOT execute on SIGKILL. FR-055's `force_flush()` in the `finally` block handles normal completion and client disconnect (BrokenPipeError) but NOT Lambda timeout. Without proactive flush, up to 1000ms of buffered spans (per FR-073's batch interval) are permanently lost on every timeout. The `finally` block `force_flush()` (FR-055) MUST be retained as defense-in-depth for non-timeout exits; FR-093 adds proactive flush for the timeout path. Source: AWS Lambda Runtime Environment Lifecycle — Lambda does not send SIGTERM before SIGKILL on invocation timeout; Lambda Runtime API — `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms` header.

**FR-035 Amendment: Function URL Sampling Limitation (Round 11 — Amends FR-035)**

- **FR-094**: FR-035's requirement that "server-side X-Ray sampling rules make independent sampling decisions, regardless of client-supplied Sampled=1" is achievable for API Gateway paths (API Gateway makes its own sampling decision when tracing is enabled) but NOT achievable for Lambda Function URL paths. Lambda Function URLs honor the incoming `Sampled=1` header from the client with no override mechanism — no WAF header-rewrite, no intermediary tracing layer, no server-side sampling override. **FR-035 is hereby SCOPED**: (a) For the API Gateway endpoint (Dashboard Lambda only — the sole API Gateway-fronted Lambda): FR-035 is satisfied by API Gateway's built-in tracing integration. Note: Ingestion (EventBridge), Analysis (SNS), Notification (EventBridge+SNS), and Metrics (EventBridge) are NOT API Gateway-fronted — they are event-driven root-span Lambdas governed by centralized sampling rules. (b) For the SSE Lambda Function URL: the system MUST mitigate client-forced sampling via application-level defense — the SSE Lambda's OTel `parentbased_always_on` sampler (FR-056) respects the parent context's `Sampled` flag, but the Lambda runtime has already created the facade segment; mitigation is limited to cost monitoring (FR-038) and Function URL throttling configuration. The risk is acknowledged: at current traffic levels (<1M/month), worst-case forced sampling costs <$5/month; at scale, Function URL throttling limits concurrent connections. Source: API Gateway X-Ray integration documentation — API Gateway makes independent sampling decisions; Lambda Function URL documentation — no X-Ray sampling override mechanism.

**ADOT Collector Config Environment Variable (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-095**: The SSE Lambda's Terraform configuration MUST set the `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` environment variable to `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml`. Without this environment variable, the ADOT Extension ignores the custom configuration file placed by FR-069 and uses its compiled-in embedded default. The embedded default includes the decouple processor (safe) but also includes unnecessary components (gRPC receiver on port 4317, potentially metrics pipeline) that consume approximately 15MB of additional memory without value. The custom config (FR-064/FR-090) strips these components and specifies the explicit `[decouple, batch]` pipeline ordering. This FR ties together FR-064 (custom config specification), FR-069 (file placement in container), and FR-090 (decouple processor requirement) with the Terraform configuration that activates the file. Source: ADOT Lambda Extension — configuration file path is read exclusively from the `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` environment variable; no filesystem auto-discovery.

**Canary Invocation Interval and Architecture (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-096**: The observability canary (FR-019/FR-049) MUST run on a 5-minute invocation interval via EventBridge (CloudWatch Events) scheduled rule. The 5-minute interval balances detection latency (10 minutes worst-case per FR-020's 2-consecutive-interval alarm) with cost efficiency (~8,640 invocations/month). The canary MUST use a two-phase architecture for CloudWatch metric health checks (FR-049): each invocation (a) emits a test metric to CloudWatch AND (b) queries for the PREVIOUS invocation's test metric (emitted 5 minutes ago, well beyond the 60-120 second ingestion delay). This eliminates the need for long Lambda timeouts waiting for CloudWatch ingestion within a single invocation. The canary Lambda timeout MUST be set to 60 seconds (sufficient for X-Ray trace query retry at 30s per FR-078, plus CloudWatch API calls). The canary MUST persist state (previous invocation's test metric identifier) in an SSM Parameter Store parameter — NOT in DynamoDB (canary must not depend on application infrastructure per FR-051's isolation principle). Source: AWS Well-Architected Reliability Pillar — monitoring systems should have minimal dependencies on the systems they monitor.

**FR-043 Amendment: Metric Namespace and Dimensions (Round 11 — Amends FR-043)**

- **FR-097**: FR-043's 6 silent failure CloudWatch metrics MUST use the unified namespace `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` with the following dimensions: `FunctionName` (the emitting Lambda function name) and `FailurePath` (one of: `circuit_breaker_load`, `circuit_breaker_save`, `audit_trail_persist`, `notification_publish`, `timeseries_fanout`, `self_healing_fetch`, `parallel_fetcher`). The unified namespace ensures all reliability metrics are queryable in a single CloudWatch namespace without cross-namespace correlation. The `FailurePath` dimension enables per-path alarming (FR-042) and aggregated reliability dashboards. Additionally, the `HighLatencyAlert` metric (FR-042) MUST use the namespace `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` — resolving the discrepancy between the audit's `SentimentAnalyzer/Ingestion` and Task 17's `SentimentAnalyzer/SSE` (the metric is emitted by the Ingestion Lambda but represents a system-level reliability signal). All existing custom metrics listed in FR-042 that currently use inconsistent namespaces SHOULD be migrated to `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` for consolidation.

**ADOT Export Failure CloudWatch Logs Monitoring (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-098**: The SSE Lambda's CloudWatch Log Group MUST have a metric filter matching the ADOT Extension's export failure log pattern: `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."`. The metric filter MUST emit a CloudWatch metric `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/ADOTExportFailure` with value 1 on each match. A CloudWatch alarm on this metric (threshold: >= 1 in any 5-minute period) provides per-invocation detection of the known span drop race condition (aws-otel-lambda#886). This complements FR-091 (BSP queue overflow detection at the SDK level) and FR-019/FR-036 (canary aggregate detection) by catching span loss at the ADOT Extension level — the "second hop" in the two-hop flush architecture (FR-074). The metric filter pattern MUST also capture the preceding log line containing `"context canceled"` to distinguish Extension shutdown races from other export failures. Source: aws-otel-lambda#886 error pattern: `"context canceled"` followed by `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."`.

**Frontend SSE TextDecoder Streaming Mode (Round 11 — New)**

- **FR-099**: The frontend SSE client (FR-032/FR-089) MUST instantiate `TextDecoder` with the `{stream: true}` option when decoding ReadableStream chunks. Without `stream: true`, the decoder treats each chunk independently, replacing incomplete multi-byte UTF-8 sequences at chunk boundaries with U+FFFD (replacement character). SSE event data may contain non-ASCII characters (article titles, sentiment analysis text with international content). The `stream: true` option retains incomplete byte sequences between `decode()` calls, correctly reconstructing multi-byte characters that span chunk boundaries. This is a one-line configuration change (`new TextDecoder('utf-8', {stream: true})`) with significant correctness implications. Source: WHATWG Encoding Standard — TextDecoder `stream` option: "If true, the decoder will not flush its internal state on each decode() call."

**Post-Proactive-Flush Graceful Termination (Round 12 — New)**

- **FR-100**: After FR-093's proactive `force_flush()` fires (remaining time < 3000ms), the streaming generator MUST yield an `event: deadline\ndata: {"reason": "timeout_imminent", "remaining_ms": <value>}\n\n` SSE event and then terminate normally (return from the generator function). This converts a potential Lambda timeout (runtime SIGKILL, no `finally` blocks) into a graceful Lambda completion (handler returns, ADOT Extension receives NORMAL Shutdown with `shutdownReason: "spindown"`). The ADOT Extension's 2000ms Shutdown phase then exports all buffered spans reliably. Without FR-100, the generator continues creating spans after proactive flush — these post-flush spans are either (a) exported in the next BSP batch interval if time allows, or (b) permanently lost when the runtime is SIGKILL'd at timeout. The frontend client (FR-032) MUST handle `event: deadline` by immediately reconnecting to a fresh invocation via the existing reconnection logic (FR-033), using short delay (not exponential backoff) since this is a server-initiated graceful close per FR-083. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — Shutdown event with `shutdownReason` reflects how the invocation ended; normal completion produces `"spindown"`, timeout produces `"timeout"`.

**OTel Python Package Version Pinning (Round 12 — New)**

- **FR-101**: OTel Python core packages (`opentelemetry-api`, `opentelemetry-sdk`, `opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http`) MUST be pinned to the same version using exact `==` specifier in the SSE Lambda's requirements file. AWS contrib packages (`opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray`, `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws`) MUST use floor pins with major version ceiling (e.g., `>=1.0.2,<2.0.0`). The OTel Python core SDK enforces lockstep `==` pins between packages internally (`opentelemetry-sdk` depends on `opentelemetry-api==<exact-version>`), so pip prevents version mismatches at install time. However, without explicit pins in requirements, different `pip install` runs on different dates resolve to different lockstep versions, making builds non-reproducible. The ADOT collector and OTel SDK communicate via OTLP v1 protocol, which has been stable since OTel proto 1.0.0 and is compatible with all ADOT Collector versions since v0.21.0. Source: PyPI package metadata — `opentelemetry-sdk` declares `opentelemetry-api==1.39.1` (exact pin); OTLP v1 proto path: `opentelemetry.proto.collector.trace.v1`.

**SSE Lambda Memory Allocation Increase (Round 12 — Amends Round 6 Assumption)**

- **FR-102**: The SSE Lambda memory allocation MUST be increased from 512MB to 1024MB. Justification: (a) ADOT Extension resident memory: ~50MB, (b) OTel SDK packages import overhead: ~30MB, (c) Python 3.13 runtime: ~100MB, (d) application code + dependencies: ~100-150MB, (e) BSP queue (1500 spans): ~15MB, (f) DynamoDB response buffers: variable. Total baseline: ~350-400MB, leaving only ~110-160MB headroom at 512MB — insufficient for burst allocations during concurrent DynamoDB responses. At 1024MB: ~624-674MB headroom, and Lambda CPU doubles (CPU scales linearly with memory), reducing cold start from ~1200ms to ~800ms. Monthly cost increase: ~$2-3 at current invocation patterns (well within FR-038's $10 alarm threshold). This amends the Round 6 assumption that "512MB provides sufficient headroom." Source: AWS Lambda pricing — $0.0000166667/GB-second; Lambda CPU allocation documentation.

**Bootstrap Deadline Propagation (Round 12 — New, Prerequisite for FR-093)**

- **FR-103**: The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap MUST read the `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms` header from the Runtime API `/runtime/invocation/next` response and make the deadline timestamp accessible to the handler. The deadline value (milliseconds since Unix epoch) MUST be passed either (a) as a `deadline_ms` key in the event data dictionary, or (b) as an environment variable `_LAMBDA_DEADLINE_MS` set before handler invocation. The handler (or streaming generator) computes remaining time as `deadline_ms - current_time_ms`. The standard `context.get_remaining_time_in_millis()` API is unavailable because the bootstrap currently passes `None` for the Lambda context parameter. Without FR-103, FR-093 (proactive deadline-aware flush) is UNIMPLEMENTABLE — the handler has no way to know the execution deadline. Confirmed by code inspection: `src/lambdas/sse_streaming/bootstrap` line 157 calls `handler(event_data, None)`. Source: AWS Lambda Runtime API — `/runtime/invocation/next` response headers include `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms`.

**Lambda Memory Utilization Alarms (Round 12 — New)**

- **FR-104**: All 6 Lambda functions MUST have CloudWatch memory utilization alarms at 85% of configured memory. The alarm monitors memory usage via CloudWatch Logs metric filter on Lambda `REPORT` log lines (which include `Max Memory Used: <N> MB`). At 85% threshold on 1024MB (SSE Lambda per FR-102), the alarm fires at ~870MB utilization, providing ~154MB headroom warning before OOM. For other Lambdas at their current memory allocations, the threshold is proportional. This is critical for the SSE Lambda where ADOT Extension + OTel SDK consume ~80MB (8% of 1024MB) of the allocation, and DynamoDB polling with large response payloads can cause memory spikes during streaming. Source: AWS Lambda Monitoring documentation — `REPORT` log line format includes `Max Memory Used`.

**FR-098 Amendment: Metric Filter Pattern Completeness (Round 12 — Amends FR-098)**

- **FR-105**: FR-098's CloudWatch Logs metric filter MUST match BOTH ADOT export failure log variants: (a) `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."` (permanent failure or context canceled per aws-otel-lambda#886), and (b) `"Exporting failed. No more retries left. Dropping data."` (retries exhausted). The metric filter pattern MUST be: `"Exporting failed" "Dropping data"` (substring match catching both variants). The original FR-098 pattern `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."` misses the retries-exhausted variant. Both variants are at ERROR log level and include structured fields: `error` (the underlying error string), `dropped_items` (count of lost spans), `data_type` ("traces"). These patterns originate from the upstream OTel Collector `exporterhelper` package (`exporter/exporterhelper/internal/retry_sender.go`) and have been stable since OTel Collector v0.67 (2022). Source: `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-collector` source code — `retry_sender.go` lines ~80-110.

**OTel SDK Initialization Error Attribution (Round 12 — New)**

- **FR-106**: OTel SDK initialization code on the SSE Lambda MUST be wrapped in a try/except block that catches initialization failures, logs a structured error with explicit details (failing component name, specific configuration error, corrective action), and then re-raises the exception. This does NOT violate FR-018's fail-fast principle — the error still propagates unhandled to the Lambda runtime, crashing the function. The purpose is error ATTRIBUTION, not error suppression. Without FR-106, a missing `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME` environment variable produces a generic Python ImportError or AttributeError traceback that does not help operators identify the root cause. The structured error log MUST include: (a) component: e.g., `"TracerProvider"`, `"AwsLambdaResourceDetector"`, `"AwsXRayLambdaPropagator"`, (b) error: the specific exception message, (c) action: e.g., `"Set OTEL_SERVICE_NAME environment variable in Terraform"`. Source: OTel Python SDK — initialization error surface is importlib and constructor exceptions.

**Deployment Ordering and Migration Safety (Round 13 — New)**

- **FR-107**: The 17 remediation tasks MUST be deployed in the following phase order: **Phase 1 (Foundation)**: Task 1 (IAM permissions) — benign if deployed before instrumentation, provides permissions needed by subsequent phases; **Phase 2 (Instrumentation)**: Tasks 2, 3, 4, 5, 13, 14 (Lambda tracing instrumentation) — can be deployed in any order within phase; **Phase 3 (Frontend)**: Task 15 (fetch() migration) — depends on Task 5 SSE ADOT for trace header availability in responses; **Phase 4 (Logging Removal)**: Tasks 6, 7, 9 (remove latency logger, cache logger, correlation ID) — ONLY after Phase 2 is verified in production per FR-109's verification gates; **Phase 5 (Monitoring)**: Tasks 8, 10, 16, 17 (annotations, frontend headers, sampling, alarms) — can be deployed alongside Phase 2 or later; **Phase 6 (Validation)**: Tasks 11, 12 (canary, downstream audit) — ONLY after Phase 2 instrumentation is deployed and emitting traces. Deploying canary before instrumentation produces false-positive failures. Deploying logging removal before instrumentation verification creates a monitoring blind spot where neither old nor new observability is operational. Source: AWS X-Ray distributed tracing best practices — instrument upstream services before downstream consumers.

- **FR-108**: All Lambda functions instrumented with ADOT (SSE Lambda initially; others if migrated in future) MUST include `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=false` as an explicit Terraform environment variable. This provides an emergency kill switch — setting to `true` disables the OTel SDK's `TracerProvider` (returns no-op tracers) while the ADOT Extension continues running (consuming ~50MB but receiving zero spans and causing zero export errors). The kill switch enables operators to disable tracing without container rebuild or redeployment, using only a Terraform variable change + `terraform apply`. The `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` environment variable is part of the OTel specification and supported since `opentelemetry-python` v1.24.0. When disabled, zero spans are created, zero spans are exported, and zero tracing-related errors or performance overhead occurs. The Lambda continues functioning normally with no observability. Source: OTel Specification — Environment Variable `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED`.

- **FR-109**: Tasks 6 (remove latency_logger), 7 (remove cache_logger), and 9 (remove correlation ID) MUST NOT be deployed until the replacement X-Ray tracing (Tasks 2-5) has been verified in production for a minimum of 2 weeks with ALL of the following verification gates passing continuously: (a) canary (Task 11) reports healthy for 14 consecutive days with zero alarm transitions, (b) X-Ray service map shows all 6 Lambda nodes with correct service names (zero `unknown_service` nodes), (c) CloudWatch `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/ADOTExportFailure` metric emits zero events for 14 consecutive days, (d) at least 100 end-to-end traces have been manually spot-checked in X-Ray console confirming complete trace propagation. If any gate fails during the dual-emit period, logging removal is blocked until the failure is resolved and the 2-week verification clock resets. During the dual-emit period, both the old logging system and new X-Ray tracing emit simultaneously — the old system provides safety net observability while the new system is validated. Source: Observability migration best practices — dual-emit with verification gates.

- **FR-110**: The SSE Lambda's ECR repository MUST maintain a tagged pre-ADOT container image (`pre-adot-baseline`) alongside the ADOT-instrumented production image. This image is the current production image WITHOUT ADOT Extension binary, WITHOUT OTel SDK packages, WITHOUT `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` env var, and WITHOUT `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` env var. The pre-ADOT image enables rapid rollback via Terraform `image_uri` change + `terraform apply` (~2 minutes) without triggering a CI/CD container build pipeline during an active incident. The image MUST be tagged (not digest-only) for human readability, MUST be excluded from ECR lifecycle policies that remove old images, and MUST be retained for at least 90 days after FR-109's verification gates pass and logging removal is deployed. Source: Container deployment rollback best practices — maintain known-good baseline images.

- **FR-111**: All X-Ray Groups created for this feature (error/fault filter per FR-039, any additional filter groups) MUST be configured with `insights_configuration { insights_enabled = true }` in the Terraform `aws_xray_group` resource. Without `insights_enabled`, X-Ray Groups function only as query-time filters — they do NOT emit CloudWatch metrics. SC-013 requires "an X-Ray Group with error/fault filter generates CloudWatch metrics for errored traces," which is impossible without `insights_enabled = true`. Enabling Insights on Groups incurs no additional cost for basic Group-derived CloudWatch metrics (fault count, error count, response time percentiles). AWS imposes a limit of 25 X-Ray Groups per region; this feature requires 1-2 Groups, well within the limit. Source: AWS X-Ray Groups documentation — `InsightsConfiguration` parameter controls CloudWatch metric emission; `aws_xray_group` Terraform resource.

- **FR-112**: The Terraform configuration for the observability canary's EventBridge scheduled rule MUST include an explicit `depends_on` reference to the `aws_lambda_permission` resource that grants EventBridge invoke permission on the canary Lambda function. EventBridge rules become active immediately upon creation and can fire before the Lambda permission resource is created by Terraform, causing the first canary invocation to fail with `AccessDeniedException`. Without `depends_on`, the resource creation order within a single `terraform apply` is non-deterministic. The `depends_on` ensures the permission exists before the rule becomes active. Source: AWS EventBridge documentation — rules are active immediately upon creation; Terraform `depends_on` meta-argument for explicit ordering.

- **FR-113**: The observability canary MUST emit a `canary.trace.completeness_ratio` CloudWatch metric on each invocation that compares the cumulative count of successfully verified test traces against test traces submitted within a configurable lookback window (default: 1 hour, covering 12 canary invocations at 5-minute intervals). The ratio is calculated as `verified_traces / submitted_traces`. A CloudWatch alarm triggers when the ratio drops below 0.95 (95%) over the lookback window. This metric complements the per-trace IsPartial check (FR-087): IsPartial detects individual incomplete traces, while completeness_ratio detects systemic trace loss where entire traces are missing (e.g., ADOT Extension consistently dropping spans due to aws-otel-lambda#886 race, or X-Ray `PutTraceSegments` throttling). The metric uses namespace `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` with dimension `Component=Canary`. Source: Observability canary design patterns — aggregate completeness ratio alongside per-invocation point checks.

**OTLP Exporter Timeout Cap (Round 14 — New, Amends FR-093 Prerequisite Chain)**

- **FR-114**: The SSE Lambda's Terraform environment variables MUST include `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT=2` (2 seconds). This caps the OTel OTLP HTTP exporter's per-request timeout when sending spans to the ADOT Extension's localhost OTLP receiver. Without this cap, the exporter uses a 10-second default timeout with up to 6 retries per HTTP POST. If the ADOT Extension crashes or hangs, `force_flush()` blocks for up to 60s per batch. With ceil(1500/64)=24 batches at max queue capacity, total block time can reach ~24 minutes — catastrophically exceeding FR-093's 3000ms pre-deadline window. At 2-second timeout, worst-case per-batch failure is ~12s (2s×6 retries), but localhost Connection Refused detection is immediate, so realistic worst-case is ~15 seconds total. The Lambda is SIGKILL'd at timeout and the Extension's 2000ms Shutdown phase exports whatever was received. Under normal operation (ADOT healthy), localhost round-trip is sub-millisecond — the 2-second cap has zero performance impact. Source: OTel Specification — `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT`; OTel Python SDK issue #4568 (force_flush timeout not enforced); OTLP HTTP exporter `DEFAULT_TIMEOUT`.

**SSE Event-Level Trace Correlation (Round 14 — New)**

- **FR-115**: Each SSE event emitted by the SSE Lambda during streaming MUST include a `trace_id` field in the JSON `data:` payload containing the X-Ray-format trace ID of the OTel span that produced the event (the `sse_event_dispatch` span from FR-001). This enables operators to trace a specific received sentiment event from the frontend all the way back to the DynamoDB poll and metric emission that generated it. The trace ID MUST be in X-Ray format (`1-{hex_timestamp}-{24_hex_digits}`), not OTel hex format, so operators can paste it directly into the X-Ray console. Bandwidth impact: ~50 bytes per event on ~500-byte JSON payloads. The frontend client SHOULD log received `trace_id` values at debug level for client-side debugging. This closes the audit Section 6 finding: "SSE events to client — Trace IDs not included in SSE event payloads." Source: Audit Section 6 — End-to-End Latency Tracing gap analysis.

**ADOT Collector Config CI Validation (Round 14 — New)**

- **FR-116**: The SSE Lambda's ADOT collector configuration file MUST be validated in CI before Docker image build using the ADOT-specific collector binary's `validate` subcommand. The validation MUST use the ADOT distribution binary (NOT `otelcol` or `otelcol-contrib`, which bundle different component sets and report false errors on ADOT-specific components like `awsxray` exporter). CI validation catches: (a) malformed YAML syntax, (b) unknown receiver/processor/exporter types, (c) invalid pipeline wiring. CI step: `docker run --rm -v $(pwd)/collector-config.yaml:/etc/otel-config.yaml public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/aws-otel-collector:<pinned-version> --config /etc/otel-config.yaml validate`. A `yamllint` step provides additional fast-fail on YAML syntax. Without CI validation, a malformed collector config silently crashes the ADOT Extension on deployment — Lambda invocations proceed without telemetry until the canary detects trace absence (~10 minutes). Source: OTel Collector `validate` subcommand; ADOT component registry.

**Dual-Emit Verification Gate Formalization (Round 14 — Amends FR-109)**

- **FR-117**: FR-109's four verification gates MUST be formalized as executable checks: **(a) Trace Structure Equivalence**: For each Lambda, compare traces from old instrumentation (Powertools/X-Ray SDK) with new instrumentation (OTel/ADOT) for the same request type. Verify all expected spans present, error/fault annotations match, and business annotations (FR-006 through FR-009) appear. Comparison is SEMANTIC (same operations and annotations), NOT structural (segment document format differs between X-Ray SDK and ADOT). **(b) Annotation Parity**: Export distinct annotation keys from X-Ray traces before and after migration; "after" set must be a superset of "before." **(c) Service Map Accuracy**: Verify X-Ray service map shows all 6 Lambda nodes with correct `service.name`, all downstream connections (DynamoDB, SNS, SendGrid), and correct edge types. **(d) Automated Trace Spot-Check**: Script queries 100 most recent traces via `GetTraceSummaries`/`BatchGetTraces` and validates: (i) expected segment count per request type, (ii) no unexpected error/fault flags vs pre-migration, (iii) e2e latency p99 not regressed >20%. Script runs daily during the 2-week verification period with results logged to S3. Source: X-Ray API — GetTraceSummaries, BatchGetTraces.

**ReadableStream Error Classification and Server Sentinel (Round 14 — New, Amends FR-033/FR-083)**

- **FR-118**: The frontend SSE client MUST classify ReadableStream errors into 4 categories with distinct reconnection strategies: **(a) Graceful server close** (`done: true` preceded by `event: done` sentinel in buffer): reconnect immediately with `Last-Event-ID`, no backoff, log INFO; **(b) Abnormal termination** (`done: true` WITHOUT sentinel): reconnect with short delay (1-3s), log WARN, track consecutive occurrences; **(c) Network error** (TypeError from `reader.read()`): exponential backoff (1s, 2s, 4s, 8s... capped 30s with jitter), log ERROR; **(d) Intentional cancellation** (AbortError from `AbortController.abort()`): do NOT reconnect. The SSE Lambda MUST emit `event: done\ndata: {}\n\n` before every intentional close (including after FR-100's `event: deadline` — sequence: yield `event: deadline`, yield `event: done`, return). `TimeoutError` from `AbortSignal.timeout()` is treated as category (c). Source: WHATWG Fetch Standard — TypeError; DOM spec — AbortError/TimeoutError; Streams Standard §4.2.3.

**CORS Preflight Cache for Trace Headers (Round 14 — New, Amends FR-014/FR-016)**

- **FR-119**: All API Gateway and Lambda Function URL CORS configurations that include `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` in `Access-Control-Allow-Headers` MUST also set `Access-Control-Max-Age: 7200` (Chrome maximum; Firefox allows 86400). This caches CORS preflight responses, eliminating the 50-200ms OPTIONS request latency on subsequent requests. Without `Access-Control-Max-Age`, browser default is 5 seconds — virtually every API call incurs preflight. Safari caps at 600s (10 minutes) — acceptable, not worth workaround. CloudWatch RUM does NOT inject `X-Amzn-Trace-Id`; the header is added by application code (FR-015). Source: MDN Access-Control-Max-Age; Fetch Living Standard — CORS preflight cache.

**X-Ray Annotation Budget Allocation (Round 14 — New)**

- **FR-120**: OTel span instrumentation on the SSE Lambda MUST allocate annotation counts within the X-Ray 50-annotation-per-segment limit. Budget: `sse_event_dispatch` (FR-006: 5 + FR-007: 5 = 10), `dynamodb_poll` (FR-009: 4), `connection_acquire/release` (FR-008: 3), `force_flush` (2), OTel semantic conventions (~5-10). Maximum per-span: ~25 of 50 limit. RESERVE: 10 annotations for diagnostic use. Non-indexed attributes (large strings, nested objects) MUST use OTel span attributes mapped to X-Ray metadata, NOT annotations. `aws.xray.annotations` attribute convention MUST NOT be used to force all attributes to annotations. Exceeding 50 silently drops excess with SDK WARNING log only. Source: X-Ray Segment Documents — 50 annotations per segment/subsegment.

**treat_missing_data Systematic Classification (Round 14 — New, Amends FR-045/Task 17)**

- **FR-121**: ALL CloudWatch alarms for this feature MUST use `treat_missing_data` per this classification: **(a) Canary/heartbeat** (FR-019, FR-036, FR-113): `"breaching"` — heartbeat absence IS the failure. **(b) Custom error metrics from metric filters** (FR-043, FR-098/FR-105, FR-123): `"breaching"` — emit only on error; silent log group = system dead. **(c) AWS-native Lambda metrics** (Lambda `Errors`, `Duration`): `"notBreaching"` — AWS publishes zero-value points during idle. **(d) Cost/billing** (FR-038): `"missing"` — billing has variable delay. **(e) Latency percentiles**: `"notBreaching"` or `"ignore"` — no traffic = no data is normal. **(f) Memory utilization** (FR-104): `"notBreaching"` — no invocations = no concern. Source: AWS CloudWatch Developer Guide; Well-Architected Reliability Pillar REL06-BP04.

**Rollback Operational Procedure (Round 14 — Amends FR-110)**

- **FR-122**: Rollback from ADOT instrumentation MUST follow this procedure: **(a) Trigger criteria** — ANY of: SSE Lambda cold start p99 > 3000ms for 3 consecutive 5-minute periods, error rate > 5% for 2 consecutive periods, memory > 90% for 3 consecutive periods, or canary completeness < 80% for 2 intervals. **(b) Immediate mitigation** — Set `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true` via Terraform apply (~2 minutes). **(c) Full rollback** (if kill switch insufficient) — Update Terraform `image_uri` to `pre-adot-baseline` and apply (~5 minutes). **(d) Post-rollback verification** — SSE Lambda error rate < 0.1%, cold start p99 < 1500ms, memory < 70%. **(e) Timeline** — Kill switch within 5 minutes; full image rollback within 15 minutes. **(f) Reset** — FR-109's dual-emit clock resets after any rollback. Source: Incident management best practices.

**ADOT Collector Startup Failure Metric Filter (Round 14 — New)**

- **FR-123**: The SSE Lambda's CloudWatch Log Group MUST have a metric filter matching ADOT collector startup failure patterns: `"failed to get config"`, `"cannot unmarshal"`, `"failed to build pipelines"`. The filter emits `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/ADOTCollectorStartupFailure` metric. This detects deployment-time config errors that crash the Extension on cold start. Without this filter, bad configs silently disable telemetry — canary detects in ~10 minutes, but this filter detects on first invocation with specific attribution. Complements FR-116 (CI validation) as defense-in-depth. Source: OTel Collector error log patterns; ADOT Extension CloudWatch logging.

- **FR-124** (P0 — CRITICAL): Every code path that catches an exception, logs it, but emits NO metric MUST emit a unified `SilentFailure/Count` CloudWatch metric with `FailurePath` dimension identifying the failure source. Five paths require instrumentation: circuit breaker state persistence, audit trail writes, notification delivery, self-healing item fetch, and time-series fanout partial writes. Each emission MUST include a structured log fallback line containing `metric_fallback: true` for CloudWatch Logs metric filter backup. Source: AWS Well-Architected OPS-08 (unified error metric with dimensions).
- **FR-125** (P0 — CRITICAL): A CloudWatch Logs metric filter MUST exist on each Lambda's log group matching `{ $.metric_fallback = true }` to generate a backup `MetricEmissionFailback/Count` metric. This out-of-band path detects put_metric_data failures without depending on put_metric_data itself. The Logs metric filter alarm MUST use `treat_missing_data = "breaching"`. Source: AWS Well-Architected REL-06, re:Invent 2023 OPS-301.
- **FR-126** (P1 — HIGH): The canary heartbeat metric (`EmissionHeartbeat`) MUST be appended to the SAME `put_metric_data` call as production metrics — not a separate API call. If production metric emission fails, the heartbeat fails with it, proving the emission pipeline is broken. The heartbeat alarm MUST use `treat_missing_data = "breaching"` with 3 consecutive evaluation periods of 60 seconds. Source: Amazon Builder's Library "Implementing health checks."
- **FR-127** (P1 — HIGH): Lambda error alarms MUST use percentage-based thresholds via CloudWatch math expressions: `IF(invocations > 10, (errors / invocations) * 100, 0)`. CRITICAL threshold: >5% error rate sustained for 2 periods. WARNING threshold: >1% error rate sustained for 3 periods. The minimum invocation guard (>10) prevents false positives at low traffic. Existing absolute-count alarms (>3/5min, >5/5min) MUST be replaced. Source: AWS Well-Architected OPS-06, AWS Observability Best Practices.
- **FR-128** (P1 — HIGH): Ingestion Lambda MUST have a latency alarm at P95 < 48,000ms (80% of 60s timeout). Notification Lambda MUST have a latency alarm at P95 < 24,000ms (80% of 30s timeout). SSE Streaming Lambda MUST have a P99 connection setup latency alarm < 5,000ms. Analysis Lambda alarm threshold MUST be recalibrated from 25,000ms (42%) to WARNING at 36,000ms (60%) and CRITICAL at 48,000ms (80%). Source: AWS Well-Architected PERF-04, Lambda Operator Guide.
- **FR-129** (P1 — HIGH): The CloudWatch dashboard MUST display ALL alarms organized into three severity-tiered widgets: (a) CRITICAL alarms (packaging failures, circuit breaker, DLQ depth, budget), (b) WARNING alarms (error rates, latency, collision rates), (c) INFORMATIONAL alarms (cost proxies, volume thresholds). A composite alarm aggregating all CRITICAL alarms MUST be created and displayed in the dashboard header. Alarm widgets MUST use alarm name prefix patterns, not explicit ARN lists, so new alarms are automatically included. Source: AWS CloudWatch Dashboard Best Practices, AWS Well-Architected OPS-08.
- **FR-130** (P2 — MEDIUM): SendGrid HTTP call tracing MUST be verified by confirming that `httplib` patching (X-Ray) or `URLLibInstrumentor` (OTel) captures the `python_http_client → urllib.request → http.client` call chain. An integration test MUST verify that a SendGrid API call produces a trace subsegment/span with the destination URL containing `api.sendgrid.com`. If auto-patching produces only generic `http.client` subsegments, a manual subsegment wrapper MUST be added with SendGrid-specific annotations (endpoint, response status). Source: X-Ray SDK supported libraries, python_http_client source.
- **FR-131** (P2 — MEDIUM): All CloudWatch alarms on application-emitted custom metrics MUST use `treat_missing_data = "missing"` (not `notBreaching`) to preserve INSUFFICIENT_DATA state during CloudWatch Metrics API degradation. Only alarms on AWS-native Lambda metrics (which AWS publishes) and cost/budget alarms may use `notBreaching`. Canary/heartbeat alarms MUST use `breaching`. Source: AWS CloudWatch docs "Configuring how alarms treat missing data."
- **FR-132** (P2 — MEDIUM): A validation check MUST exist that parses the HL remediation checklist task table and each fix-*.md work order file, comparing the FR sets assigned to each task. Any FR present in the HL table but absent from the corresponding work order file MUST be flagged as a synchronization gap. This check MUST run as part of the specification validation workflow. Source: IEEE 830 requirements traceability, ISO 29148.
- **FR-133** (P2 — MEDIUM): Collision rate alarm evaluation periods MUST be reduced: high collision alarm from 3 periods (15min) to 2 periods (10min), low collision alarm from 6 periods (30min) to 3 periods (15min). Error rate alarm thresholds on ingestion and analysis Lambdas MUST be converted from absolute count to percentage-based (FR-127). Source: AWS CloudWatch Alarms Best Practices.

**Silent Failure Alarm Configuration (Round 16 — New, Completes FR-124)**

- **FR-134** (P0 — CRITICAL): A CloudWatch alarm MUST exist on the `SilentFailure/Count` metric (FR-124) for EACH of the 7 `FailurePath` dimension values (FR-142). Alarm configuration: threshold > 0 for any single data point, evaluation period 1×1min, `treat_missing_data = "missing"` (per FR-131 — application-emitted metric). Alarm naming pattern: `{env}-silent-failure-{FailurePath}` for automatic inclusion in dashboard severity widgets (FR-129). An AGGREGATE composite alarm across all FailurePath-specific alarms MUST be created and included in the CRITICAL tier of FR-129's dashboard header. Without this FR, FR-124's metric is emitted but unwatched — the primary silent failure detection path has no alarm despite SC-019 expecting one. Source: AWS CloudWatch Alarms Best Practices; Well-Architected OPS-08.

**Frontend Trace Header Propagation Verification Gate (Round 16 — New, Amends FR-015)**

- **FR-135** (P0 — CRITICAL): A deployment Phase 3 (FR-107 — Frontend) blocking gate MUST verify that `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` headers are present on ALL outbound `fetch()` requests from the browser to: (a) API Gateway endpoints (same-origin), (b) Lambda Function URL SSE endpoint (cross-origin, `fetch()+ReadableStream` from FR-033), (c) any other cross-origin API endpoints. The verification test MUST use Playwright request interception (`page.on('request')`) to inspect outbound headers and confirm valid X-Ray trace ID format. CloudWatch RUM's `FetchPlugin` injects the header pre-fetch via argument mutation and does NOT interfere with ReadableStream response processing (confirmed by source inspection). However, injection depends on: (1) `addXRayTraceIdHeader: true` being configured, (2) the target URL passing RUM's `isUrlAllowed()` filter, (3) CORS `Access-Control-Allow-Headers` including `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` on the target server (FR-014/FR-082/FR-119). If ANY of these prerequisites fails, RUM silently drops the header. The gate MUST test with actual browser requests, not unit-level mocks. No silent fallback — if header injection fails, the gate MUST block deployment and require remediation. Source: aws-rum-web SDK `FetchPlugin.ts` source; CloudWatch RUM Developer Guide — HTTP telemetry configuration.

**Canary Out-of-Band Alerting Channel Specification (Round 16 — New, Specifies FR-021/FR-050)**

- **FR-136** (P1 — HIGH): The canary's out-of-band alerting channel (referenced by FR-021, FR-050, SC-021) MUST be a cross-region SNS topic in a DIFFERENT AWS region from the primary deployment. The canary Lambda calls `sns.publish()` directly to this cross-region topic (not via CloudWatch Alarms) when it detects: (a) X-Ray ingestion failure exceeding threshold, (b) CloudWatch metric emission pipeline failure (`EmissionHeartbeat` missing per FR-126), (c) canary self-execution failure. The SNS topic MUST have at least two subscription types: email distribution list AND webhook integration (PagerDuty, OpsGenie, or equivalent). The canary's IAM execution role MUST include `sns:Publish` permission for the cross-region topic ARN. This channel survives primary-region CloudWatch degradation because: SNS publish is a direct API call (no CloudWatch dependency), the topic is in a different region, and email/webhook delivery is independent of CloudWatch. Source: AWS Well-Architected REL-13 (multi-region monitoring); Amazon Builder's Library "Implementing health checks."

**SNS Trace Propagation Verification Gate (Round 16 — New)**

- **FR-137** (P1 — HIGH): A deployment Phase 2 (FR-107 — Instrumentation) blocking gate MUST verify that X-Ray trace context propagates through SNS from the Ingestion Lambda to the Analysis Lambda. The test: (a) trigger an ingestion event that publishes to SNS, (b) capture the Ingestion Lambda's trace ID, (c) wait with retry-and-backoff (30s then 60s, per X-Ray's eventual consistency), (d) query X-Ray `BatchGetTraces` for the trace ID, (e) confirm BOTH Lambda segments AND the SNS connecting segment appear. Critical prerequisite: the SNS subscription MUST NOT use `rawMessageDelivery: true`, which strips the `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute and breaks propagation. The gate MUST also verify `rawMessageDelivery` is `false` on all Ingestion→Analysis SNS subscriptions via `sns:GetSubscriptionAttributes`. This verification exists because 9 prior assumptions in this spec were invalidated — automatic SNS propagation is too critical to leave unverified. Source: AWS X-Ray Developer Guide — "Tracing SNS event notifications"; SNS Developer Guide — System attributes and raw message delivery.

**API Gateway and Function URL Latency Alarms (Round 16 — New)**

- **FR-138** (P1 — HIGH): The API Gateway-fronted Dashboard Lambda MUST have CloudWatch alarms on API Gateway's `IntegrationLatency` metric at P99 < 5,000ms and on `5XXError` rate at >1% sustained for 2 periods. The SSE Streaming Lambda (Function URL, not API Gateway) MUST have equivalent alarms on Lambda service metrics `Url5xxError`. API Gateway alarms capture the full request lifecycle including authorization, WAF evaluation, and integration latency that Lambda-side duration alarms (FR-128) cannot measure. Ingestion (EventBridge), Analysis (SNS), Notification (EventBridge+SNS), and Metrics (EventBridge) are event-driven Lambdas with no HTTP interface — they are covered by Lambda-native metrics only. All alarms use `treat_missing_data = "notBreaching"` per FR-121 classification (AWS-native metrics). Source: AWS API Gateway CloudWatch Metrics documentation; Lambda Function URL metrics; Well-Architected PERF-04.
