**force_flush() Hard Timeout Wrapper (Round 16 — New, Amends FR-093)**

- **FR-139** (P1 — HIGH): The SSE Lambda's `force_flush()` call (FR-055, FR-093) MUST be wrapped in a thread-based hard timeout of 2,500ms, leaving 500ms from FR-093's 3,000ms deadline window for generator termination (`event: deadline` + `event: done` + return). The wrapper spawns a daemon thread for `force_flush()`, calls `thread.join(timeout=2.5)`, and proceeds regardless of completion. This bounds total flush duration even when the ADOT Extension is hung (accepting TCP connections but not responding to OTLP requests). Without this wrapper, `BatchSpanProcessor.force_flush()` exports 22 batches sequentially (FR-073 `max_queue_size=1350` ÷ `max_export_batch_size=64`), each blocking up to FR-114's 2s per-request OTLP timeout = 44s total — far exceeding FR-093's 3,000ms budget and causing Lambda timeout instead of graceful `event: deadline` termination. SC-064 MUST be amended to also test the hung-Extension scenario (TCP accept, no response), not just port-unreachable. Spans in unflushed batches are LOST (acceptable — fail fast, NO FALLBACKS). Source: OTel Python SDK `force_flush()` timeout non-enforcement — opentelemetry-python#4568 (open); `BatchSpanProcessor` sequential export implementation; Python `threading.Thread.join(timeout)` documentation.

**ADOT Extension Mid-Stream Crash Detection (Round 16 — New)**

- **FR-140** (P1 — HIGH): The SSE Lambda MUST emit a `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/ADOTExtensionUnavailable` CloudWatch metric when the OTLP exporter fails to deliver spans to `localhost:4318` during streaming. Detection: a CloudWatch Logs metric filter on the SSE Lambda log group matching the OTel SDK's exporter WARNING log patterns for connection failure (`"Failed to export"`, `"Connection refused"`, `"Connection reset"`). This provides per-invocation detection within the CloudWatch Logs pipeline latency (~seconds), complementing FR-123's startup failure detection and the canary's aggregate detection (~10 minutes, 2× FR-048 interval). The metric alarm MUST use `treat_missing_data = "missing"` (normal operation produces no metric). When this alarm fires simultaneously with FR-123's startup alarm, it indicates a persistent ADOT configuration problem; when it fires alone, it indicates a mid-stream Extension crash (OOM, collector pipeline failure). Source: OTel Specification — Exporters MUST NOT throw exceptions; ADOT Lambda Extension lifecycle documentation.

**SSE Reconnection Trace Chain Group (Round 16 — New)**

- **FR-141** (P2 — MEDIUM): An X-Ray Group named `sse-reconnections` MUST be created with filter expression `annotation.previous_trace_id BEGINSWITH "1-"` to capture all SSE reconnection events, with `insights_enabled = true` (FR-061 pattern) to generate CloudWatch metrics for system-wide reconnection frequency. An alarm on reconnection rate > 10/minute indicates SSE Lambda instability. The operator workflow for session-level debugging: (1) find initial trace by user/time, (2) extract `session_id` from annotation (FR-008), (3) filter X-Ray traces by `annotation.session_id = "{value}"`, (4) sort results by timestamp to see the full reconnection chain with `previous_trace_id` links. Each reconnection creates a NEW trace ID (new Lambda invocation = new X-Ray facade segment); the `session_id` annotation is the join key across traces. The `previous_trace_id` annotation MUST be set on ALL SSE connections — on first connection, the value is `"none"` (not omitted) to ensure the annotation exists for all traces. Source: AWS X-Ray Groups documentation; X-Ray Filter Expression reference.

**FR-124 Path Enumeration Alignment (Round 16 — Amends FR-124)**

- **FR-142** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-124's `FailurePath` dimension MUST enumerate exactly 7 distinct values matching SC-004's 7 silent failure paths: `circuit_breaker_load`, `circuit_breaker_save`, `audit_trail`, `notification_delivery`, `self_healing_fetch`, `fanout_partial_write`, `parallel_fetcher_aggregate`. FR-124's current text lists "five paths" with "circuit breaker state persistence" (ambiguous — could be load or save or both) and omits parallel fetcher error aggregation entirely (audit Section 8.7, SC-004 item 7). This amendment ensures FR-124 satisfies SC-004 without interpretation ambiguity. Source: SC-004 (7 paths enumerated); audit Section 8.7.

**Metric Fallback Log Line Format Specification (Round 16 — Amends FR-124)**

- **FR-143** (P2 — MEDIUM): The structured log fallback line required by FR-124 MUST be a single JSON-formatted log line matching the exact structure: `{"metric_fallback": true, "failure_path": "<path>", "metric_name": "SilentFailure/Count", "exception_type": "<type>", "exception_message": "<truncated_to_256_chars>", "timestamp": "<ISO8601>"}`. This line MUST be emitted via a dedicated JSON-emitting call (e.g., `json.dumps()` to stdout or `logging.getLogger().info(json.dumps(...))`), NOT the Lambda's default logging format (which may be plaintext). FR-125's CloudWatch Logs metric filter pattern `{ $.metric_fallback = true }` requires JSON-structured log events — plaintext lines containing the literal string "metric_fallback: true" do NOT match JSON metric filter syntax. Each Lambda MAY use any logging format for all other log lines; only the metric_fallback line requires JSON. Source: CloudWatch Logs Metric Filter pattern syntax — JSON patterns require JSON-formatted log events.

**OTel Manual Span Error Status Requirement (Round 17 — New)**

- **FR-144** (P0 — CRITICAL): ALL manually-created OTel spans on the SSE Lambda MUST call BOTH `span.set_status(StatusCode.ERROR, description)` AND `span.record_exception(exception)` when an exception occurs within the span's scope. The ADOT X-Ray exporter's `makeCause()` function is GATED on `span.Status().Code() == StatusCodeError` — without `set_status(StatusCode.ERROR)`, the X-Ray segment document has `fault: false` and `cause: null`, regardless of whether `record_exception()` was called. This means: (a) X-Ray Group filter expressions `fault = true OR error = true` (FR-034) MISS the error, (b) X-Ray console error/fault filtering (SC-002) MISSES the error, (c) CloudWatch metrics generated from X-Ray Groups do NOT count the error, (d) the operator sees a "healthy" trace for a failed operation. Exception: HTTP-attributed spans (with `http.status_code` >= 400) are mapped to X-Ray error/fault via separate attribute-based logic independent of StatusCode — but manual internal/DynamoDB spans have no HTTP status code fallback. For non-streaming Lambdas, Powertools Tracer `@tracer.capture_method` automatically calls the equivalent of `set_status(ERROR)` on exception (FR-029 handles this). For the SSE Lambda's ~675 manual spans per invocation, EVERY error path MUST explicitly set both. This is the most fundamental requirement for X-Ray error visibility on the SSE Lambda. Source: ADOT X-Ray Exporter `cause.go` — `makeCause()` gated on `StatusCodeError`; OTel Specification — Span API SetStatus; `segment.go` — `fault` flag mapping.

**Canary FR-018 Fail-Fast Exemption (Round 17 — New)**

- **FR-145** (P1 — HIGH): The canary Lambda (Task 11) MUST catch and handle X-Ray SDK, OTel SDK, and ADOT Extension initialization errors WITHOUT crashing. This is the SOLE FORMALIZED exemption from FR-018's fail-fast mandate. Rationale: the canary's purpose is to detect and report X-Ray outages — if the canary itself crashes on X-Ray initialization failure, the entire meta-observability architecture (FR-125, FR-126, FR-136) becomes inoperative. The system loses its ability to detect X-Ray degradation, which is the single most critical gap this spec exists to prevent. The canary MUST: (a) attempt normal X-Ray/OTel initialization, (b) on initialization failure, log a structured error with `{"canary_init_failed": true, "component": "<failed_component>", "error": "<message>"}`, (c) continue executing its CloudWatch health check and SNS alerting functions, (d) report its own initialization failure as a critical finding alongside any X-Ray health findings, (e) emit a `CanaryInitFailure` CloudWatch metric for alarming. The canary's OWN traces are best-effort — visible when X-Ray is healthy, lost when X-Ray is down. Its critical alerting path (FR-136 cross-region SNS) MUST NOT depend on X-Ray. Source: AWS Well-Architected Operational Excellence Pillar — "Monitor the health of your monitoring systems."

**Canary Lambda Instrumentation Scope (Round 17 — New)**

- **FR-146** (P2 — MEDIUM): The canary Lambda (new function #7, not in FR-001's 6-Lambda scope) MUST be instrumented with the same approach as other non-streaming Lambdas (Powertools Tracer per FR-029 pattern). However, all instrumentation initialization MUST be wrapped per FR-145's exemption. FR-001's scope text ("all 6 Lambda functions") is NOT amended — the canary is architecturally distinct as a meta-observability component. The canary's instrumentation serves a different purpose than production Lambda instrumentation: it provides operator visibility into canary execution (useful for debugging canary failures) rather than end-user request tracing. When X-Ray is healthy, canary traces are visible alongside production traces. When X-Ray is down, canary traces are lost but canary alerting continues via FR-136.

**FR-124 Silent Failure Path Enumeration Correction (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-147** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-124's inline text MUST be amended from "five distinct silent failure paths" to "seven distinct silent failure paths" to match the authoritative enumeration in FR-142 and SC-092. The seven paths are: (1) `circuit_breaker_load`, (2) `circuit_breaker_save`, (3) `audit_trail`, (4) `notification_delivery`, (5) `self_healing_fetch`, (6) `fanout_partial_write`, (7) `parallel_fetcher_aggregate`. FR-124's original text bundled circuit breaker into one path and omitted parallel_fetcher_aggregate. FR-134 creates 7 alarms referencing these 7 FailurePath dimension values — an implementer following FR-124's unamended text creates 5 metrics, leaving 2 alarm ARNs referencing non-existent metrics (permanent INSUFFICIENT_DATA state on `circuit_breaker_save` and `parallel_fetcher_aggregate` alarms). This is a documentation-only amendment; no behavioral change. Source: FR-142 enumeration; SC-092 dimension list; FR-134 alarm definitions.

**Frontend RUM Readiness Gate (Round 18 — New)**

- **FR-148** (P0 — CRITICAL): The frontend application MUST NOT issue its first `fetch()` call to any instrumented backend endpoint (API Gateway or Lambda Function URL) until CloudWatch RUM's FetchPlugin has completed patching `window.fetch`. The application MUST implement a readiness check that confirms `window.fetch` has been wrapped by the FetchPlugin before initiating any backend communication, including the SSE streaming connection. If RUM initialization has not completed within 5 seconds of page load, the application MUST proceed without the readiness gate and log a structured warning (`{"rum_init_timeout": true, "delay_ms": 5000}`) — this is NOT a fallback (the application does not retry RUM initialization or use alternative tracing), it is a bounded wait to avoid blocking the user experience indefinitely. The 5-second bound is necessary because RUM CDN delivery can fail entirely (CDN outage, ad blocker, CSP policy), and the application must remain functional without RUM — trace headers will be absent but the application works. Detection mechanism: FR-135's Playwright deployment gate verifies the readiness gate exists. FR-085's Playwright SSE test verifies the SSE connection carries the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. Implementation note: The RUM web client SDK does not expose a native readiness event — the readiness check may need to poll for the presence of the `cwr` (CloudWatch RUM) global object or check `window.fetch.toString()` for evidence of shimmer wrapping. Source: aws-rum-web SDK `FetchPlugin.ts` — synchronous monkey-patching via shimmer; CDN snippet loading semantics.

**Post-Proactive-Flush Span Creation Prohibition (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-149** (P1 — HIGH): After FR-093's proactive flush fires (triggered at `get_remaining_time_in_millis() <= 3000`), the SSE streaming generator MUST NOT create any new OTel spans. All span-creating operations (poll cycle spans, DynamoDB call spans, event formatting spans) MUST be guarded by a `flush_fired` flag that is set atomically when the proactive flush begins. If an exception occurs after flush (e.g., during generator cleanup), the exception MUST be logged via structured JSON (same format as FR-143) but NOT recorded as an OTel span. The generator's final operations after flush MUST be limited to: (a) yielding `event: deadline\ndata: {"reason": "lambda_deadline"}\n\n` per FR-100, (b) returning from the generator function. This amendment closes the window between proactive flush and generator termination where orphaned spans could be created with no export path. Source: OTel Python SDK BatchSpanProcessor — no mechanism for "emergency re-flush" after queue re-population.

**OTel Error Handling Context Manager Pattern (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-150** (P1 — HIGH): FR-144's dual-call requirement (record_exception + set_status) MUST be implemented via OTel's `start_as_current_span()` context manager with `record_exception=True, set_status_on_exception=True` (the defaults since opentelemetry-python v0.16b0) for ALL spans where exceptions PROPAGATE out of the `with` block. For spans containing try/except blocks that CATCH exceptions without re-raising (i.e., the 7 silent failure paths per FR-142), the caught exception MUST be manually handled with BOTH `span.record_exception(exception)` AND `span.set_status(StatusCode.ERROR, str(exception))` INSIDE the except block BEFORE any other error handling (metric emission, logging, etc.). The context manager's automatic handling does NOT fire for caught exceptions — the `use_span()` internal implementation only calls `record_exception()` and `set_status(ERROR)` in its own except block, which is bypassed when the inner code catches the exception. This distinction is the root cause of FR-144's ambiguity: automatic handling is correct for unexpected errors, but the SSE Lambda's 7 silent failure paths are ALL caught exceptions by design (they must not crash the generator). Every silent failure path MUST have explicit dual-call as the FIRST two lines of its except block. Source: OTel Python SDK `opentelemetry/trace/__init__.py` — `use_span()` implementation; Python language reference — exception propagation in nested try/except.

**Canary Warm-Invocation TracerProvider Re-Initialization (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-151** (P1 — HIGH): The canary Lambda's handler function MUST check whether TracerProvider is in a valid state on EVERY invocation, not just cold starts. If module-level TracerProvider initialization failed (detected via FR-145's error handling), the handler MUST attempt re-initialization on each subsequent warm invocation. The re-initialization attempt MUST be: (a) guarded by a module-level flag (`_tracer_init_failed = True`), (b) bounded by a 2-second timeout to prevent blocking the canary's primary alerting function, (c) logged as `{"canary_reinit_attempt": true, "success": <bool>}` regardless of outcome. If re-initialization succeeds, the flag is cleared and subsequent invocations use normal instrumentation. If re-initialization fails again, the handler continues with FR-145's degraded mode. This prevents a transient ADOT Extension hiccup during one cold start from permanently disabling canary tracing for the execution environment's lifetime (potentially hours). Source: Python language semantics — module-level code executes once per process; Lambda execution model — warm invocations reuse the same process.

**FR-109/FR-117 Gate Precedence Clarification (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-152** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-109's verification gate (d) ("100 traces manually spot-checked for expected annotations") is SUPERSEDED by FR-117's automated trace validation script for deployment gate purposes. FR-109 gate (d) is reclassified as a one-time acceptance test during initial implementation, NOT a recurring deployment gate. FR-117's automated script is the authoritative recurring gate, executing on every deployment per FR-107 Phase 5. The automated script MUST define expected segment counts per request type: (a) Dashboard Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=3 DynamoDB subsegments + >=1 httplib subsegment (SendGrid path only), (b) Ingestion Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=1 DynamoDB subsegment + >=1 SNS subsegment, (c) Analysis Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=2 DynamoDB subsegments, (d) Notification Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=1 httplib subsegment, (e) SSE Streaming Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=5 subsegments (poll cycles vary), (f) Metrics Lambda: 1 Lambda segment + >=2 DynamoDB subsegments + >=1 CloudWatch subsegment. The expected counts are MINIMUMS — actual counts may be higher depending on code paths exercised. Source: Application architecture — Lambda function responsibilities and downstream dependencies.

**FR-018 Explicit Scope Statement (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-153** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-018's fail-fast mandate MUST include an explicit scope statement: "FR-018 applies to ALL Lambda functions in the system EXCEPT those explicitly exempted by a numbered FR. As of Round 18, the sole exemption is FR-145 (canary Lambda). Any future Lambda function added to the system MUST default to FR-018 fail-fast behavior. Exemptions require a new FR with documented rationale for why the Lambda must survive X-Ray initialization failure." This prevents scope ambiguity when new Lambda functions are added to the architecture — without this statement, an implementer could argue that FR-018 applies only to the original 6 Lambdas in FR-001, leaving new functions uninstrumented. Source: Spec architecture — FR-001 scope vs FR-145 exemption; defensive specification practice.

**FR-132 Automated Staleness Remediation Trigger (Round 18 — Amendment)**

- **FR-154** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-132's automated staleness detection MUST trigger a concrete remediation action, not merely log a warning. When the automated audit detects that the HL remediation checklist is stale (missing rounds, missing SCs, missing risk entries), the system MUST: (a) create a GitHub issue titled "HL Document Staleness: Missing Rounds {N}-{M}" with the specific gaps enumerated, (b) label the issue `doc-staleness` and `priority:high`, (c) block the next `/speckit.specify` round from proceeding until the issue is resolved or explicitly deferred with documented rationale. The current state of the HL document demonstrates that detection-only staleness tracking is insufficient — FR-132 exists in Round 15, yet the HL document is 2 rounds stale by Round 18 with 13 missing risk entries and 39 missing SCs. Detection without enforcement is equivalent to no detection. Source: Observed failure — FR-132 detection mechanism failed to prevent staleness accumulation over Rounds 16-18.

**Trace Data PII Prohibition (Round 18 — New)**

- **FR-155** (P2 — MEDIUM): X-Ray span annotations and metadata MUST NOT contain personally identifiable information (PII) including but not limited to: email addresses, user names, IP addresses, sentiment analysis input text, API keys, or authentication tokens. OTel span attributes that are mapped to X-Ray annotations (indexed, queryable) or metadata (non-indexed but stored) MUST be limited to: trace correlation identifiers (trace_id, session_id, request_id), operational metrics (latency, cache_hit_rate, queue_depth), categorical classifiers (event_type, failure_path, span_kind), and infrastructure identifiers (function_name, region). If a span attribute might contain user-generated content (e.g., error messages that include user input), the value MUST be truncated to a classification label (e.g., "ValueError" instead of "ValueError: invalid email user@example.com"). X-Ray trace data retention is 30 days (non-configurable). This FR does not affect CloudWatch Logs (which have separate data handling) or the application's functional data stores. Source: AWS Shared Responsibility Model — customer responsibility for data classification in trace stores; GDPR Article 5(1)(c) — data minimization principle.

**BSP Deadlock Diagnostic Differentiation (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-156** (P0 — CRITICAL): The SSE Lambda's `force_flush()` call path MUST be resilient to `BatchSpanProcessor` internal deadlock (opentelemetry-python#3886) AND MUST differentiate the failure cause diagnostically. FR-139's thread-based hard timeout wrapper handles both ADOT Extension hang (external — TCP accept, no OTLP response) and BSP deadlock (internal — worker thread holds `self.condition` lock indefinitely) identically: the flush call is terminated after 2500ms. However, the SPAN FATE differs: in Extension hang, spans were dequeued from BSP and held by the exporter (lost in exporter memory); in BSP deadlock, spans remain in the BSP deque with the lock unreleased (cannot be exported, retried, or recovered). The SSE Lambda MUST emit a structured log after FR-139 timeout that distinguishes the two cases: (a) if the OTLP TCP connection to localhost:4318 was established before timeout, log `{"flush_timeout_cause": "bsp_or_extension_hang", "otlp_connection": "established"}`; (b) if the OTLP TCP connection to localhost:4318 failed with ECONNREFUSED, log `{"flush_timeout_cause": "extension_unavailable", "otlp_connection": "refused"}`. This diagnostic distinction enables operators to differentiate Extension issues (solvable via restart/redeploy) from BSP bugs (solvable via SDK version upgrade or configuration change). This is the THIRD distinct span-loss vector in the spec: (1) Extension hang → FR-139 thread wrapper; (2) Extension drop → FR-074 accepted ~30% loss; (3) BSP deadlock → FR-156 diagnostic differentiation. Source: opentelemetry-python#3886 — `BatchSpanProcessor` deadlock bug; confirmed in Python 3.11+.

**FR-154 Retroactive Staleness Enforcement (Round 20 — Gate)**

- **FR-157** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-154's staleness enforcement gate MUST be retroactively applied as a Round 20 acceptance criterion. The HL remediation checklist (`docs/x-ray/HL-x-ray-remediation-checklist.md`) is 1 full round stale: (a) Progress Log ends at Round 17 — missing Round 18; (b) cumulative totals show 146 FRs / 96 SCs — actual is 155 FRs / 105 SCs (9 FRs and 9 SCs from Round 18 missing); (c) Work Order table task-to-FR mappings do not include Round 18 FRs (FR-147 through FR-155); (d) Risk Assessment table does not include Round 18 risk entries. Per FR-154(c), the next specification round cannot proceed until the staleness issue is resolved or explicitly deferred. This FR documents the explicit deferral with rationale: HL synchronization is deferred to a dedicated synchronization task (not a specification round) because (i) Round 20's primary purpose is blind spot discovery; (ii) HL synchronization requires updating 5 sections with 9 FRs, 9 SCs, 4 edge cases, 3 assumptions, and 1 Progress Log entry — mechanical work that should not consume specification analysis budget; (iii) a GitHub issue titled "HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18" MUST be created as part of Round 20 acceptance. The deferral is time-bounded: HL synchronization MUST be completed before implementation begins on any task (FR-107 Phase 0 prerequisite). Source: Observed failure — FR-132 (Round 15) detection and FR-154 (Round 18) enforcement both exist but the HL document they govern is stale through Round 20, proving specification-level enforcement without external tracking (GitHub issue) is insufficient.

**ADOT Cold Start Latency Budget (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-158** (P1 — HIGH): The SSE Lambda MUST have a measured and documented cold start latency budget that accounts for ADOT Extension overhead. AWS publishes NO official benchmarks for ADOT Lambda Extension cold start impact (confirmed: opentelemetry-lambda#263 states "we currently do not publish expected startup times"). Community reports range from 200ms to 2000ms+ depending on memory allocation and runtime configuration. FR-102 increased SSE Lambda memory to 1024MB based on memory calculations but established no latency constraint. The cold start latency budget MUST be: (a) measured in preprod with the ADOT-embedded Docker image at 1024MB memory; (b) documented as a P95 threshold of < 2000ms for cold start (handler invocation latency, excluding Extension INIT which runs concurrently per Lambda lifecycle); (c) verified as a Phase 1 deployment gate in FR-107's ordering; (d) re-measured when ADOT version, OTel SDK version, or Lambda memory allocation changes. If measured cold start exceeds 2000ms, memory allocation MUST be increased until the budget is met, or an architectural review determines an alternative approach (e.g., provisioned concurrency). This FR does NOT mandate provisioned concurrency as a default — it mandates replacing assumption with measurement. Source: AWS Lambda Performance documentation — cold start latency components; opentelemetry-lambda#263 — ADOT cold start discussions; aws-otel-lambda#228 — community cold start measurements ranging 200ms-4000ms+.

**ADOT Extension IAM Permission Enumeration (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-159** (P1 — HIGH): Lambda execution roles for ADOT-instrumented Lambdas (SSE Lambda and canary Lambda) MUST include ALL IAM actions required by the ADOT Extension: (a) `xray:PutTraceSegments` — trace data submission; (b) `xray:PutTelemetryRecords` — Extension health telemetry; (c) `xray:GetSamplingRules` — centralized sampling rule retrieval; (d) `xray:GetSamplingTargets` — per-rule sampling target allocation; (e) `xray:GetSamplingStatisticSummaries` — sampling statistics reporting. FR-017 requires "X-Ray IAM permissions" but does not enumerate ADOT-specific actions. The existing `AWSXRayDaemonWriteAccess` managed policy covers ONLY actions (a) and (b). Missing `GetSampling*` actions (c-e) cause the ADOT Extension's `awsproxy` to fail silently, causing the OTel sampler to fall back to `TraceIDRatioBased` at 1 trace/sec — a catastrophic degradation from 100% sampling to ~0.001% with NO error visible to the Lambda function and NO CloudWatch alarm. The IAM policy MUST either use a custom policy statement with all 5 actions or combine `AWSXRayDaemonWriteAccess` with `AWSXrayReadOnlyAccess`. Source: ADOT permissions documentation — aws-otel.github.io/docs/setup/permissions/; AWS X-Ray identity-based policy examples.

**RESPONSE_STREAM + ADOT Extension Lifecycle Verification (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-160** (P1 — HIGH): The Lambda RESPONSE_STREAM + ADOT Extension lifecycle interaction MUST be verified in preprod before production deployment. The spec's foundational assumption — that the ADOT Extension remains alive and accepts OTLP spans during the entire SSE streaming phase — has NO canonical documentation from AWS. The AWS Lambda Extensions API states "After receiving the function response from the runtime, Lambda returns the response to the client, even if extensions are still running" — written for buffered responses where "function response" is a single event. For streaming, "function response" is continuous. If the Extension interprets response header send as invoke-phase completion and begins pre-Shutdown cleanup, streaming-phase spans may be dropped or lost. The verification gate MUST: (a) deploy the ADOT-instrumented SSE Lambda in preprod with a 15-second streaming duration; (b) create OTel spans at 1-second intervals throughout the streaming phase; (c) query X-Ray for ALL spans including the final span created at second 14; (d) confirm ≥95% of streaming-phase spans appear in X-Ray (allowing for known ~30% edge-case drop from aws-otel-lambda#886, but 95% aggregate across many invocations); (e) this gate blocks FR-107 Phase 2 progression. This is the spec's ONLY foundational architectural assumption that lacks a canonical source. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — Extensions lifecycle phases; AWS Lambda Response Streaming documentation — no mention of Extension interaction; absence of documentation is the finding.

**Function URL Sampling Cost Guard (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-161** (P1 — HIGH): Lambda Function URL invocations MUST have a sampling cost guard that prevents unbounded X-Ray spend in production. With `parentbased_always_on` sampler (FR-056), Function URL invocations have no parent context (bypass API Gateway entirely), making every invocation a root span sampled at 100%. At $5/million traces, 10 million Function URL invocations/day costs $50 — exceeding FR-038's monthly cost guard in a single day. The cost guard MUST include: (a) an X-Ray centralized sampling rule with `ServiceName = "{sse_lambda_function_name}"` and `URLPath = "*"` that limits Function URL sampling to a configurable rate (100% in dev/preprod per FR-034, configurable for production); (b) FR-038's billing alarms MUST include a per-day anomaly detection alarm (not just monthly thresholds) that fires when daily X-Ray cost exceeds 200% of the trailing 7-day average; (c) the production sampling rate MUST be adjustable via the X-Ray console without code deployment. Note: this FR does NOT change the sampler from `parentbased_always_on` to `xray` — the `parentbased_always_on` sampler correctly honors parent decisions for API Gateway-fronted Lambdas. The centralized sampling rule provides the cost control for parentless (Function URL) traffic while preserving 100% sampling for API Gateway traffic (Dashboard Lambda only) that inherits parent decisions. Source: AWS X-Ray pricing — $5.00 per million traces recorded; X-Ray centralized sampling rules; OTel `parentbased_always_on` specification — delegates to root sampler when no parent context exists.

**SC-064 Split — Distinct Failure Mode Verification (Round 20 — Amendment)**

- **FR-156a** (P2 — MEDIUM, informational): SC-064 (Round 14, amended Round 17) is SUPERSEDED by SC-064a and SC-064b in Round 20. The original SC tested two distinct failure modes (port-unreachable and hung Extension) in a single success criterion. These failure modes exercise different code paths: port-unreachable triggers ECONNREFUSED (fast, no thread wrapper), hung Extension requires FR-139's thread wrapper (slow, 2500ms timeout). A single SC testing two code paths produces ambiguous pass/fail — if one mode passes and the other fails, the SC status is undefined. The split ensures each failure mode is independently verifiable.

**Exhaustive treat_missing_data Classification (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-162** (P2 — MEDIUM): All CloudWatch alarms MUST have an explicitly documented `treat_missing_data` classification. FR-121 (Round 14) classifies by alarm type and FR-131 (Round 15) mandates `missing` for application metric alarms, but neither provides the exhaustive per-alarm mapping needed by implementers. The exhaustive classification is: (a) `treat_missing_data = "breaching"`: canary heartbeat alarms (FR-126 — absence = system down), `no_new_items` alarm (absence = pipeline broken); (b) `treat_missing_data = "missing"`: all application-emitted custom metric alarms (`StuckItems`, `ConnectionAcquireFailures`, `EventLatencyMs`, `SilentFailure/Count` per FR-124, all FR-043 reliability metrics, `MetricsLambdaErrors`, `HighLatencyAlert`, `PollDurationMs`, `AnalysisErrors`), all Lambda error rate alarms (FR-127), all Lambda latency alarms (FR-128), API Gateway `IntegrationLatency` alarms (FR-138), all memory utilization alarms (FR-104); (c) `treat_missing_data = "notBreaching"`: AWS-native cost/billing alarms (FR-038), X-Ray billing alarms (SC-016). Zero alarms use `"ignore"`. Zero alarms rely on the CloudWatch provider default (which varies between console and API creation). Source: CloudWatch alarm documentation — treat_missing_data semantics; AWS Well-Architected REL-06 — alarm configuration best practices.

**X-Ray Trace Archival for Production Incidents (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-163** (P2 — MEDIUM): Production X-Ray trace data MUST be archivable to S3 before the 30-day retention window expires for any production incident that triggers a post-mortem or escalation. FR-155 documents the 30-day retention as non-configurable. The archival mechanism MUST: (a) be triggered manually by an operator as part of the incident response procedure (FR-122 rollback process); (b) use the X-Ray `GetTraceSummaries` and `BatchGetTraces` APIs to export trace documents for the incident time window; (c) store exported traces in S3 with a 1-year retention policy matching the organization's incident record retention; (d) be documented in the operational runbook alongside FR-122's rollback procedure with rate-limit awareness (`BatchGetTraces` is limited to 5 traces/request at 5 requests/sec — 100,000 traces takes ~67 minutes). This FR does NOT mandate continuous or automated archival (cost prohibitive at scale) — it mandates a documented manual procedure that operators CAN execute when needed for incidents. Source: AWS X-Ray API Reference — GetTraceSummaries, BatchGetTraces rate limits; AWS X-Ray quotas — 30-day trace data retention (non-configurable).

**Work Order File Synchronization Enforcement (Round 20 — New)**

- **FR-164** (P2 — MEDIUM): Work order files (`docs/x-ray/fix-*.md`) MUST enumerate ALL functional requirements mapped to their respective tasks in the HL document's Work Order table. FR-132 (Round 15) detects work order staleness but does not enforce resolution. As of Round 20, fix-*.md files contain only Round 1-6 FRs — 100+ FRs from Rounds 7-20 are mapped in the HL document but absent from individual implementation guides. An implementer using `fix-sse-subsegments.md` (Task 5) as their task guide would see only the original FRs and miss 50+ requirements added in Rounds 7-18. The synchronization MUST: (a) be completed before implementation begins on any task (FR-107 Phase 0 prerequisite, jointly with FR-157); (b) be validated by FR-132's automated check with zero gaps; (c) include FR cross-references with round annotations (e.g., "FR-100 (Round 12)") to provide implementers with requirement provenance. Source: Observed failure — work order staleness has persisted since Round 7 despite FR-132 detection existing since Round 15.

---

### Round 21 Emergent Issues Identified

**13 emergent issues identified (2 CRITICAL, 5 HIGH, 6 MEDIUM)**

1. **CRITICAL**: FR-156's third span-loss vector (BSP deadlock, opentelemetry-python#3886) is FIXED in SDK v1.33.0+ — project uses v1.39.1 which has the rewritten `BatchProcessor` using `collections.deque` + `threading.Event` instead of the old `threading.Condition` with nested lock acquisition. The "three catalogued span-loss vectors" reduces to TWO. FR-156's diagnostic logging remains valuable but the risk profile changes fundamentally.
2. **CRITICAL**: SC-040's verification method ("confirming zero 'Queue is full' log entries") is INVALID on SDK v1.39.1 — the new `BatchProcessor` uses `collections.deque([], max_queue_size)` where `appendleft()` silently drops the oldest span with NO log, NO callback, NO metric. This is by OTel design (issue #4261 — logging in `emit()` causes infinite recursion via logging instrumentation). An operator cannot detect BSP queue overflow through logs alone.
3. **HIGH**: ADOT Extension does NOT restart after crash within the same execution environment — confirmed by AWS Lambda Extensions API documentation. The TracerProvider module-level singleton retains a stale OTLP exporter pointing to localhost:4318, receiving ECONNREFUSED on every export attempt. The OTLP HTTP exporter auto-reconnects when the target becomes reachable (no TracerProvider recreation needed), but since the Extension NEVER restarts, recovery never occurs for the sandbox's lifetime (~5-15 minutes). This is a FOURTH span-loss vector (not previously catalogued) that affects ALL spans on the affected sandbox, not just edge-case timing windows.
4. **HIGH**: No IAM policy drift detection for X-Ray permissions — FR-159 enumerates 5 required IAM actions but no automation detects if permissions are silently removed. AWS has no native "expected vs actual" IAM drift service. AWS Config `iam-policy-change` managed rule is the closest native solution; CloudTrail + EventBridge can detect IAM mutation events.
5. **HIGH**: Canary dead-man detection gap — FR-126's heartbeat alarm (`treat_missing_data=breaching`) detects a stopped canary IF CloudWatch Alarms service is healthy. But if the canary stops running AND primary-region CloudWatch Alarms are degraded simultaneously, the cross-region SNS (FR-136) cannot fire because it depends on the canary Lambda executing. This is a double-failure scenario (EventBridge/Lambda failure + CloudWatch failure) with zero external detection.
6. **HIGH**: PutTraceSegments TPS quota is ~2,500/region (not 2,600 as stated in spec assumptions), AND it is adjustable via Service Quotas (quota code `L-AB6D2D9B`). The spec treats this as a hard, non-adjustable limit. Exceeding it returns `ThrottledException` with permanently lost segments in `UnprocessedTraceSegments`.
7. **HIGH**: OTLP HTTP exporter retry behavior blocks BSP worker thread — retries up to 6 times with exponential backoff (up to 10s total), holding `_export_lock`. During retry sleep, the BSP worker thread is blocked and spans accumulate in the deque. Under ADOT Extension degradation (intermittent 5xx), this amplifies span loss beyond the ~30% edge-case from aws-otel-lambda#886.
8. **MEDIUM**: X-Ray Groups quota (25/region) and Sampling Rules quota (25/region) are BOTH adjustable via Service Quotas — not "non-adjustable" as previously assumed. However, the spec creates multiple Groups (FR-013 error group, FR-141 sse-reconnections) without tracking total count against quota.
9. **MEDIUM**: X-Ray encryption at rest is enabled by default with AWS-managed key — optional CMK available via `PutEncryptionConfig`. Not addressed in spec despite FR-155 covering PII prohibition. Encryption-at-rest configuration should be documented for compliance posture.
10. **MEDIUM**: GetTraceSummaries has a 6-hour maximum time range window per request — FR-163's archival procedure must issue multiple requests with sliding time windows for incidents spanning >6 hours, compounding the rate-limit delay.
11. **MEDIUM**: Centralized X-Ray sampling rules do NOT override ParentBased sampler parent decisions — they only apply at trace roots (no parent context). FR-161's cost guard controls Function URL traffic (rootless) but has NO effect on API Gateway traffic (Dashboard Lambda only) that inherits parent sampling decisions. This is correct behavior but must be explicitly documented to prevent implementer confusion. Note: Ingestion, Analysis, Notification, and Metrics are root-span Lambdas (EventBridge/SNS triggered, no parent context) — centralized rules DO apply to them.
12. **MEDIUM**: Lambda Function URL is invisible in X-Ray service map — no separate "Function URL" node exists (unlike API Gateway). Operators lose gateway-level latency breakdown (authorization, WAF evaluation, integration latency). Service map shows the Lambda function directly.
13. **MEDIUM**: ADOT version upgrade procedure needs formalization — container-based ADOT (FR-069/FR-070) requires Dockerfile digest update + rebuild + deploy + cold-start re-measurement (FR-158). No runbook documents this procedure or its required verification gates.

**FR-156 BSP Deadlock Vector Status Amendment (Round 21 — Amendment)**

- **FR-165** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-156's characterization of BSP deadlock (opentelemetry-python#3886) as an active span-loss vector MUST be amended. The OTel Python SDK v1.33.0 (released 2025) completely rewrote `BatchSpanProcessor` internals — the old implementation used `threading.Condition` with nested lock acquisition patterns that deadlocked under `atexit`/`fork`; the new implementation (used in this project's pinned v1.39.1) uses a `collections.deque` + `threading.Event` (`_worker_awaken`) pattern with no nested locks. FR-156's diagnostic distinction between "bsp_or_extension_hang" and "extension_unavailable" remains architecturally valuable — it differentiates ADOT Extension failures from SDK-internal issues. However, the structured log label `bsp_or_extension_hang` MUST be amended to `extension_hang` because BSP deadlock is no longer a possible cause at the pinned SDK version. The spec's "THREE catalogued span-loss vectors" MUST be reduced to TWO: (1) ADOT Extension drop race (FR-074), (2) ADOT Extension hang (FR-139). FR-156's BSP deadlock vector is RETIRED for SDK v1.33.0+ with the caveat that re-introducing older OTel SDK versions would re-expose this risk. Source: OTel Python SDK `opentelemetry/sdk/_shared_internal/__init__.py` — `BatchProcessor` class (v1.39.1), lines 84-243; `os.register_at_fork` handling at lines 123-126; opentelemetry-python#3886 — fix merged in v1.33.0.

**SC-040 Verification Method Correction (Round 21 — Amendment)**

- **FR-166** (P0 — CRITICAL): SC-040's verification method ("confirming zero 'Queue is full' log entries") MUST be replaced. The SDK v1.39.1 `BatchProcessor.emit()` method uses `collections.deque([], max_queue_size)` where `appendleft()` silently evicts the oldest element when full — there is NO log entry, NO callback, and NO metric on span drop. The `emit()` method explicitly documents this constraint: "Do not add any logging.log statements to this function, they can be being routed back to this emit function, resulting in endless recursive calls" (opentelemetry-python#4261). The replacement verification method MUST: (a) instrument a test wrapper around the BSP's internal `deque` that counts `len(deque)` at each `emit()` call and records the high-water mark; (b) assert that the high-water mark never reaches `max_queue_size` during a standard 15-second streaming session; (c) alternatively, compare total spans created (counted by a test `SpanProcessor` shim) against total spans exported (counted by a test `SpanExporter` shim) — any discrepancy indicates dropped spans. FR-091's capture of BSP WARNING "Queue is full, dropping span" is also INVALIDATED — this log message does not exist in SDK v1.39.1. Source: OTel Python SDK `_shared_internal/__init__.py:200-208` — `emit()` method with deque; opentelemetry-python#4261 — logging recursion prohibition.

**ADOT Extension Non-Recovery Span-Loss Documentation (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-167** (P1 — HIGH): The spec MUST document ADOT Extension non-recovery as a DISTINCT span-loss scenario (separate from FR-074 drop race and FR-139 hang). When the ADOT Extension process crashes (OOM, segfault, collector pipeline failure) within a Lambda execution environment, the Lambda service does NOT restart it. The Extension is dead for ALL subsequent warm invocations on that sandbox (potentially 5-15 minutes until idle recycling). The TracerProvider module-level singleton's OTLP HTTP exporter automatically retries connections to localhost:4318, receiving `ConnectionError` on each attempt. The BSP catches all exporter exceptions by OTel specification design (`_shared_internal/__init__.py:178-195`), so the Lambda continues executing normally with zero trace export and zero visible errors. Detection: FR-140's `ADOTExtensionUnavailable` CloudWatch Logs metric filter detects the per-invocation failure; the canary (FR-019/FR-036) detects aggregate trace loss. Recovery: only execution environment recycling (idle timeout) or new cold start. The spec's span-loss vector catalogue MUST be updated to THREE vectors: (1) ADOT Extension drop race (FR-074, ~30% edge-case), (2) ADOT Extension hang (FR-139, thread wrapper abort), (3) ADOT Extension crash non-recovery (FR-167, 100% loss on affected sandbox). Unlike vectors 1 and 2 which affect individual flush operations, vector 3 affects ALL spans on the affected sandbox for its remaining lifetime. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — Extensions started once during INIT, not restarted on crash; OTel Python SDK `BatchProcessor._export()` exception handling; OTLP HTTP exporter `_export()` retry with `ConnectionError`.

**IAM Policy Drift Detection for X-Ray Permissions (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-168** (P1 — HIGH): An automated mechanism MUST detect when IAM permissions required by ADOT-instrumented Lambdas (FR-159's 5 actions) are modified or removed. AWS has no native "expected vs actual" IAM policy drift service. The detection MUST use one of: (a) AWS Config `iam-policy-change` managed rule with a CloudWatch Events rule that evaluates Lambda execution role policies against the required 5-action set, or (b) CloudTrail EventBridge rule matching `IAM:PutRolePolicy`, `IAM:DetachRolePolicy`, `IAM:DeleteRolePolicy`, and `IAM:AttachRolePolicy` events for ADOT-instrumented Lambda execution role ARNs, triggering evaluation of whether the 5 required actions remain present. When drift is detected, the mechanism MUST: (a) emit a `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/IAMPolicyDrift` CloudWatch metric with `FunctionName` dimension, (b) trigger a CloudWatch alarm, (c) include the specific missing action(s) in the alarm description. This prevents the silent degradation to 1 trace/sec caused by missing `GetSampling*` permissions (FR-159) from persisting undetected. The detection latency for IAM changes via CloudTrail is typically < 15 minutes. Source: AWS Config managed rules — `iam-policy-change`; AWS CloudTrail event reference — IAM events; FR-159 silent fallback analysis.

**Canary Dead-Man External Health Check (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-169** (P1 — HIGH): The canary's liveness MUST be externally verifiable beyond CloudWatch-internal mechanisms. FR-126's heartbeat alarm (`treat_missing_data=breaching`) detects a stopped canary when CloudWatch Alarms service is healthy. FR-136's cross-region SNS detects failures when the canary runs and discovers problems. Neither mechanism detects the double-failure scenario: canary stops running AND primary-region CloudWatch Alarms are degraded. The canary Lambda MUST emit a heartbeat signal to an external monitoring endpoint on every successful invocation: (a) a cross-region CloudWatch metric in the SAME region as FR-136's cross-region SNS topic (NOT the primary region), published via direct `cloudwatch.put_metric_data()` to the backup region endpoint, OR (b) a POST to an external uptime monitoring service (PagerDuty heartbeat, OpsGenie heartbeat, or equivalent) that alerts when heartbeats stop. The external heartbeat MUST be fire-and-forget (best-effort, no error propagation to canary logic) because the canary's primary function (FR-145) must not be disrupted by heartbeat delivery failures. This external heartbeat closes the last remaining gap in the meta-observability chain: X-Ray → canary detects → CloudWatch + cross-region SNS alerts → external heartbeat verifies canary is alive. Source: AWS Well-Architected REL-13 — "monitor the health of your monitoring systems across regions"; PagerDuty heartbeat monitoring pattern.

**PutTraceSegments TPS Quota Correction and Monitoring (Round 21 — Amendment)**

- **FR-170** (P1 — HIGH): The spec's assumption of "2,600 segments/second/region" as the X-Ray throughput limit MUST be corrected to "~2,500 TPS default" (actual value varies by region). This quota IS adjustable via AWS Service Quotas (quota code `L-AB6D2D9B`). The spec MUST: (a) correct all references from "2,600" to "~2,500 (adjustable)" — specifically the Round 3 assumption and any edge case referencing this limit; (b) add a CloudWatch alarm on the `AWS/XRay` service quota utilization metric or a custom metric derived from `PutTraceSegments` API response parsing for `UnprocessedTraceSegments` count; (c) document that exceeding the quota returns `ThrottledException` and affected segments are listed in `UnprocessedTraceSegments` — data is PERMANENTLY lost (not queued or retried by the X-Ray service). At current projected traffic (<1M requests/month), this limit is not a concern. At 10x traffic growth, with 100% sampling and ~45 spans per SSE invocation, the system would produce ~520 segments/sec at peak — well within quota. However, burst traffic during incidents could spike higher. The Service Quotas alarm provides early warning before data loss occurs. Source: AWS X-Ray Service Quotas — quota code `L-AB6D2D9B`; AWS Service Quotas documentation — quota utilization alarms.

**OTLP Exporter Retry-Induced BSP Worker Block (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-171** (P2 — MEDIUM): The spec MUST document that the OTLP HTTP exporter's retry behavior can block the BSP worker thread for up to 10 seconds per failed batch export. The exporter retries up to `_MAX_RETRYS = 6` times with exponential backoff (`2^retry_num * random.uniform(0.8, 1.2)` seconds) on HTTP 408 or 5xx responses. During retry sleep (`self._shutdown_in_progress.wait(backoff_seconds)`), the BSP worker thread is blocked and cannot process other batches. Spans continue accumulating in the deque from `emit()` calls. With `schedule_delay_millis=1000` and retry blocking, the effective export interval degrades from 1 second to 11+ seconds under Extension degradation, causing deque overflow and silent span drops (FR-166). This is NOT a bug — the OTel spec mandates retry for transient failures. However, it amplifies span loss beyond FR-074's ~30% edge case during ADOT Extension degradation scenarios. FR-114's `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT=2` caps individual request timeout but does NOT cap total retry duration. Mitigation: the retry loop checks `deadline` and aborts when total timeout exceeds `self._timeout` (default 10s). Note: HTTP 429 (rate limit) is NOT retried by the OTLP HTTP exporter — this deviates from the OTel spec recommendation. Source: OTel Python SDK `trace_exporter/__init__.py:174-208` — export retry loop; `_common/__init__.py:29-34` — `_is_retryable()`; opentelemetry-python — retry policy implementation.

**X-Ray Groups and Sampling Rules Quota Tracking (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-172** (P2 — MEDIUM): The spec MUST track X-Ray Groups and Sampling Rules against their per-region quotas. Both quotas default to 25 per region and are adjustable via Service Quotas. Current spec creates at minimum: (a) 1 error/fault Group (FR-013), (b) 1 `sse-reconnections` Group (FR-141), (c) 1 centralized sampling rule for Function URL (FR-161), plus the default Group and default sampling rule. This leaves ~21 Groups and ~22 sampling rules available. Future additions (per-Lambda Groups, per-environment sampling rules, per-customer trace Groups) could exhaust quotas without warning. The Terraform configuration MUST: (a) include a comment documenting the current Group and Sampling Rule count against the 25-per-region quota; (b) be validated by a CI check that counts `aws_xray_group` and `aws_xray_sampling_rule` resources across all Terraform configurations and warns when count exceeds 20 (80% of default quota). Source: AWS X-Ray Service Quotas — Groups quota code `L-F895D63C`, Sampling Rules quota code `L-B5F5E1ED`; both adjustable.

**X-Ray Encryption-at-Rest Documentation (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-173** (P2 — MEDIUM): The spec MUST document X-Ray's encryption-at-rest configuration. X-Ray encrypts ALL trace data at rest by default using an AWS-managed key (zero customer configuration required). Optionally, a customer-managed CMK can be configured via `PutEncryptionConfig` API per-region. FR-155 prohibits PII in trace data; encryption-at-rest provides defense-in-depth for data that inadvertently contains sensitive content during the 30-day retention window. The spec MUST: (a) document that default encryption is active and sufficient for the current threat model; (b) note that CMK configuration is available if the organization's compliance posture requires customer-controlled encryption keys; (c) NOT mandate CMK by default (adds KMS cost and key management complexity without security benefit beyond what AWS-managed encryption provides). This FR is informational — it documents the existing security posture rather than requiring changes. Source: AWS X-Ray Developer Guide — "Data protection in AWS X-Ray"; `PutEncryptionConfig` API reference.

**GetTraceSummaries Time Window Constraint (Round 21 — Amendment)**

- **FR-174** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-163's trace archival procedure MUST account for the `GetTraceSummaries` API's 6-hour maximum time range window per request. For incidents spanning more than 6 hours, the archival script MUST issue multiple requests with sliding 6-hour time windows to cover the full incident duration. This compounding constraint — combined with the 30 TPS rate limit and 100-result pagination — means archiving a 24-hour incident with 100,000 traces requires: (a) 4 time windows × multiple paginated requests to enumerate trace IDs, (b) 20,000 `BatchGetTraces` requests (5 traces/request) at 5 TPS = ~67 minutes for export. Total archival time for a 24-hour incident: ~70-90 minutes depending on trace distribution across time windows. FR-163's runbook MUST include this time estimation formula and recommend starting archival immediately upon incident declaration (not waiting for post-mortem). Source: AWS X-Ray API Reference — `GetTraceSummaries` parameters; confirmed 6-hour maximum time range window, 30 TPS rate limit, 100 results per page.

**Centralized Sampling Rule Scope Documentation (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-175** (P2 — MEDIUM): The spec MUST explicitly document the interaction between `parentbased_always_on` sampler (FR-056) and centralized X-Ray sampling rules (FR-161). Centralized sampling rules ONLY apply at trace roots — spans with no parent context. They do NOT override parent sampling decisions propagated via `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. For this system: (a) API Gateway-fronted Lambdas (Dashboard, Ingestion, Analysis, Notification) receive parent sampling decisions FROM API Gateway — centralized rules have NO effect on these Lambdas; (b) Function URL Lambda (SSE Streaming) receives no parent context from Function URL — centralized rules ARE the sampling decision; (c) EventBridge-triggered Lambda (Canary) receives no parent context — centralized rules apply; (d) the Metrics Lambda receives no parent context (EventBridge Scheduler) — centralized rules apply. FR-161's cost guard therefore controls SSE + Canary + Metrics Lambda sampling rates. API Gateway Lambdas are always sampled at whatever rate API Gateway decides (typically 100% for first request/sec + 5% thereafter per default rule). Implementers MUST understand this distinction to avoid expecting centralized rules to reduce API Gateway Lambda trace volume. Source: OTel SDK `sampling.py:349-367` — `ParentBased` delegation logic; X-Ray centralized sampling specification; AWS API Gateway X-Ray sampling behavior.

**Lambda Function URL Service Map Limitation (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-176** (P2 — MEDIUM): The spec MUST document that Lambda Function URL invocations are INVISIBLE as a separate node in the X-Ray service map. Unlike API Gateway (which creates its own X-Ray segment and appears as a gateway node), Function URL acts as a passthrough — the trace shows the Lambda function directly with no intermediary. Operators lose gateway-level latency breakdown (authorization time, TLS negotiation, integration latency) that API Gateway provides. The SSE Lambda (accessed via Function URL) appears in the service map as a Lambda node with downstream dependencies (DynamoDB, CloudWatch) but no upstream gateway node. For debugging SSE connection establishment latency, operators MUST use Lambda `REPORT` log lines (`Init Duration` for cold start, `Duration` for handler) rather than X-Ray gateway-level metrics. FR-138's Function URL `Url5xxError` alarm partially compensates for the missing gateway-level error visibility. Source: AWS Lambda Function URL documentation — no X-Ray segment creation; AWS Lambda X-Ray tracing documentation — segment created by Lambda service, not Function URL.

**ADOT Version Upgrade Runbook (Round 21 — New)**

- **FR-177** (P2 — MEDIUM): An operational runbook MUST document the ADOT version upgrade procedure for container-based Lambda deployments (FR-069/FR-070). The procedure MUST include: (a) check ADOT release notes for breaking changes in collector config schema, exporter behavior, or resource detector output; (b) update Dockerfile ADOT image digest (`COPY --from=public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/aws-otel-lambda-extension-amd64:NEW_VERSION@sha256:NEW_DIGEST`); (c) run CI collector config validation (FR-116/SC-066) against the new ADOT binary; (d) deploy to preprod and re-measure cold start latency (FR-158 gate); (e) run FR-160's streaming span retention verification (≥95%); (f) run FR-117's automated trace validation (segment counts, annotation keys); (g) verify ADOT Extension logs show `"Successfully fetched sampling rules"` (FR-159/SC-109 IAM verification); (h) if all gates pass, update production Dockerfile and deploy. The procedure MUST be cross-referenced from FR-070 (digest pinning) and FR-110 (pre-ADOT baseline image retention). ADOT upgrades MUST NOT be bundled with application code changes — they are independently deployable and independently rollbackable (revert Dockerfile digest). Source: ADOT release process — aws-otel.github.io; FR-070 digest pinning rationale; FR-110 rollback image retention.

---

### Round 22 Emergent Issues Identified

**13 emergent issues identified (2 CRITICAL, 4 HIGH, 7 MEDIUM)**

(Focus areas: sampling graduation, kill switch criteria, partial deployment detection, query performance, multi-account strategy, PII scanning, ADOT overhead, warm invocation interaction, canary interference, GitHub issue verification)

1. **CRITICAL**: FR-170's PutTraceSegments TPS correction from "2,600" to "~2,500" is ITSELF incorrect — the AWS default is **500 TPS per region** (Service Quotas L-AB6D2D9B). The "~2,500" figure may represent an account-specific quota increase. New environments, regions, or accounts start at 500 TPS. At current projected traffic with 100% sampling (~520 segments/sec peak), the system EXCEEDS the default 500 TPS quota at peak load without a Service Quotas increase.
2. **CRITICAL**: FR-157's required GitHub issue ("HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18") confirmed DOES NOT EXIST — zero issues matching "staleness", "Round 18", "SC-107", or "FR-157" found across all 19 repository issues. SC-107 requirement is unfulfilled.
3. **HIGH**: No sampling graduation plan for transitioning from 100% to reduced rates as traffic grows. OTel supports `parentbased_traceidratio` for graduated reduction. API Gateway controls downstream Dashboard Lambda sampling decisions — centralized rules have NO effect on the Dashboard Lambda (the sole API Gateway-routed Lambda, confirmed in FR-175). All other Lambdas (Ingestion, Analysis, Notification, Metrics, SSE, Canary) are root-span and governed by centralized rules.
4. **HIGH**: Kill switch `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true` (FR-059) has NO documented activation criteria. Industry best practice: reduce sampling first (FR-179), kill switch only as last resort when collector failure rate >50% or cold start exceeds 2s.
5. **HIGH**: `aws lambda update-function-configuration` REPLACES ALL environment variables — omitting existing vars deletes them. Kill switch procedure must capture existing vars first via `get-function-configuration`. Published versions require new version publish + alias update.
6. **HIGH**: OTel Python SDK's `ReadableSpan` passed to `SpanProcessor.on_end()` is READ-ONLY. Attribute modification is impossible post-creation, making PII redaction via custom SpanProcessor architecturally impossible. Only mutable point: `SpanProcessor.on_start()` or span creation.
7. **HIGH**: No cross-Lambda deployment version tracking. Terraform partial apply can leave N of 6 Lambdas on new version with no detection mechanism. AWS has no native deployment cohort tracker for Lambda functions.
8. **MEDIUM**: Canary traces appear in production X-Ray data with no filtering. X-Ray Groups with annotation filter `!annotation.synthetic` provide separation. W3C Trace Context has NO synthetic flag.
9. **MEDIUM**: Annotation budget unmanaged — max 50 indexed annotations per trace (non-adjustable). Spec creates annotations across multiple FRs without tracking count. High-cardinality data should use metadata (not indexed).
10. **MEDIUM**: ADOT resource overhead not formally budgeted: 35-70 MB cold, 40-60 MB warm, 200-500ms cold start, 1-5ms warm invocation. Project's 1024 MB is sufficient (~960 MB for application).
11. **MEDIUM**: In-flight span loss on sandbox recycle: 2-second default flush window (configurable to max 10s via `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT`). SIGKILL = no graceful shutdown, all pending spans lost.
12. **MEDIUM**: Multi-account X-Ray via OAM not addressed. Full trace graph preserved, no double PutTraceSegments counting, sampling rules per-account only. Future-state, not blocking.
13. **MEDIUM**: GetTraceSummaries has no `MaxResults` parameter — `Sampling=true` returns statistical subset, potentially incomplete. FR-174's archival MUST set `Sampling=false`.

**PutTraceSegments Default TPS Correction (Round 22 — Amendment)**

- **FR-178** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-170's correction from "2,600" to "~2,500 TPS" MUST be further corrected. The AWS default quota for PutTraceSegments (L-AB6D2D9B) is **500 TPS per region**, not ~2,500. The ~2,500 figure documented in Round 21 may represent an account-specific quota increase. This distinction is critical: (a) any NEW environment, region, or AWS account starts at 500 TPS; (b) current projected peak traffic with 100% sampling (~520 segments/sec) EXCEEDS the default quota; (c) a Service Quotas increase request MUST be part of the deployment checklist for new environments. The spec MUST differentiate between "default quota" (500 TPS) and "applied quota" (account-specific, verify via `aws service-quotas get-service-quota --service-code xray --quota-code L-AB6D2D9B`). Source: AWS X-Ray Service Quotas — documented default is 500 TPS, adjustable via L-AB6D2D9B.

**FR-157 GitHub Issue Filing (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-190** (P0 — CRITICAL): The GitHub issue required by SC-107 ("HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18") MUST be filed. Verified: zero issues exist in the sentiment-analyzer-gsk repository matching "staleness", "Round 18", "SC-107", or "FR-157" across all 19 open/closed issues. FR-157's requirement for retroactive HL document staleness tracking is unfulfilled. The issue MUST be titled "HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18 — Retroactive Tracking (FR-157/SC-107)" and reference FR-157, SC-107.

**Sampling Graduation Plan (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-179** (P1 — HIGH): A documented sampling graduation plan MUST specify phase transitions: (a) Phase 1 — `parentbased_always_on`, 100% sampling, for dev and <500 TPS; (b) Phase 2 — `parentbased_traceidratio` at 50% via `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER=parentbased_traceidratio` / `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG=0.5`, for 500-2000 TPS; (c) Phase 3 — same at 10%, for >2000 TPS; (d) Phase 4 — tail-based sampling at collector level. Phase transitions triggered by PutTraceSegments quota utilization alarms. The Dashboard Lambda (sole API Gateway-fronted Lambda) inherits parent sampling decisions (FR-175) — centralized rule changes do NOT affect it. All other Lambdas (Ingestion, Analysis, Notification, Metrics, SSE, Canary) are root-span and respond to centralized rule changes. Source: OTel SDK specification — sampler environment variable configuration.

**Kill Switch Activation Criteria (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-180** (P1 — HIGH): FR-059's `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` kill switch MUST have documented activation criteria: (a) p99 duration increases >5% correlated with tracing → reduce sampling; (b) X-Ray `ThrottledCount` >0 sustained 5 min → reduce to 25%; (c) monthly trace count >150% budget → reduce to 10%; (d) ADOT exporter failure rate >50% for 10 min → set `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true`; (e) Init Duration >2s with OTel vs <500ms baseline → set `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true`. Sampling reduction (FR-179) is ALWAYS first mitigation before kill switch. Source: OTel specification — OTEL_SDK_DISABLED creates NoOp providers.

**Lambda Environment Variable Update Hazard (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-181** (P1 — HIGH): Kill switch procedure (FR-180) MUST document that `aws lambda update-function-configuration` REPLACES ALL environment variables. Procedure MUST: (a) capture existing vars via `get-function-configuration`; (b) add `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true` to captured set; (c) call `update-function-configuration` with complete set. For alias-based production deployments, also requires `publish-version` + `update-alias`. Source: AWS Lambda API Reference — UpdateFunctionConfiguration.

**Deployment Version Tagging and Skew Detection (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-182** (P1 — HIGH): All 6 Lambda functions MUST be tagged with `deploy-sha` (git SHA or Terraform run ID) and carry `DEPLOYMENT_VERSION` environment variable. A post-apply skew detection check MUST query all 6 tags and fail on mismatch. Skew detection MUST emit `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/DeploymentVersionSkew` CloudWatch metric and trigger P1 alarm. Recovery: re-run `terraform apply`. Source: AWS Lambda tags documentation; Terraform partial apply behavior.

**OTel Python ReadableSpan Immutability (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-183** (P1 — HIGH): The spec MUST document that `ReadableSpan` (passed to `SpanProcessor.on_end()`) is READ-ONLY — attributes CANNOT be modified post-creation. PII redaction via custom SpanProcessor `on_end()` is architecturally impossible in Python SDK. The only mutation point is during active span lifetime (`on_start()` or between `start_span()` and `end()`). The OTel Collector's `redaction` processor operates on protobuf data (fully mutable) but ADOT Lambda Extension may not include contrib processors. Source: OTel Python SDK `trace/__init__.py` — ReadableSpan class.

**Span Attribute Allow-Listing (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-184** (P1 — HIGH): PII prevention MUST use attribute allow-list enforced at span creation via custom `SpanProcessor.on_start()` (receives mutable `Span`, unlike `on_end()`). The allow-list MUST: (a) define permitted annotation keys per Lambda; (b) strip unlisted attributes; (c) be validated by CI test scanning all `set_attribute()` calls; (d) log structured warning when unlisted attribute stripped. FR-155's PII prohibition becomes enforceable rather than advisory. Source: OTel Python SDK — `SpanProcessor.on_start(span, parent_context)` receives mutable Span.

**Canary Trace Annotation Standard (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-185** (P1 — HIGH): Canary traces MUST carry `annotation.synthetic = True` (boolean) on root spans. X-Ray Group `production-traces` with filter `!annotation.synthetic` provides canary-free view. X-Ray Group `canary-traces` with filter `annotation.synthetic = true` for canary monitoring. The `synthetic` key MUST be reserved/prohibited in non-canary Lambdas via FR-184's allow-list. W3C Trace Context has NO synthetic flag. Source: X-Ray filter expression documentation; W3C Trace Context Level 1 — Section 3.2.2.5.

**Annotation Budget Strategy (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-186** (P2 — MEDIUM): Annotation budget strategy MUST respect 50-per-trace hard limit. Strategy MUST: (a) categorize annotation-worthy (indexed, queryable) vs metadata-worthy (non-indexed); (b) allocate per-component: API Lambdas ≤15, SSE Lambda ≤25, Canary ≤10; (c) track in CI (warn >40, fail >50); (d) use metadata for high-cardinality non-queryable data. GetTraceSummaries `Sampling` parameter MUST be `false` for precise queries. Source: X-Ray segment document spec — 50 annotation limit.

**ADOT Resource Overhead Budget (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-187** (P2 — MEDIUM): Formal ADOT overhead budget: cold start 200-500ms + 100-300ms SDK init; memory 35-70 MB cold, 40-60 MB warm; warm invocation 1-5ms; CPU proportional to Lambda memory. Project's 1024 MB provides ~960 MB for application. Validation gate: FR-158 cold start MUST verify ADOT overhead ≤500ms of Init Duration. Cost: 1024 MB vs theoretical 512 MB without ADOT = ~2x compute cost — accepted trade-off per "traces are CRUCIAL" principle. Source: AWS ADOT Lambda documentation.

**In-Flight Span Loss on Sandbox Recycle (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-188** (P2 — MEDIUM): In-flight span loss window: ADOT Extension gets 2-second default SHUTDOWN window (configurable to 10s max via `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT`). At full BSP queue (1500 spans, batch=64), flushing requires ~24 batches — 2 seconds is INSUFFICIENT. `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` SHOULD be set to 10 seconds. For SIGKILL (Lambda timeout), NO graceful shutdown occurs. FR-093/FR-139 proactive flush mitigates predictable terminations only. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — SHUTDOWN lifecycle.

**Multi-Account X-Ray via OAM (Round 22 — New)**

- **FR-189** (P2 — MEDIUM): Future-state multi-account X-Ray via CloudWatch OAM: full trace graph preserved, NO double PutTraceSegments counting, sampling rules per-account (not shared), OAM is regional, max 5 sinks per source. Terraform: `aws_oam_sink` (monitoring account) + `aws_oam_link` (source accounts). Informational — not required for current single-account deployment. Source: AWS CloudWatch OAM documentation; Terraform AWS provider.

### Round 23 Emergent Issues Identified

**12 emergent issues identified (1 CRITICAL, 5 HIGH, 6 MEDIUM)**

(Focus areas: PII enforcement gap in attribute allow-listing, dependency version safety for OTel SDK and Powertools, X-Ray annotation survivability under truncation, ADOT degraded-state detection, operational hardening for deployment skew and canary detection latency, sampling graduation per-Lambda behavior)

1. **CRITICAL**: FR-184's attribute allow-list SpanProcessor operates in `on_start()` — this ONLY filters attributes passed at span creation time via the `attributes={}` parameter. Any code that calls `span.set_attribute(key, value)` AFTER creation bypasses the filter entirely. The OTel Python SDK provides no hook for intercepting `set_attribute()` calls during a span's active lifetime. PII can leak into X-Ray annotations via any post-creation `set_attribute()` call in application code, silent failure try/except blocks (FR-150), or third-party instrumentation libraries.
2. **HIGH**: SpanProcessor registration ordering is unspecified. `TracerProvider.add_span_processor()` wraps processors in `SynchronousMultiSpanProcessor` which calls `on_start()` and `on_end()` callbacks in REGISTRATION order. FR-184's allow-list SpanProcessor MUST be registered BEFORE the `BatchSpanProcessor`. If reversed, any future SpanProcessor that processes attributes in `on_start()` would see unfiltered data. Registration ordering is a zero-cost defensive invariant.
3. **HIGH**: X-Ray silently drops annotations beyond 50 per segment with NO defined truncation order. The ADOT X-Ray exporter maps OTel string/int/float/bool span attributes to X-Ray annotations. If a span has >50 such attributes, X-Ray API silently drops the excess with no error response. The truncation order (which 50 survive) is implementation-dependent and undocumented. OTel's automatic exception attributes (`exception.type`, `exception.message`, `exception.stacktrace`) consume 3 annotation slots per exception per span WITHOUT being tracked in FR-186's annotation budget. Under error conditions, the effective annotation budget is 47 (50 - 3 exception attributes), not 50.
4. **HIGH**: FR-177 defines an ADOT Extension upgrade runbook with 8 verification gates, but NO equivalent runbook exists for OTel Python SDK upgrades. A security vulnerability forcing an upgrade from v1.39.1 could change: (a) `BatchProcessor` internal implementation (deque behavior, silent drop mechanics); (b) `force_flush()` semantics and return values; (c) `SpanProcessor` callback signatures; (d) OTLP exporter retry behavior; (e) `BoundedAttributes` eviction policy. Any of these would invalidate spec assumptions validated against v1.39.1 source code.
5. **HIGH**: FR-101 pins OTel Python core packages but Powertools Tracer (`aws-lambda-powertools`) is UNPINNED. Powertools Tracer's `auto_patch` behavior (FR-060), `capture_method` decorator behavior (FR-031 async generator prohibition), and exception capture semantics (FR-029) are foundational to non-streaming Lambda instrumentation. A Powertools upgrade could silently re-enable `auto_patch=True` as default, reintroduce async generator decorator support with different semantics, or change exception capture behavior — all without triggering any spec compliance alarm.
6. **HIGH**: FR-167 assumes ADOT Extension crash terminates the Extension process, triggering Lambda service to destroy the execution environment. However, the ADOT Collector is written in Go, where `recover()` catches panics without process termination. A recovered panic in the collector's export pipeline could leave the Extension process alive (reports healthy to Lambda Runtime API, OTLP receiver accepts connections on :4318) but internally broken (export pipeline non-functional). Spans are accepted by the OTLP receiver but silently dropped in the broken exporter. No ECONNREFUSED (Extension is alive), no export timeout (receiver responds promptly), no Lambda error — a completely silent failure mode undetectable by FR-139's thread wrapper, FR-140's crash metric, or the canary's aggregate check.
7. **MEDIUM**: FR-096 specifies 5-minute canary interval. FR-020 requires detection within 2 consecutive intervals. Formal detection latency: worst-case 10 minutes (outage starts just after successful canary run at T=0, detected at T=5, confirmed at T=10). Outages shorter than 5 minutes are architecturally undetectable by canary. X-Ray API eventual consistency (~30s) adds to detection latency. Complementary per-invocation detection via FR-098 metric filters provides ~1-minute granularity for export failures but not for X-Ray service-side ingestion failures.
8. **NOT A RISK (Confirmed)**: `force_flush()` called twice within a single invocation on SDK v1.39.1 is safe. The second call signals the worker thread via `threading.Event`; the worker wakes, finds an empty deque (drained by first flush), exports nothing, and signals completion. `force_flush()` is idempotent on an empty queue. FR-093 proactive flush + FR-055 finally-block flush safely coexist — the second flush is a no-op.
9. **NOT A RISK (Confirmed)**: ADOT Extension startup race with Lambda handler is not a risk. Per AWS Lambda Extensions API lifecycle, Extension INIT completes and Extension calls `/extension/event/next` BEFORE the Lambda service sends the INVOKE event to the runtime. By the time the handler function executes, the Extension's OTLP receiver on :4318 is ready. On cold starts, the OTel BSP's first export attempt (1000ms after first span creation per FR-073) occurs well after Extension initialization.
10. **MEDIUM**: FR-184's CI validation gate (FR-184(c): "CI test scanning all `set_attribute()` calls") must cover the ENTIRE codebase including transitive dependencies and third-party instrumentation libraries that may call `set_attribute()` on spans obtained via `opentelemetry.trace.get_current_span()`. Libraries like `opentelemetry-instrumentation-urllib` add attributes (`http.method`, `http.url`) that may contain PII (e.g., user IDs in URL paths).
11. **MEDIUM**: FR-179 defines 4 global sampling graduation phases but does not account for the per-Lambda behavioral split documented in FR-175. API Gateway-fronted Lambdas (Dashboard, Ingestion, Analysis, Notification) inherit parent sampling decisions — centralized rule changes have NO effect on them. Function URL Lambdas (SSE), EventBridge Lambdas (Canary, Metrics) create root spans governed by centralized rules. Sampling graduation Phase 2-4 rate reductions ONLY affect 3 of 7 Lambdas. To reduce sampling on API Gateway Lambdas, API Gateway tracing must be disabled and OTel sampler must control directly — but disabling API Gateway tracing removes the API Gateway node from the X-Ray service map.
12. **MEDIUM**: FR-182's deployment version skew detection alarm fires during EVERY rolling Terraform apply because Lambda functions update sequentially (not atomically). A 6-Lambda update takes 30-60 seconds, during which deploy-sha values diverge. Without a tolerance window, every deployment triggers a P1 alarm — alarm fatigue. With an excessively long tolerance window, genuine partial-apply failures go undetected.

**FR-184 Allow-List Bypass Prevention (Round 23 — Amendment)**

- **FR-191** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-184's `SpanProcessor.on_start()` allow-list ONLY filters attributes set at span creation time (via `attributes={}` parameter to `start_span()` or `start_as_current_span()`). Attributes added later via `span.set_attribute(key, value)` bypass the filter entirely — the OTel SDK provides no `on_set_attribute()` callback. Defense-in-depth mitigation MUST include: (a) **Project convention**: ALL span attributes MUST be set at creation time via the `attributes={}` parameter; `span.set_attribute()` calls post-creation are PROHIBITED except for dynamic values that can only be determined during span execution (e.g., `db.statement` result count) — these MUST use allow-listed keys only; (b) **CI static analysis gate**: code search for `.set_attribute(` and `span[` patterns; each occurrence MUST use an allow-listed key — unlisted keys fail CI; scope includes ALL Python files in the Lambda deployment package, not just application code; (c) **Runtime audit SpanProcessor**: a second SpanProcessor registered AFTER the BSP that inspects `ReadableSpan.attributes` in `on_end()` and emits a structured WARNING log for any attribute key NOT in the allow-list — cannot remove (ReadableSpan is immutable) but enables detection; (d) **CloudWatch Logs metric filter**: pattern `{ $.allow_list_violation = true }` → `AllowListViolation` metric → alarm with `treat_missing_data=notBreaching`. Source: OTel Python SDK — `Span.set_attribute()` is a direct method on the mutable `Span` object with no SpanProcessor callback.

**SpanProcessor Registration Ordering (Round 23 — New)**

- **FR-192** (P1 — HIGH): `TracerProvider.add_span_processor()` MUST be called in this exact order: (1) `AllowListSpanProcessor` (FR-184), (2) `AuditSpanProcessor` (FR-191(c)), (3) `BatchSpanProcessor`. Rationale: `SynchronousMultiSpanProcessor` calls `on_start()` in registration order — the allow-list filter runs first, stripping unlisted attributes from the mutable span before any other processor sees them. The audit processor runs in `on_end()` (registration order irrelevant for ReadableSpan inspection, but consistent ordering is a zero-cost invariant). The BSP runs last, enqueuing the filtered span for export. If a future SpanProcessor is added, it MUST be inserted between AllowList and BSP. Source: OTel Python SDK `SynchronousMultiSpanProcessor.on_start()` — iterates `self._span_processors` in insertion order.

**X-Ray Annotation Priority and Exception Budget (Round 23 — Amendment)**

- **FR-193** (P1 — HIGH): FR-186's annotation budget MUST account for OTel automatic exception attributes. OTel's `record_exception()` adds 3 attributes per exception per span: `exception.type`, `exception.message`, `exception.stacktrace`. These are mapped to X-Ray annotations by the ADOT exporter and count against the 50-annotation limit. Effective annotation budget: (a) normal operation: 50 annotations available per FR-186 allocation; (b) error conditions: 47 annotations available (50 - 3 exception attributes); (c) multiple exceptions per span (e.g., retry with catch): 50 - (3 * N_exceptions). FR-186's per-component allocation MUST be reduced by 3: API Lambdas ≤12 (was 15), SSE Lambda ≤22 (was 25), Canary ≤7 (was 10). CI annotation budget tracking (FR-186(c)) MUST include `exception.*` attributes in the count and warn at >37, fail at >47.
