Additionally, X-Ray's truncation order for >50 annotations is UNDEFINED in AWS documentation. The ADOT exporter sends all attributes; X-Ray API silently drops excess. To ensure critical annotations survive truncation, the AllowListSpanProcessor SHOULD order attributes by priority (diagnostic-critical first) via `OrderedDict` in `on_start()`. Source: X-Ray API Reference — PutTraceSegments; ADOT X-Ray exporter `cause.go` — exception attribute mapping.

**OTel Python SDK Upgrade Runbook (Round 23 — New)**

- **FR-194** (P1 — HIGH): An OTel Python SDK upgrade runbook MUST be created with 6 verification gates, cross-referenced from FR-101. Gates: (1) **Changelog review**: identify behavioral changes in `BatchProcessor`, `SpanProcessor`, OTLP exporter, `BoundedAttributes`, and sampler; (2) **BSP span-count comparison test**: create N spans, force_flush(), verify N spans exported (detects silent drop behavior changes); (3) **force_flush() timing test**: simulate ADOT Extension hang (TCP accept, no response), verify FR-139 thread wrapper terminates within 2500ms (detects timeout enforcement changes); (4) **Memory stability test**: 100+ warm invocations, assert memory growth < 5MB (detects daemon thread leak regression); (5) **Allow-list behavior test**: verify FR-191's AllowListSpanProcessor functions correctly with new SDK version (on_start() receives mutable Span, on_end() receives ReadableSpan); (6) **1-week preprod soak**: deploy to preprod with canary monitoring before production. Source: OTel Python SDK migration guides — behavioral changes between major versions.

**Powertools Tracer Version Pinning (Round 23 — Amendment)**

- **FR-195** (P1 — HIGH): FR-101's version pinning scope MUST extend to Powertools Tracer. `aws-lambda-powertools` MUST be pinned to compatible range (e.g., `>=3.23,<4.0`) in all Lambda requirements files. Behavioral assumptions per version MUST be documented: (a) v3.x: `auto_patch=True` default; `capture_method` does not handle async generators (FR-031); exceptions auto-captured as subsegment faults (FR-029); (b) any major version upgrade (e.g., v4.0) MUST be treated with the same rigor as an OTel SDK upgrade (FR-194). Source: aws-lambda-powertools changelog — breaking changes in major versions.

**ADOT Extension Degraded State Detection (Round 23 — New)**

- **FR-196** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-167's span-loss vector #3 (ADOT Extension crash) MUST be extended to cover degraded state (Extension alive but internally broken). Detection mechanism: before each `force_flush()` call (FR-093/FR-055), the Lambda function SHOULD perform a lightweight health probe — a single empty OTLP export request to `localhost:4318/v1/traces` with zero spans. Expected response: HTTP 200. If response is non-200, timeout, or contains error body, the Extension is classified as degraded. On degraded detection: (a) emit `ADOTExtensionDegraded` CloudWatch metric (distinct from `ADOTExtensionUnavailable` in FR-140); (b) skip `force_flush()` (avoid blocking on broken Extension); (c) set `extension.degraded=true` annotation on current span (for canary detection). **CORRECTION (Round 24)**: The `recover()` assumption is DENIED — OTel Collector does NOT use `recover()` in pipeline goroutines. The degraded state scenario DOES still exist but via a DIFFERENT mechanism: persistent X-Ray API errors (429/500) cause exporter retry exhaustion, leaving Extension alive but dropping spans. See FR-200 (amendment) and FR-201 (new vector).

**Canary Detection Latency Documentation (Round 23 — New)**

- **FR-197** (P2 — MEDIUM): Canary detection latency MUST be formally documented: (a) worst-case detection latency = 2 * interval = **10 minutes** (outage starts at T=0+1s, first detection at T=5, confirmation at T=10); (b) outages shorter than 1 interval (5 minutes) are **architecturally undetectable** by canary; (c) transient X-Ray degradation recovered within <10 minutes may be completely invisible to operators; (d) X-Ray API eventual consistency (~30s) adds to detection latency; (e) canary provides **steady-state health monitoring**, NOT real-time alerting. Real-time X-Ray health signals: ADOT export failure logs (FR-098) + metric filters provide per-invocation detection (~1-minute granularity) as a complementary mechanism to canary aggregate detection. The 5-minute interval (FR-096) is a deliberate trade-off: faster intervals increase canary cost and X-Ray API consumption without eliminating the eventual-consistency detection gap.

**Sampling Graduation Per-Lambda Configuration (Round 23 — Amendment)**

- **FR-198** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-179's sampling graduation phases MUST specify per-Lambda behavior based on the architectural split documented in FR-175: (a) **Root-span Lambdas** (Function URL: SSE; EventBridge: Ingestion, Canary, Metrics, Notification; SNS: Analysis): governed by centralized X-Ray sampling rules; FR-179 Phase 2-4 rate reductions take effect immediately; this covers 6 of 7 Lambdas; (b) **Child-span Lambda** (API Gateway: Dashboard only): inherits parent sampling decisions from API Gateway; centralized rule changes have NO effect; sampling reduction requires changing API Gateway tracing configuration from `Active` to `PassThrough` — but this removes the API Gateway node from X-Ray service map; (c) **Recommended approach**: keep API Gateway tracing at `Active` (100% sampling on the Dashboard Lambda API Gateway path) and apply FR-179 graduated reduction to all root-span Lambdas; accept that Dashboard traces are always 100% sampled; cost impact is bounded because Dashboard invocations are request-proportional; (d) If 100% API Gateway sampling becomes cost-prohibitive, document that disabling API Gateway tracing trades service map fidelity for cost savings. **CORRECTION (Round 25 Clarification)**: R23 incorrectly listed Ingestion, Analysis, and Notification as API Gateway-fronted child-span Lambdas. Ground truth from Terraform: Ingestion is EventBridge-triggered, Analysis is SNS-triggered, Notification is EventBridge+SNS-triggered. Only Dashboard is API Gateway-fronted. This correction means centralized sampling rules apply to 6 of 7 Lambdas, significantly simplifying the sampling graduation plan.

**Deployment Version Skew Tolerance Window (Round 23 — Amendment)**

- **FR-199** (P2 — MEDIUM): FR-182's deployment version skew detection alarm MUST include a tolerance window to prevent alarm fatigue during routine deployments. Specification: (a) **Tolerance window**: 5 minutes after a deploy-sha change is detected on ANY Lambda; (b) **Suppression mechanism**: CloudWatch alarm `ActionsSuppressor` (composite alarm) that suppresses the skew alarm during the tolerance window; (c) **Tolerance trigger**: first Lambda function update with a new deploy-sha value starts the 5-minute window; (d) **Post-tolerance assertion**: after 5 minutes, ALL 6 Lambdas MUST have converged to the same deploy-sha; if not, alarm fires; (e) **Failed partial apply**: if `terraform apply` fails mid-update, permanent skew persists — alarm fires after tolerance window expires, which is correct behavior (genuine failure, not routine deployment); (f) **Metric**: `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/DeploymentSkewDuration` tracks seconds of skew per deployment for trend monitoring.

### Round 24 Emergent Issues Identified

**10 emergent issues identified (2 CRITICAL, 3 HIGH, 3 MEDIUM, 2 LOW)**

(Focus areas: ADOT architecture corrections via canonical source validation, assumption resolution, process gaps, span-loss vector reclassification)

1. **CRITICAL**: ADOT recovered panic vector DENIED — OTel Collector does NOT use `recover()` in pipeline goroutines (`exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go`). Panics crash the entire Extension process. R23's "NEW VECTOR CANDIDATE" (FR-196 basis) is architecturally impossible. The `StatusRecoverableError` mechanism is voluntary component status reporting, not panic recovery.
2. **CRITICAL**: `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` environment variable does NOT EXIST — GitHub-wide code search returned zero results across all ADOT and OTel Lambda repositories. The 2s extension shutdown window is a Lambda platform constraint (enforced via SIGKILL), not configurable by the Extension. Spec referenced a non-existent configuration mechanism.
3. **HIGH**: ADOT Lambda Extension has ZERO span processors — `aws-otel-lambda/adot/collector/lambdacomponents/default.go` confirms only receivers, exporters, and extensions. All span processing (PII filtering FR-191, allow-listing, annotation budgeting FR-193) MUST happen in the Python SDK. ADOT is a pass-through exporter only.
4. **HIGH**: New span-loss vector identified — ADOT exporter backend error degraded state. X-Ray API returns persistent 429/500, exporter retries exhaust `max_elapsed_time`, spans dropped. Extension stays alive (responds to lifecycle events) but exported span count drops to near-zero.
5. **HIGH**: Requirements checklist tracks only 44% of spec requirements — 70/199 FRs and 63/143 SCs have tracking rows. ~169 requirements have no checkbox. Cannot serve as implementation source of truth.
6. **MEDIUM**: Span-loss vector catalog requires correction — "recovered panic" candidate must be retired (DENIED), replaced by "exporter backend errors" vector.
7. **MEDIUM**: Lambda platform 2s shutdown window is a hard constraint — all flush timing calculations must reference Lambda Extensions API documentation, not non-existent env vars. Impacts FR-062, FR-063, FR-068.
8. **MEDIUM**: Component Coverage Map in HL checklist stale — stops at R14 detail, R15-R23 additions not mapped in Component Coverage Map table.
9. **LOW**: ADOT vs upstream OTel Lambda component divergence — ADOT strips all 9 processors from upstream. `decouple` processor (improves span retention during Extension shutdown) not available. `aws-otel-lambda#842` tracks this as feature request.
10. **LOW**: `StatusRecoverableError` vs `recover()` confusion — OTel Collector has voluntary component-level status reporting mechanism (`component/componentstatus/status.go`), not Go panic recovery. Spec must distinguish these clearly.

**3 Confirmed Non-Risks (Investigated and Dismissed)**:
1. SendGrid HTTP tracing uncertainty — CONFIRMED WORKING. `python_http_client` → `urllib.request` → `http.client`. X-Ray `patch(['httplib'])` instruments this path. OTel `URLLibInstrumentor` also works. No uncertainty remains.
2. SNS cross-Lambda trace propagation — CONFIRMED AUTOMATIC via `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute when Active Tracing enabled. No manual `MessageAttributes` needed. Caveat: `rawMessageDelivery: true` breaks it (already in FR-137).
3. ADOT recovered panic as distinct span-loss vector — DENIED. Panics crash the entire Extension process. Identical to span-loss vector #3 (crash, FR-167), not a distinct vector.

**ADOT Recovered Panic Vector Retirement (Round 24 — Amendment)**

- **FR-200** (P0 — CRITICAL): FR-196's ADOT Extension degraded state detection MUST be amended. The "recovered panic" scenario documented in Round 23 is DENIED — OTel Collector does NOT use `recover()` in pipeline goroutines (`exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go` has no `recover()` wrapper). A panic in any exporter goroutine crashes the entire Collector process and therefore the entire ADOT Extension. This makes "recovered panic" identical to span-loss vector #3 (ADOT Extension crash, FR-167), not a distinct vector. FR-196's detection mechanism (canary detects Extension alive but not exporting) remains valid but MUST be reframed: the degraded state occurs when the ADOT exporter enters retry exhaustion due to persistent X-Ray API errors (429/500), NOT from recovered panics. The health probe mechanism (empty OTLP request to `:4318`) still detects this — a healthy receiver with a degraded exporter returns HTTP 200 for the OTLP request but silently drops spans downstream. Source: `opentelemetry-collector` `exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go` — consumer goroutines have no `recover()` wrapper; panics propagate to the process level.

**ADOT Exporter Backend Error Span-Loss Vector (Round 24 — New)**

- **FR-201** (P1 — HIGH): A NEW span-loss vector MUST be catalogued: **Vector #4 — ADOT exporter backend error degraded state**. ADOT Extension remains alive (responding to Extensions API lifecycle events) but its exporter component drops spans due to persistent X-Ray API errors. Mechanism: (a) X-Ray PutTraceSegments returns 429 (rate limit) or 5xx (server error); (b) OTel Collector `exporterhelper` retries per its `retry_on_failure` configuration (default: enabled, exponential backoff, `max_elapsed_time: 300s`); (c) during Lambda execution, retry exhaustion causes the `exporterqueue` to drop spans when queue capacity is reached; (d) during Lambda shutdown, the 2s platform window truncates retry attempts; (e) Extension process remains alive — it responds to INVOKE/SHUTDOWN lifecycle events — but exported span count drops to near-zero. Detection: canary observes sustained trace loss with Extension alive (same mechanism as FR-196, root cause is backend errors). Distinguishing from vector #1 (drop race, ~30%): sustained near-100% loss rate vs intermittent partial loss. Distinguishing from vector #3 (crash): Extension process alive vs terminated. Source: OTel Collector `exporterhelper` `retry_sender.go` — retry configuration; AWS X-Ray PutTraceSegments API — throttling behavior.

**Lambda Platform Shutdown Window Constraint Documentation (Round 24 — Amendment)**

- **FR-202** (P1 — HIGH): All spec references to the non-existent `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` environment variable MUST be corrected. The Extension shutdown window is a Lambda platform constraint: (a) Lambda sends SHUTDOWN event to registered Extensions; (b) Extensions have up to **2 seconds** to complete cleanup (including `force_flush()` and OTLP export); (c) this 2-second window is NOT configurable by the Extension — it is a Lambda platform enforcement via SIGKILL; (d) the OTel Collector's internal `shutdown_timeout` configuration (default 5s) is truncated to the Lambda platform's 2s window; (e) FR-062 and FR-063's flush timing calculations MUST reference the Lambda Extensions API shutdown phase documentation, not `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT`. The only environment variables for ADOT collector configuration are `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_URI` (custom config path) and deprecated `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE`. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API documentation — "After the runtime responds to the shutdown event, or if the Extensions API does not receive a response, Lambda sends a SIGKILL to each extension after 2 seconds."

**ADOT Zero-Processor Architecture Documentation (Round 24 — New)**

- **FR-203** (P1 — HIGH): The spec MUST explicitly document that the ADOT Lambda Extension includes ZERO span processors. The Extension's collector binary contains only: receivers (`otlpreceiver`), exporters (`awsxrayexporter`, `awsemfexporter`, `prometheusremotewriteexporter`, `debugexporter`, `otlpexporter`, `otlphttpexporter`), and extensions (`sigv4authextension`). Implications: (a) all span processing — attribute allow-listing (FR-191), SpanProcessor ordering (FR-192), annotation budgeting (FR-193), PII filtering — MUST occur in the Python SDK's `TracerProvider` SpanProcessor chain; (b) the ADOT Extension is a pass-through exporter; no server-side filtering, redaction, or attribute manipulation is possible; (c) the upstream OTel Lambda layer (`open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda`) includes 9 processors (including `attributesprocessor`, `filterprocessor`, `batchprocessor`) — ADOT's fork strips all of them; (d) `aws-otel-lambda#842` is an open feature request to add the `decouple` processor to ADOT (which improves span retention during Extension shutdown). This is an architectural constraint, not a bug — ADOT prioritizes layer size and startup latency over processing flexibility. Source: `aws-otel-lambda/adot/collector/lambdacomponents/default.go` — `otelcol.Factories` struct with zero `Processors` entries.

**Requirements Checklist Completeness (Round 24 — New)**

- **FR-204** (P2 — MEDIUM): The requirements checklist (`specs/1219-xray-exclusive-tracing/checklists/requirements.md`) MUST contain tracking rows for ALL FRs and SCs defined in the spec. Current state: 70/199+ FRs and 63/143+ SCs have tracking rows (~44% coverage). Missing rows: R1-R9 FRs (FR-001 through FR-084 except 5), R13-R16 FRs and SCs, R18 FRs and SCs. Target: 100% of spec FRs and SCs have a tracking row with checkbox. Superseded FRs (e.g., those amended in later rounds) MUST be tracked with `[SUPERSEDED by FR-NNN]` annotation rather than removed. This ensures the checklist serves as the single source of truth for implementation status. Source: Process requirement — specification traceability.

**Ingestion/Bucket Write Trace Annotations (Round 25 Clarification — New)**

- **FR-205** (P1 — HIGH): The Analysis Lambda (which performs the time-series fanout, NOT the Ingestion Lambda — Ingestion fetches articles and publishes to SNS, Analysis receives via SNS and writes buckets) MUST create a subsegment for each ticker price or sentiment batch write to DynamoDB time-based buckets, annotated with: `ticker_symbol` (string), `failed_buckets` (string, comma-separated resolution names that failed after all retries exhausted, empty string if none — e.g., `"1h,3h"`; count is derived from the string), and `ingestion_duration_ms` (int, wall-clock milliseconds for the complete bucket write operation). A bucket is "failed" ONLY when all retries are exhausted and the data was NOT written — retried-then-succeeded counts as success. Transient DynamoDB throttling that resolves on retry is visible via DynamoDB's `ThrottledRequests` CloudWatch metric, not this annotation. The raw duration annotation enables query-time threshold filtering (e.g., `annotation.ingestion_duration_ms > 500`) without baking a threshold at write time — operators can tighten thresholds as traffic patterns emerge without redeployment. No `is_slow` boolean — threshold judgment belongs at query time, not write time, to avoid historical discontinuities when thresholds change. Source: Clarification session 2026-03-09/2026-03-10 — under-specified ingestion write path trace annotations and latency observability.

**Canary API Gateway Subsegment Completeness Validation (Round 25 Clarification — New)**

- **FR-207** (P1 — HIGH): The observability canary (FR-019/FR-096) MUST include a synthetic health-check request through API Gateway to the Dashboard Lambda, then validate the resulting trace contains BOTH the API Gateway segment AND the expected Dashboard Lambda subsegments with annotations. Currently the canary only tests its own EventBridge-triggered traces, which cannot detect ADOT Extension failures on the Dashboard Lambda — the sole API Gateway-fronted Lambda. When ADOT crashes on the Dashboard Lambda (span-loss vector #3), API Gateway's own X-Ray segment still arrives in X-Ray, masking the Lambda-side failure. The canary MUST: (a) issue an HTTP request to a dedicated `/api/v2/health` endpoint on the Dashboard Lambda via API Gateway, (b) query X-Ray for the resulting trace using `GetTraceSummaries` with the trace ID from the response `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header, (c) validate that the trace contains at minimum: 1 API Gateway segment + 1 Lambda segment + >=1 DynamoDB subsegment (per FR-152's expected segment counts for Dashboard Lambda), (d) if subsegment validation fails for 2 consecutive canary intervals, fire a dedicated `CanarySubsegmentIncomplete` CloudWatch alarm. This detects the specific failure mode where traces appear "present" but are structurally incomplete due to Lambda-side ADOT failure. Source: Clarification session 2026-03-10 — canary blind spot for API Gateway-fronted trace completeness.

**Analysis Lambda Deadline-Aware Flush (Round 25 Clarification — New)**

- **FR-206** (P1 — HIGH): The Analysis Lambda MUST implement deadline-aware `force_flush()` between sequential time-series bucket writes. The Analysis Lambda performs up to 32 sequential `update_item` calls per ticker (8 resolutions × 4 conditional updates each), multiplied by ticker count. Under DynamoDB throttling, this sequential path can approach the 60s Lambda timeout. Lambda timeout triggers SIGKILL — `finally` blocks do NOT execute, and all buffered spans (including FR-205 annotations) are permanently lost. The Analysis Lambda MUST check `context.get_remaining_time_in_millis()` after each resolution's update batch (i.e., between each of the 8 resolution iterations). If remaining time falls below a configurable threshold (default: 5000ms), the Lambda MUST: (a) call `TracerProvider.force_flush()` to export all buffered spans, (b) annotate the current subsegment with `flush_reason = "deadline"` and `resolutions_completed` (int, count of resolutions written before flush), (c) return early, reporting incomplete writes via FR-205's `buckets_failed` and `failed_buckets` annotations. The bucket writes remain sequential — parallelization was considered but rejected due to OTel `threading.local()` context propagation breakage requiring explicit context attachment per thread. Source: Clarification session 2026-03-10 — Analysis Lambda timeout risk on sequential bucket update path; FR-093 precedent for SSE Lambda deadline-aware flush.

### Key Entities

- **X-Ray Trace**: A distributed trace spanning one or more service components, identified by a trace ID in the format `1-{hex_timestamp}-{24_hex_digits}`. Propagated via the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header.
- **X-Ray Subsegment**: A named, timed span within a trace representing a discrete operation (e.g., a DynamoDB query, a connection acquisition). Can carry annotations (indexed, searchable key-value pairs) and metadata (non-indexed structured data).
- **X-Ray Annotation**: An indexed key-value pair attached to a subsegment. Annotations are searchable in the X-Ray console and API, making them the primary mechanism for filtering traces by business attributes (e.g., `event_type = "bucket_update"`, `cache_hit_rate = 0.85`).
- **X-Ray Canary**: A scheduled probe that validates X-Ray ingestion health and data integrity by submitting and querying test traces, reporting results via a separate (non-X-Ray) channel.
- **X-Ray Group**: A filtered view of traces defined by a filter expression (e.g., `fault = true`). Groups automatically generate CloudWatch metrics, enabling alarm-based monitoring from trace data without manual metric emission.
- **X-Ray Sampling Rule**: A server-side configuration that controls which requests are traced. Rules specify a reservoir (guaranteed minimum per second) and a fixed rate (percentage of additional requests). Rules are evaluated by priority (lowest number first).

## Assumptions

- ~~The X-Ray SDK auto-patches HTTP client libraries including the one used by the SendGrid SDK.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 2**: The SendGrid SDK uses `python-http-client` which uses Python's stdlib `urllib.request`. The X-Ray SDK does NOT auto-patch `urllib`. SendGrid HTTP calls require explicit X-Ray subsegments (see FR-028).
- The existing CloudWatch RUM configuration (`enable_xray = true`) already generates browser-side X-Ray trace contexts. The frontend needs to extract and propagate these, not generate new ones. CloudWatch RUM's web client auto-injects `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` headers on `fetch()` calls when `addXRayTraceIdHeader: true` is configured in the http telemetry options.
- When both the publishing and subscribing Lambda functions have Active X-Ray tracing enabled, AWS automatically propagates trace context through SNS via the `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute. No manual MessageAttributes configuration is needed for cross-Lambda trace linking.
- Auto-instrumentation patches all supported AWS SDK calls (DynamoDB, SNS, CloudWatch, etc.) transparently. Explicit subsegments are needed only for business logic operations not covered by auto-patching.
- The X-Ray canary's query latency window (time between trace submission and retrievability) is typically 5-30 seconds due to X-Ray's eventual consistency model.
- Standard AWS managed policies for X-Ray provide sufficient permissions for Lambda trace emission and telemetry reporting.
- ~~The X-Ray SDK's `xray_recorder.begin_segment()` API can create independent segments outside the Lambda runtime's auto-created segment. These segments can carry a specified trace ID to link them to the original invocation, appearing as part of the same distributed trace.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 3**: `begin_segment()` is a documented no-op in Lambda. The SDK's `LambdaContext.put_segment()` silently discards segments with a log warning (source: `aws_xray_sdk/core/lambda_launcher.py:55-59`). The `FacadeSegment` raises `FacadeSegmentMutationException` on all mutation operations including `close()`, `put_annotation()`, `put_metadata()`, `set_aws()`, `add_exception()`, and `serialize()`. Additionally, the X-Ray daemon within the Lambda execution environment may begin shutting down after the handler returns in `RESPONSE_STREAM` mode, making even raw UDP emission unreliable. **Replacement**: The SSE Lambda uses a Lambda Extension-based tracing mechanism (e.g., ADOT — AWS Distro for OpenTelemetry) that runs as a separate process with its own lifecycle. Lambda Extensions receive INIT, INVOKE, and SHUTDOWN lifecycle events and continue running after the handler returns. The extension accepts trace spans via local OTLP endpoint and exports to X-Ray, providing trace data emission during response streaming without depending on the X-Ray SDK's LambdaContext.
- **(Round 2)** The X-Ray SDK supports `str`, `int`, `float`, and `bool` annotation types. All annotations defined in this spec use these types. `None` values are silently dropped, so annotations MUST use explicit sentinel values or be omitted when the value is unavailable.
- **(Round 2)** Adding Powertools Tracer as a dependency to all non-streaming Lambda containers adds approximately 5-10MB to the deployment package and 50-100ms to cold start. This is acceptable given that the Lambdas already include the aws-xray-sdk dependency.
- **(Round 3)** The `EventSource` browser API does not support custom HTTP headers. This is defined in the WHATWG HTML Living Standard, Section 9.2. The constructor signature is `EventSource(url, eventSourceInitDict)` where `eventSourceInitDict` only supports `withCredentials: boolean`. CloudWatch RUM's automatic trace header injection patches `window.fetch()` and `XMLHttpRequest.prototype.open` but does NOT patch `EventSource`. Trace propagation for SSE connections requires using `fetch()` + `ReadableStream` instead.
- **(Round 3)** Adding the ADOT Lambda Extension to the SSE Lambda adds approximately 40-60MB to the execution environment and 50-200ms to cold start (runs concurrently with Lambda INIT, partially masking overhead). The extension provides an OTLP receiver on localhost that accepts trace spans independently of the X-Ray SDK lifecycle.
- **(Round 3)** X-Ray's region-level throughput limit is 2,600 segments per second. Beyond this, `PutTraceSegments` returns `ThrottledException` and affected segments are listed in `UnprocessedTraceSegments` — data is permanently lost, not queued. The X-Ray daemon provides batching and burst capacity but cannot sustain above-limit throughput.
- **(Round 3)** The default `threading.local()` context storage used by the X-Ray SDK correctly propagates across `asyncio.new_event_loop().run_until_complete()` boundaries when called from the same thread. This is because `run_until_complete()` executes coroutines on the calling thread. The X-Ray SDK's `AsyncContext` alternative uses `TaskLocalStorage`, which is scoped to `asyncio.Task` objects and does NOT propagate across event loop boundaries.
- **(Round 3)** At current traffic levels (<1M requests/month), 100% X-Ray sampling costs less than $5/month, well within the cost guard thresholds. The free tier covers the first 100,000 traces recorded per month.
- **(Round 4)** CloudFront is not in the current architecture — removed in Features 1203-1207. Browser-to-backend trace propagation via `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` headers reaches API Gateway and Lambda Function URLs directly without intermediary header manipulation. CloudFront treats `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` as a restricted header and replaces client-sent values with its own; re-introducing CloudFront would break browser-originated trace propagation (see edge case).
- **(Round 4)** ADOT Lambda Extension in "sidecar-only" mode (OTLP receiver without auto-instrumentation) does not conflict with Powertools Tracer or the X-Ray SDK. Conflicts arise only when ADOT auto-instrumentation is enabled via the `AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER` environment variable, which activates handler wrapping (`AwsLambdaInstrumentor`) and botocore patching (`BotocoreInstrumentor`).
- **(Round 4)** CloudWatch metric ingestion delay (time between `put_metric_data` and metric availability via `get_metric_statistics`) is typically 60-120 seconds. The canary's CloudWatch health check query window must account for this delay. Source: AWS CloudWatch API documentation.
- **(Round 4)** At current traffic levels with 100% X-Ray sampling, the gap between X-Ray trace availability and CloudWatch metric availability for error detection is effectively zero — every error has both an X-Ray trace and a CloudWatch metric. The dual-instrumentation requirement for silent failure paths (FR-043) provides insurance for the future when production sampling may be reduced below 100%.
- **(Round 5)** The OTel `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator` reads the `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` Lambda environment variable and extracts `Root` (trace ID), `Parent` (span ID), and `Sampled` (sampling decision) into the OTel context. This provides the bridge between the Lambda runtime's X-Ray trace and the OTel SDK's span hierarchy. When combined with `parentbased_always_on` sampler, the OTel SDK honors the Lambda runtime's sampling decision. Source: `opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray` package, PyPI.
- ~~**(Round 5)** The OTel `BatchSpanProcessor`'s default batch timeout of 200ms means streaming-phase spans are exported to the ADOT Extension incrementally during the 15-second streaming lifecycle. The `force_flush()` call at end of generator handles only the final partial batch (spans created in the last <200ms before generator exhaustion). The flush target is localhost (ADOT Extension), not remote X-Ray API.~~ **CORRECTED in Round 9**: The actual `BatchSpanProcessor` `schedule_delay_millis` default is **5000ms** (5 seconds), NOT 200ms. FR-073 overrides to 1000ms, making the corrected statement: "With FR-073's tuned 1000ms schedule delay, streaming-phase spans are exported approximately every 1 second. The `force_flush()` call at end of generator handles the final partial batch (spans created in the last <1000ms before generator exhaustion)." The original 200ms figure was incorrect and caused downstream reasoning errors about the flush window. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 — `BatchSpanProcessor` default `schedule_delay_millis=5000`; OTel Specification, BatchSpanProcessor section.
- **(Round 5)** The ADOT Extension layer in sidecar-only mode (no `AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER`, OTLP receiver only) is approximately 35-45MB unzipped. The additional OTel Python SDK packages (FR-057) add approximately 5-10MB. Combined with the SSE Lambda's existing deployment package, the total remains well within the 250MB Lambda deployment limit.
- **(Round 5)** The X-Ray `PutTraceSegments` API rejects segment documents exceeding 64KB. The X-Ray SDK and OTel SDK both mitigate this by emitting completed subsegments/spans as independent documents, but individual documents with large metadata can still exceed the limit. The 50-annotation-per-subsegment limit (2,048 chars each) produces ~100KB of annotation data at maximum, which exceeds 64KB — in practice, annotations are small (typically <50 chars each), keeping documents well under the limit.
- **(Round 6)** The `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` environment variable is updated by the Lambda runtime at the start of each invocation and remains stable for the duration of that invocation. `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator.extract()` reads `os.environ.get("_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID")` on each call with no internal caching. Module-level extraction captures only the INIT-phase value, which becomes stale on warm invocations.
- ~~**(Round 6)** The SSE Lambda's current memory allocation of 512MB provides sufficient headroom for the ADOT Extension (~40-60MB) plus OTel SDK packages (~5-10MB). No memory increase is required. Source: Terraform `infrastructure/terraform/main.tf` — `memory_size = 512`.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 12**: See FR-102. Memory increase to 1024MB required. ADOT Extension (~50MB) + OTel SDK (~30MB) + runtime (~100MB) + application (~150MB) = ~330MB baseline leaves insufficient headroom at 512MB. Source: AWS Lambda performance benchmarks.
- ~~**(Round 6)** The Lambda RESPONSE_STREAM runtime calls the generator's `.close()` method or propagates `BrokenPipeError` when the client disconnects mid-stream, ensuring the generator's `finally` block executes reliably. The `finally` block is NOT deferred to garbage collection.~~ **PARTIALLY INVALIDATED in Round 11**: This assumption is CORRECT for client disconnect (BrokenPipeError is raised, generator `.close()` is called, `finally` block executes) but INCORRECT for Lambda timeout. Lambda does NOT send SIGTERM to the custom runtime process on timeout — the process is killed directly (SIGKILL after Extension Shutdown phase). Python `finally` blocks do NOT execute on SIGKILL. FR-055's `force_flush()` in the `finally` block handles normal completion and client disconnect but NOT Lambda timeout. FR-093 adds proactive deadline-aware flush to cover the timeout path. Source: AWS Lambda Runtime Environment Lifecycle — Extensions receive Shutdown event with `shutdownReason: "TIMEOUT"`; runtime process is terminated.
- **(Round 6)** Powertools Tracer's `auto_patch=True` patches `botocore.client.BaseClient._make_api_call` at module import time. These patches are global (not scoped to the handler phase) and remain active during the streaming phase. The X-Ray daemon's ability to accept subsegments created by auto-patched calls during RESPONSE_STREAM streaming is undocumented by AWS and may be unreliable — the daemon process lifecycle after handler return is not guaranteed.
- **(Round 7)** The ADOT Lambda Extension's default collector configuration for Lambda includes an OTLP HTTP receiver on port 4318 and an AWS X-Ray exporter pipeline. In sidecar-only mode (no `AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER`), the collector receives OTel spans via OTLP and exports them to X-Ray without any auto-instrumentation. If the default config includes extraneous components, a custom `collector.yaml` is required. Source: ADOT Lambda Extension GitHub repository — `adot/collector/config.yaml`.
- ~~**(Round 7)** The SSE Lambda currently uses zero Lambda layers (S3-packaged deployment). Adding 1 ADOT Extension layer is well within the 5-layer Lambda limit. The combined unzipped size (Lambda package + ADOT collector-only layer ~35MB) remains within the 250MB Lambda deployment limit. Source: AWS Lambda quotas — 5 layers per function, 250MB unzipped deployment limit.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 8**: The SSE Lambda is container-based (ECR image with `python:3.13-slim` + custom bootstrap), NOT ZIP-deployed. Lambda container images CANNOT use Lambda Layers (source: AWS Lambda Container Image docs — "You cannot add Lambda layers to container images"). ADOT is embedded in the container image via multi-stage Dockerfile build. Container images have a 10GB size limit, not 250MB. The 5-layer limit is irrelevant.
- **(Round 7)** The X-Ray daemon process (~16MB) and ADOT Lambda Extension (~40-60MB) coexist within the SSE Lambda's 512MB memory allocation. Combined tracing infrastructure overhead is ~76MB (15% of total), leaving ~436MB for the Python runtime and application code. This is validated against the current SSE Lambda memory usage. Source: Terraform `infrastructure/terraform/main.tf` — SSE Lambda `memory_size = 512`, zero layers currently.
- **(Round 7)** The OTel Python SDK's `BatchSpanProcessor` spawns one daemon thread per instantiation. Module-level `TracerProvider` instantiation creates exactly one thread for the lifetime of the execution environment. Repeated instantiation without `shutdown()` orphans daemon threads (~1MB each), causing monotonic memory growth. Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor.__init__()` starts `threading.Thread(daemon=True)`.
- **(Round 7)** The `set_global_textmap()` function in the OTel Python SDK unconditionally overwrites the global propagator, including any propagator loaded from the `OTEL_PROPAGATORS` environment variable at import time. The env var sets the initial default; `set_global_textmap()` is effective at any subsequent call. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 — `opentelemetry/propagate/__init__.py`.
- **(Round 8)** The SSE Lambda is container-based, using `python:3.13-slim` as its base image with a custom `bootstrap` script that implements the Lambda Runtime API for RESPONSE_STREAM mode. Lambda Extensions (including ADOT) are Lambda service-level features, not runtime-level — they are discovered by scanning `/opt/extensions/` during INIT and launched as separate processes. The ADOT Extension registers with the Extensions API (`/2020-01-01/extension/register`) independently of the custom runtime. No bootstrap modifications are needed. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API documentation.
- **(Round 8)** AWS publishes ADOT Lambda Extension images on the public ECR gallery at `public.ecr.aws/aws-observability/`. The multi-stage Dockerfile pattern `COPY --from=adot-image /opt/extensions/ /opt/extensions/` extracts the collector binary. Image tags must be digest-pinned (`@sha256:...`) for reproducible builds. Source: ECR Public Gallery — AWS Observability.
- **(Round 8)** The OTel `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` (from `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws`) reads `AWS_LAMBDA_FUNCTION_NAME`, `AWS_LAMBDA_FUNCTION_VERSION`, `AWS_REGION`, `AWS_LAMBDA_LOG_STREAM_NAME`, and `AWS_LAMBDA_FUNCTION_MEMORY_SIZE` environment variables. These are set by the Lambda service regardless of base image. The detector sets `cloud.provider`, `cloud.platform`, `cloud.region`, `faas.name`, `faas.version`, `faas.instance`, and `faas.max_memory` — but does NOT set `service.name`. Without explicit `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`, the default is `unknown_service`. Source: `opentelemetry-python-contrib` — `sdk-extension/opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws/src/opentelemetry/sdk/extension/aws/resource/_lambda.py`.
- **(Round 8)** The OTel `BatchSpanProcessor` default configuration (`schedule_delay_millis=5000`, `max_queue_size=2048`, `max_export_batch_size=512`) is designed for long-running server processes, not Lambda. For the SSE Lambda (900s streaming), the 5s delay is functionally acceptable since `force_flush()` drains the entire queue synchronously. However, reduced defaults (`schedule_delay_millis=1000`, `max_queue_size=256`, `max_export_batch_size=64`) consume less memory and export more frequently, reducing the risk of data loss if `force_flush()` is not reached. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 — `BatchSpanProcessor` defaults and `OTEL_BSP_*` env vars.
- **(Round 9)** The ADOT Lambda Extension's decouple processor (Lambda-specific batch processor) decouples span reception from export, preventing the Extension from signaling invocation completion until all queued spans are exported to the X-Ray backend. This is the accepted mitigation for the known span drop race condition (aws-otel-lambda#886). The decouple processor is included in the ADOT Extension's default Lambda configuration. Source: https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda/blob/main/collector/processor/decoupleprocessor/README.md
- **(Round 9)** The `TracerProvider(shutdown_on_exit=False)` parameter prevents Python `atexit` handler registration. In Lambda, the `atexit` handler is redundant because FR-055 mandates `force_flush()` at end of each streaming session, and the ADOT Extension has its own SHUTDOWN phase for final export. Disabling `atexit` eliminates the thread pool shutdown race (opentelemetry-python#4461) with zero functional impact.
- **(Round 9)** X-Ray trace propagation delay (time between `PutTraceSegments` and availability via `BatchGetTraces`) is documented as "generally 30 seconds" in the AWS FAQ. This is eventual consistency, NOT a deterministic SLA. Under regional load or during X-Ray service degradation, delay may exceed 30 seconds. The canary's retry-with-backoff (30s then 60s per FR-078) accounts for this variability.
- **(Round 9)** CloudWatch `put_metric_data` error codes fall into two categories: (a) transient/retryable: `ThrottlingException`, `InternalFailure`, `ServiceUnavailable`, `InternalServiceError`; (b) permanent/IAM: `AccessDeniedException`, `NotAuthorized`, `InvalidClientTokenId`. The boto3 SDK raises `botocore.exceptions.ClientError` with error code accessible via `error.response['Error']['Code']`. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/APIReference/CommonErrors.html
- **(Round 9)** The SSE Lambda's event stream format uses `id:` fields in SSE frames, enabling `Last-Event-ID` based resumption per the SSE protocol specification. If the current SSE Lambda does not emit `id:` fields, FR-081's server-side support requires adding them. The `id:` value must be monotonically increasing or otherwise orderable to support "resume from position" semantics.
- **(Round 9)** The `ReadableStreamDefaultReader.closed` Promise is supported in all modern browsers (Chrome 78+, Firefox 65+, Safari 10.1+) and is the canonical mechanism for detecting stream close type. Source: MDN Web Docs — ReadableStreamDefaultReader.closed.
- ~~**(Round 5)** The OTel `BatchSpanProcessor`'s default batch timeout is 200ms.~~ **CORRECTED in Round 9 (FR-084)**: The actual default `schedule_delay_millis` is 5000ms (5 seconds). FR-073 overrides to 1000ms. The original 200ms figure was incorrect. Source: OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 source code; OTel Specification, BatchSpanProcessor defaults.
- **(Round 10)** AWS is rolling out a new Lambda X-Ray segment format that eliminates the Invocation subsegment and uses `aws.responseLatency`/`aws.responseDuration` annotations on the function segment. Customer subsegments attach directly to `AWS::Lambda::Function` segment instead of the Invocation subsegment. OTel span parenting via `AwsXRayLambdaPropagator` is format-independent because it reads `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` which provides trace context regardless of segment format. Powertools Tracer subsegments may attach to a different parent under the new format, but this affects only handler-phase cosmetics in the X-Ray console — not trace correctness. No spec changes required; this assumption documents awareness. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/services-xray.html
- **(Round 10)** The SSE Lambda MUST NOT be deployed in a VPC when using Function URL response streaming. AWS docs confirm: "Function URLs do not support response streaming in VPC environments, but invoking functions using the InvokeWithResponseStream API is supported." If deployed in a VPC, responses are silently buffered instead of streamed — no error, no warning, just degraded behavior. The current architecture uses DynamoDB (public endpoint via AWS SDK), so VPC is not needed. If VPC access is required in the future (e.g., VPC-only RDS or ElastiCache), the SSE Lambda must either (a) remain non-VPC and access VPC resources via VPC endpoints or PrivateLink, or (b) be invoked via SDK `InvokeWithResponseStream` from a non-VPC intermediary Lambda with a Function URL. Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/configuration-response-streaming.html
- **(Round 10)** The project's span-per-poll-cycle convention for SSE streaming instrumentation (FR-025/FR-026: one parent span per DynamoDB poll cycle, child spans for db query + event dispatch + metric emit) is project-specific and NOT aligned with any OTel semantic convention — because none exists. The OTel specification's section on streaming instrumentation for GenAI spans explicitly says "TODO" (no span-per-event vs span-per-connection convention defined). When OTel publishes streaming semantic conventions, the project SHOULD evaluate alignment and migrate if feasible. Until then, the current convention is the best-available approach. Source: https://opentelemetry.io/docs/specs/semconv/gen-ai/gen-ai-spans/
- **(Round 10)** AWS Lambda response streaming supports only Node.js managed runtimes and custom runtimes. The Python managed runtime (`python3.x`) does NOT support response streaming — `InvokeMode: RESPONSE_STREAM` returns buffered responses identical to `BUFFERED` mode. The SSE Lambda uses `python:3.13-slim` with a custom `bootstrap` script, which IS a custom runtime. This is the architectural reason the SSE Lambda requires container-based deployment with a custom bootstrap (not just for ADOT embedding). Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/configuration-response-streaming.html — "Response streaming currently supports the Node.js managed runtimes and custom runtimes."
- **(Round 8 AMENDED in Round 10)** ~~FR-073's `max_queue_size=256` provides sufficient headroom for the SSE Lambda's span throughput.~~ **CORRECTED in Round 10 (FR-086)**: The original `max_queue_size=512` (updated from 256 in an earlier round) is INSUFFICIENT. Recalculation: 15s stream × 15 polls/s × 3 spans/poll = ~675 spans/invocation. FR-086 amends to `max_queue_size=1500` (>= 2x expected throughput). Source: OTel Python SDK — `BatchSpanProcessor.on_end()` silent drop on queue full.
- **(Round 11)** The OTel Python SDK (v1.39.1) is fully compatible with Python 3.13. All 4 FR-057 packages (`opentelemetry-sdk`, `opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http`, `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws`, `opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray`) have explicit Python 3.13 PyPI classifiers, zero deprecation warnings, and work correctly with the standard GIL-enabled Python 3.13 build. Free-threading (PEP 703) is NOT enabled in `python:3.13-slim`. Source: PyPI package metadata classifiers; runtime import verification.
- **(Round 11)** API Gateway with X-Ray tracing enabled makes its own sampling decision regardless of client-supplied `Sampled=1` in the incoming `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. Lambda Function URLs do NOT have this behavior — they honor the incoming `Sampled` field directly. The asymmetry means FR-035's server-side sampling override works for API Gateway paths but not for Function URL paths. Source: API Gateway X-Ray integration documentation.
- **(Round 11)** The ADOT Lambda Extension's embedded default configuration (used when `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` is not set) includes the decouple processor, OTLP HTTP receiver on port 4318, and AWS X-Ray exporter. However, it also includes unnecessary components (gRPC receiver, potentially metrics pipeline) that consume ~15MB of extra memory. The Extension does NOT auto-discover config files at filesystem paths — it reads the path exclusively from the `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE` environment variable. Source: ADOT Lambda Extension GitHub repository — `collector/lambdacomponents/default.go`.
- **(Round 11)** The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap at `src/lambdas/sse_streaming/bootstrap` reads `Lambda-Runtime-Aws-Request-Id` from the Runtime API `/runtime/invocation/next` response but does NOT read `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id`. On cold start, the Lambda service sets `_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID` in the process environment. On warm invocations, the env var retains the cold start value unless the bootstrap explicitly updates it. This is confirmed by code inspection (lines 39-51 of the bootstrap). Source: AWS Lambda Custom Runtime Contract; project source code.
- ~~**(Round 6)** The SSE Lambda's current memory allocation of 512MB provides sufficient headroom for the ADOT Extension (~40-60MB) plus OTel SDK packages (~5-10MB). No memory increase is required. Source: Terraform `infrastructure/terraform/main.tf` — `memory_size = 512`.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 12**: ADOT Extension consumes ~50MB resident memory, OTel SDK packages add ~30MB import overhead, Python 3.13 runtime requires ~100MB, and application code + dependencies require ~100-150MB. Total baseline of ~350-400MB leaves only ~110-160MB headroom at 512MB — insufficient for burst allocations. Additionally, Lambda CPU scales linearly with memory; at 512MB, cold start is ~1200ms vs ~800ms at 1024MB. FR-102 increases memory to 1024MB. Source: AWS Lambda performance benchmarks; ADOT Lambda Extension documentation.
- **(Round 12)** Concurrent Lambda invocations each get their own isolated execution environment (Firecracker microVM) with their own ADOT Extension process. Lambda guarantees at most one concurrent invocation per execution environment. The OTLP receiver on `localhost:4318` is per-environment (each has its own network namespace). Zero risk of cross-invocation span corruption from concurrency. Sequential warm invocations on the same environment share the Extension process but are serialized — never concurrent. Source: AWS Lambda Execution Environment lifecycle documentation.
- **(Round 12)** The ADOT Extension receives a Shutdown event on Lambda timeout with `shutdownReason: "timeout"` and a 2000ms grace period, even though the runtime process is SIGKILL'd. This means already-received spans (those that completed Hop 1: SDK→Extension) CAN be exported to X-Ray during the Extension's Shutdown phase. Spans still in the BSP queue (Hop 1 not started) are permanently lost because the runtime is dead. FR-093's proactive flush ensures Hop 1 completes before timeout. FR-100's graceful termination converts the timeout into a normal completion, providing an even more reliable Shutdown. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — Shutdown event lifecycle.
- **(Round 12)** OTel Python core packages enforce lockstep versioning via internal `==` dependency pins. `opentelemetry-sdk` hard-pins `opentelemetry-api==<exact-version>`. The pip resolver prevents installation of mismatched core packages (build fails with `ResolutionImpossible`). AWS contrib packages (`opentelemetry-propagator-aws-xray`, `opentelemetry-sdk-extension-aws`) use wide `~=1.12` pins against core, allowing any core version >= 1.12. Source: PyPI package metadata; pip resolver behavior.
- **(Round 12)** The OTLP v1 protocol (proto path: `opentelemetry.proto.collector.trace.v1`) is stable and backward-compatible between OTel Python SDK 1.25+ through 1.39.1 and ADOT Collector versions since v0.21.0 (mid-2022). Version skew between the OTel SDK OTLP exporter and the ADOT collector at the protocol level is not a risk. Source: OTel proto v1.0.0 specification.
- **(Round 12)** SSE Lambda memory increase from 512MB to 1024MB costs approximately $2-3/month additional at current invocation patterns (~8,000 invocations/month × 15s average duration). This is well within the FR-038 cost alarm threshold of $10. Source: AWS Lambda pricing — $0.0000166667/GB-second.
- **(Round 12)** The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap currently passes `None` for the Lambda context parameter: `handler(event_data, None)`. The standard `context.get_remaining_time_in_millis()` API is therefore unavailable to the handler. FR-103 addresses this by reading `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms` and making it accessible. Source: Project source code — `src/lambdas/sse_streaming/bootstrap` line 157.
- **(Round 13)** The `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED` environment variable is part of the OTel specification and has been supported in `opentelemetry-python` since v1.24.0 (released mid-2024). When set to `true`, the SDK returns no-op implementations for all telemetry APIs (tracers, meters, loggers). The variable is read at SDK initialization time (module-level `TracerProvider` creation per FR-065); changing it after initialization has no effect until the Lambda execution environment is recycled (idle timeout ~5-15 minutes). In Lambda, this means the kill switch takes effect within minutes as execution environments are recycled. Source: OTel Environment Variable Specification — `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED`.
- **(Round 13)** X-Ray Groups require `insights_enabled = true` in the `InsightsConfiguration` to emit CloudWatch metrics. Without this setting, Groups are purely query-time filters — they match traces when operators search, but they do NOT push any metrics to CloudWatch. The `insights_enabled` attribute is independent of X-Ray Insights pricing tier — enabling it on a Group does not incur Insights charges for root cause analysis or impact detection; it only enables basic Group-derived CloudWatch metrics (fault count, error count, response time statistics). Source: AWS X-Ray API Reference — `CreateGroup` API `InsightsConfiguration` parameter; AWS X-Ray pricing page.
- **(Round 13)** EventBridge scheduled rules become active immediately upon creation. There is no built-in delay, "pending" state, or activation delay. If the rule's target (Lambda function) is not yet invocable due to missing `aws_lambda_permission`, the first invocation fails with `AccessDeniedException`. Terraform's `depends_on` meta-argument ensures deterministic resource creation ordering within a single `terraform apply`. Without `depends_on`, Terraform creates independent resources in parallel, making the ordering non-deterministic. Source: AWS EventBridge documentation — rule state lifecycle; Terraform resource ordering documentation.
- **(Round 13)** AWS ECR image lifecycle policies support tag-based exclusion rules. Images tagged with specific prefixes (e.g., `pre-adot-baseline`) can be exempted from automatic cleanup. ECR repositories support up to 10,000 images. The `pre-adot-baseline` image for rollback purposes is a single image (~500MB for the SSE Lambda container) with negligible storage cost (~$0.05/month at ECR pricing of $0.10/GB/month). Source: AWS ECR Lifecycle Policy documentation — `tagPrefixList` filter.
- **(Round 14)** The `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT` environment variable is supported by the `opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http` package and controls per-request timeout for the OTLP HTTP exporter. Default is 10 seconds. Setting to 2 seconds caps worst-case block during ADOT Extension failure while still allowing normal localhost round-trips (sub-millisecond). Source: OTel Python SDK OTLP HTTP exporter — `DEFAULT_TIMEOUT` and environment variable override.
- **(Round 14)** The ADOT collector binary's `validate` subcommand is available in ADOT v0.40.0+ and produces deterministic exit codes (0 for valid, non-zero for invalid). Validates component references, pipeline wiring, and config schema without starting the collector. The `validate` subcommand from `otelcol-contrib` MUST NOT be used because ADOT bundles different components than contrib. Source: OTel Collector documentation — `validate` subcommand.
- **(Round 14)** Browser CORS preflight cache respects `Access-Control-Max-Age` reliably across Chrome (max 7200s), Firefox (max 86400s), and Safari (max 600s). Cache key is origin + path + method. Source: Fetch Living Standard — CORS preflight cache.
- **(Round 14)** The 50-annotation-per-segment X-Ray limit is sufficient for this feature's instrumentation given the annotation budget (max ~25 per span per FR-120). The 10-annotation reserve provides headroom for diagnostic annotations. Source: X-Ray API documentation — PutTraceSegments annotation limits.
- **(Round 14)** The `event: done` sentinel event pattern (FR-118) is compatible with the frontend's custom SSE parser. Adding a new event type (`done`) requires parser extension but does not conflict with existing types (`data`, `retry`, `deadline` per FR-100). Source: WHATWG HTML Living Standard §9.2.
- **(Round 14)** OTel Python SDK `force_flush()` return value (`True`/`False`) is NOT a reliable indicator of export success. Returns `True` when queue is drained, `False` only when processor is shut down. Export failures during flush do not affect return value. Code MUST NOT use the return value as a health signal. Source: OTel Python SDK `_shared_internal/__init__.py` lines 237-243; issue #4568.
- **(Round 14)** The `treat_missing_data` classification in FR-121 relies on the distinction between "zero-value data points" (metric published with value 0) and "missing data points" (no metric published). AWS-native Lambda metrics publish zero-value points during idle. Custom metric filters with `default_value="0"` emit zeros only when the log group receives non-matching events — NOT when completely silent. Source: AWS CloudWatch Developer Guide — metric filter default values.
- **(Round 15)** CloudWatch Logs metric filters and CloudWatch Metrics use separate API endpoints and subsystems; a Metrics API degradation does not affect Logs metric filter processing. This enables Logs metric filters as a reliable out-of-band backup for put_metric_data failures. Source: AWS regional degradation post-incident reports (us-east-1, 2023-02).
- **(Round 15)** The `python_http_client` library used by SendGrid SDK calls `urllib.request.urlopen()` internally, which resolves to `http.client.HTTPSConnection`. X-Ray's `httplib` patch and OTel's `URLLibInstrumentor` both capture this call chain. Source: python_http_client source code on GitHub.
- **(Round 15)** CloudWatch `put_metric_data` API pricing at $0.01 per 1,000 requests makes the additional metric emission from 5 silent failure paths and 1 heartbeat negligible (estimated ~$2.70/month total for all new custom metrics). Source: CloudWatch pricing page.
- **(Round 15)** Composite alarm `ActionsSuppressor` (added 2022) can prevent alert storms during maintenance windows without silencing the underlying individual alarms. Source: AWS CloudWatch composite alarm documentation.
- **(Round 15)** Lambda error rate math expression `IF(invocations > 10, (errors / invocations) * 100, 0)` requires CloudWatch metric math in alarm definition, which is supported in Terraform via `metric_query` blocks. The minimum invocation guard of 10 prevents division artifacts at low traffic.
- **(Round 15)** Work order files (fix-*.md) were last synchronized around Round 6 (FR-060 range). Rounds 7-14 added FR-062 through FR-123, mapped only in HL doc table. Task 5 has the largest gap: 36 FRs in HL but not in work order file. Source: Manual audit of fix-sse-subsegments.md vs HL doc.
- **(Round 15)** The `analysis_latency_high` alarm threshold at 25,000ms (42% of 60s timeout) is for an async SNS-triggered Lambda where cold starts add 1-5s jitter. AWS recommends 80% of timeout (48,000ms) for async Lambdas to reduce cold-start false positives. Dashboard Lambda's 1,000ms threshold is UX-driven (not timeout-driven) and correctly calibrated. Source: AWS Well-Architected PERF-04.
- **(Round 16)** CloudWatch RUM's `FetchPlugin` monkey-patches `window.fetch` by wrapping the function and injecting headers BEFORE the actual `fetch()` call via argument mutation. The `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header is added to ALL `window.fetch()` calls that pass the `isUrlAllowed()` URL filter (`urlsToInclude`/`urlsToExclude`). Response body processing (including ReadableStream) is NOT intercepted — RUM only reads `response.status` and `Content-Length` header. Cross-origin requests require the target server to include `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` in CORS `Access-Control-Allow-Headers` for the header to be sent by the browser. If CORS preflight rejects the header, the browser silently drops it — fetch() succeeds but without the trace header. Source: aws-rum-web SDK `FetchPlugin.ts` source code; shimmer monkey-patching library.
- **(Round 16)** Cross-region SNS `publish()` from a Lambda in the primary region to a topic in a backup region has typical latency of 50-200ms. This is acceptable for canary alerting since canary detection latency is already ~10 minutes (2× FR-048 interval). The canary Lambda's execution role must include `sns:Publish` with the cross-region topic ARN — IAM policies are global and work cross-region. Source: AWS IAM documentation — global service.
- **(Round 16)** Python `threading.Thread(daemon=True)` combined with `thread.join(timeout=T)` correctly returns after T seconds if the thread has not completed. In Lambda, when the execution environment freezes (after handler returns), daemon threads are suspended but not cleaned up — they resume on the next warm invocation. The abandoned `force_flush()` thread may complete during freeze or on next invocation — this is acceptable because BSP handles concurrent access and `force_flush()` is idempotent. Source: Python 3.13 `threading` documentation; OTel Python SDK `BatchSpanProcessor` thread safety.
- **(Round 16)** API Gateway publishes `IntegrationLatency` and `Latency` metrics per-stage. Lambda Function URLs do NOT publish through API Gateway and use Lambda service metrics instead (`UrlRequestCount`, `Url4xxError`, `Url5xxError`). The SSE Streaming Lambda uses Function URLs (not API Gateway), so FR-138's API Gateway alarms apply only to the 4 API Gateway-fronted Lambdas (Dashboard, Ingestion, Analysis, Notification). The Metrics Lambda is internally triggered (EventBridge) and has neither API Gateway nor Function URL metrics — it is covered by Lambda-native metrics only. Source: AWS API Gateway Monitoring documentation; Lambda Function URL metrics.
- **(Round 16)** SNS `rawMessageDelivery` mode strips ALL system message attributes including `AWSTraceHeader`, breaking X-Ray trace propagation. SNS-to-Lambda subscriptions with `rawMessageDelivery: true` deliver the raw SNS message body without the SNS envelope or system attributes. The Ingestion→Analysis SNS topic subscription MUST NOT use `rawMessageDelivery` for trace propagation to work. Source: AWS SNS Developer Guide — "Amazon SNS raw message delivery."
- **(Round 16)** OTel Python SDK `BatchSpanProcessor.force_flush()` exports batches SEQUENTIALLY — each `exporter.export()` call blocks until the batch is exported or the per-request timeout expires. With `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT=2` and 22 batches (1350 queue ÷ 64 batch size), worst-case total duration is 44 seconds if every batch times out. The `timeout_millis` parameter passed to `force_flush()` is accepted but NOT enforced (opentelemetry-python#4568, still open). Source: OTel Python SDK `BatchSpanProcessor` source; GitHub issue #4568; PR #4564 (merged June 2025).
- **(Round 17)** The ADOT X-Ray exporter's `makeCause()` function (in `opentelemetry-collector-contrib/exporter/awsxrayexporter/internal/translator/cause.go`) is gated on `span.Status().Code() == StatusCodeError`. Exception events recorded via `span.record_exception()` are processed by `makeCause()` to populate the X-Ray `cause` field (with exception type, message, stack), but ONLY when StatusCode is ERROR. When StatusCode is UNSET, exception events exist on the span but are NOT reflected in the X-Ray segment document — the segment has `fault: false` and `cause: null`. This is confirmed behavior in ADOT Collector v0.40+ and is a direct consequence of the X-Ray segment document schema where `fault`, `error`, and `throttle` are top-level booleans determined by the exporter, not by the presence of exception events. Source: ADOT X-Ray Exporter source code; X-Ray Segment Document API Reference.
- **(Round 17)** The canary Lambda is architecturally distinct from the 6 production Lambdas. It is the ONLY Lambda that: (a) queries X-Ray APIs (GetTraceSummaries, BatchGetTraces), (b) performs cross-region SNS publish (FR-136), (c) is exempt from FR-018 fail-fast on X-Ray initialization, (d) has an EventBridge scheduled trigger (not API Gateway or Function URL). Its Powertools Tracer instrumentation is wrapped in FR-145's error handling, meaning instrumentation failures produce structured logs and metrics rather than Lambda crashes.
- **(Round 17)** OTel SpanKind determines X-Ray segment type via the ADOT exporter's `MakeSegment()` function: `SpanKind.SERVER` and `SpanKind.CONSUMER` → X-Ray top-level segment; `SpanKind.CLIENT`, `SpanKind.PRODUCER`, `SpanKind.INTERNAL` → X-Ray subsegment. For the SSE Lambda's manually-created spans: DynamoDB and CloudWatch calls should use `SpanKind.CLIENT` (renders as remote dependency in service map), internal processing logic should use `SpanKind.INTERNAL` (renders within the Lambda node). Incorrect SpanKind produces correct traces but incorrect service map topology. Source: ADOT X-Ray Exporter `segment.go`.
- **(Round 18)** CloudWatch RUM's FetchPlugin uses the `shimmer` library to monkey-patch `window.fetch` SYNCHRONOUSLY — once the AwsRum constructor completes, all subsequent `fetch()` calls are intercepted without additional async steps. However, the AwsRum constructor itself is typically loaded via a CDN `<script>` snippet which may be `async` or `defer`, meaning the constructor execution timing is non-deterministic relative to application JavaScript. The FetchPlugin does NOT expose a readiness event, callback, or promise — detection of patching completion requires checking for side effects (e.g., `window.fetch.toString()` containing shimmer wrapper code, or presence of `window.cwr` global). Source: aws-rum-web SDK FetchPlugin.ts source code; shimmer library documentation.
- **(Round 18)** OTel Python SDK's `start_as_current_span()` decorator/context manager defaults to `record_exception=True` and `set_status_on_exception=True` since v0.16b0. These defaults cause the context manager to automatically call `span.record_exception(exception)` and `span.set_status(StatusCode.ERROR)` when an exception propagates OUT of the `with` block (i.e., is not caught by inner try/except). When inner code catches an exception without re-raising, the context manager's `__exit__` receives `exc_type=None` and does NOT invoke automatic error handling. This means: (a) for spans with no inner try/except, FR-144 compliance is automatic; (b) for spans wrapping the 7 silent failure try/except blocks, FR-144 compliance requires explicit manual dual-call. Source: OTel Python SDK source `opentelemetry/trace/__init__.py` — `use_span()` implementation; confirmed behavior since v0.16b0 (December 2020).
- **(Round 18)** Python module-level code (including `TracerProvider()` constructor, `set_tracer_provider()`, and `BatchSpanProcessor()` initialization) executes exactly ONCE per process — on the first import. Lambda's warm invocation model reuses the same process, so module-level code is NOT re-executed on warm invocations. If module-level initialization fails (exception caught by FR-145), the module-level variables retain their failed/partial state for all subsequent warm invocations. Re-initialization requires handler-level code that explicitly re-creates the objects. This is standard Python semantics but is a critical architectural consideration for the canary's FR-145 resilience requirement. Source: Python Language Reference — the import system; AWS Lambda execution environment reuse documentation.
- **(Round 20)** ~~The `BatchSpanProcessor` deadlock documented in opentelemetry-python#3886 affects Python 3.11+ runtimes and has been reproduced under high concurrency conditions (multiple threads calling `on_end()` while the worker thread is blocked in `export()`). The deadlock is a known open issue as of 2026-03-03.~~ **CORRECTED in Round 21**: opentelemetry-python#3886 is FIXED in SDK v1.33.0+. The project's pinned SDK v1.39.1 uses the rewritten `BatchProcessor` (`opentelemetry/sdk/_shared_internal/__init__.py`) with `collections.deque` + `threading.Event` pattern — no nested locks. FR-139's thread-based hard timeout wrapper remains architecturally valuable for ADOT Extension hang detection but BSP deadlock is no longer a possible cause. See FR-165. Source: OTel Python SDK `_shared_internal/__init__.py` — `BatchProcessor` class v1.39.1; opentelemetry-python#3886 — fix merged in v1.33.0.
- **(Round 20)** The ADOT Lambda Extension remains alive and accepts OTLP spans during the ENTIRE streaming phase of a Lambda RESPONSE_STREAM invocation. **This is an UNVERIFIED assumption** — no AWS documentation explicitly addresses Extension lifecycle during response streaming. AWS Lambda Extensions documentation states "After receiving the function response from the runtime, Lambda returns the response to the client, even if extensions are still running" but was written for buffered responses. For streaming, the "function response" is continuous. FR-160 mandates preprod verification before production deployment. If this assumption is FALSE, the SSE Lambda's OTel instrumentation architecture requires redesign. Source: Assumption based on Extension being an external process with independent lifecycle; NO canonical source confirms this for streaming mode. **PARTIALLY CONFIRMED (Round 24)**: OTel Lambda lifecycle manager (`collector/internal/lifecycle/manager.go`) subscribes to `platform.runtimeDone` events via the Telemetry API. For streaming responses, `runtimeDone` fires when the stream is closed. During streaming, the Extension process remains alive and its OTLP receiver continues accepting spans. The fix from `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-lambda#310` (Telemetry API synchronization) applies to streaming mode. However, no AWS documentation explicitly confirms Extension lifecycle during `RESPONSE_STREAM` — preprod verification mandate (FR-160) remains correct.
- **(Round 20)** Lambda Function URL invocations have no parent X-Ray sampling context because they bypass API Gateway entirely. When the OTel sampler is `parentbased_always_on` (FR-056) and there is no parent context, the sampler delegates to the configured root sampler which is `always_on` — meaning 100% of Function URL invocations are sampled as root spans. This is correct for dev/preprod (per FR-034) but creates unbounded cost risk in production at scale. Source: OTel SDK sampler specification — `parentbased_always_on` delegates to root sampler when no parent exists; OTel default root sampler is `always_on`.
- **(Round 20)** The ADOT Extension's `awsproxy` component proxies X-Ray `GetSamplingRules` and `GetSamplingTargets` API calls to enable centralized sampling. If the Lambda execution role lacks `xray:GetSamplingRules` permission, the awsproxy returns an error and the OTel sampler falls back to `TraceIDRatioBased` with a default of 1 trace/sec. This fallback is SILENT — no CloudWatch alarm fires, no Lambda error is raised, no structured log is emitted by default. The only observable symptom is dramatically reduced trace volume in X-Ray. Source: ADOT Remote Sampling documentation — aws-otel.github.io/docs/getting-started/remote-sampling/; OTel sampler fallback behavior specification.
- **(Round 20)** The ADOT Extension's localhost OTLP endpoint (port 4318) accepts trace data from ANY process within the Lambda execution environment without authentication. This is by design — Lambda's execution environment provides network isolation at the sandbox level. A compromised dependency running in the same Lambda could inject arbitrary trace data into X-Ray via the local OTLP endpoint. The practical risk is low (Lambda sandbox isolation) but the security model should be documented. FR-155's PII prohibition applies to data sent BY the application; it does not protect against injected trace data from compromised dependencies. Source: ADOT permissions documentation — "The proxy extension allows any application with network connectivity to the collector to send requests to X-Ray without authentication."

- **(Round 21)** OTel Python SDK v1.39.1 `BatchProcessor.emit()` uses `collections.deque([], max_queue_size)` for span queuing. When the deque is full, `appendleft()` silently evicts the oldest element — there is NO log entry, NO callback, NO metric emitted. The `emit()` method contains an explicit comment: "Do not add any logging.log statements to this function, they can be being routed back to this emit function, resulting in endless recursive calls" (opentelemetry-python#4261). This means span drops are fundamentally undetectable from within the SDK. Detection requires external comparison of created vs exported span counts. Source: OTel Python SDK `_shared_internal/__init__.py:200-208` — `emit()` method.
- **(Round 21)** ADOT Lambda Extension processes are started ONCE during Lambda INIT and are NOT restarted if they crash (OOM, segfault). A crashed Extension is dead for all subsequent warm invocations on that execution environment. The OTLP HTTP exporter's `requests.Session` creates new TCP connections per request, so if the Extension were to restart (which it doesn't), the exporter would auto-reconnect without TracerProvider recreation. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API lifecycle documentation; OTel Python SDK `trace_exporter/__init__.py:156-172`.
- **(Round 21)** The OTLP HTTP exporter retries failed exports up to 6 times with exponential backoff (`2^retry_num * random.uniform(0.8, 1.2)` seconds). Retryable conditions: HTTP 408 or any 5xx status. Non-retryable: all 4xx except 408 — notably HTTP 429 (rate limit) is NOT retried, deviating from OTel spec recommendation. Total retry duration capped at `self._timeout` (default 10s). During retry sleep, the BSP worker thread is blocked via `_export_lock`, preventing other batches from being exported. Source: OTel Python SDK `trace_exporter/__init__.py:174-208`; `_common/__init__.py:29-34`.
- **(Round 21)** X-Ray PutTraceSegments TPS quota is ~2,500/region default (NOT 2,600 as previously stated), adjustable via AWS Service Quotas (quota code `L-AB6D2D9B`). X-Ray Groups quota is 25/region (adjustable, quota code `L-F895D63C`). X-Ray Sampling Rules quota is 25/region (adjustable, quota code `L-B5F5E1ED`). All three quotas were previously assumed to be hard/non-adjustable. Source: AWS X-Ray Service Quotas documentation.
- **(Round 21)** X-Ray encrypts ALL trace data at rest by default using an AWS-managed key. Optional customer-managed CMK available via `PutEncryptionConfig` API per-region using envelope encryption. No customer action required for default encryption. Source: AWS X-Ray Developer Guide — "Data protection in AWS X-Ray."
- **(Round 21)** `GetTraceSummaries` API has a 6-hour maximum time range window per request. For broader searches, multiple requests with sliding 6-hour windows are required. Rate limit: 30 TPS. Pagination: 100 trace summaries per response with `NextToken`. Source: AWS X-Ray API Reference — `GetTraceSummaries` parameters.
- **(Round 21)** Centralized X-Ray sampling rules only apply at trace roots (no parent context). They do NOT override parent sampling decisions propagated via `X-Amzn-Trace-Id`. For `parentbased_always_on` (FR-056), the ParentBased wrapper delegates to the root sampler only when no parent exists. API Gateway-fronted Lambdas inherit parent sampling decisions; Function URL Lambdas, EventBridge-triggered Lambdas, and the canary create root spans governed by centralized rules. Source: OTel SDK `sampling.py:349-367` — `ParentBased` delegation logic; AWS X-Ray centralized sampling specification.
- **(Round 21)** Lambda Function URL does NOT create its own X-Ray segment — there is no separate "Function URL" node in the X-Ray service map. The Lambda service creates the segment. Operators lose gateway-level latency breakdown (authorization, WAF, integration latency) compared to API Gateway. Source: AWS Lambda Function URL documentation; Lambda X-Ray tracing documentation.
- **(Round 21)** CloudWatch RUM DOES inject `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` headers into browser `fetch()` calls when `enableXRay: true` and `addXRayTraceIdHeader: true` are configured. RUM creates its own traces on the client side using the X-Ray SDK for JavaScript. Backend segments become children of the RUM-originated trace, creating end-to-end browser-to-backend traces. Requires CORS `Access-Control-Allow-Headers: X-Amzn-Trace-Id` on the backend. Source: CloudWatch RUM Developer Guide — "CloudWatch RUM with X-Ray."
- **(Round 21)** OTel `AwsLambdaResourceDetector` reads `os.environ` on every `detect()` call (no caching in the detector). However, `Resource` objects are created once during TracerProvider initialization and are immutable. On warm invocations, the same `TracerProvider` (and same `Resource`) is reused. Environment variables like `AWS_LAMBDA_LOG_STREAM_NAME` that change between cold starts retain their cold-start values in the cached Resource. Source: OTel Python SDK `extension/aws/resource/_lambda.py:35-62`.
- **(Round 21)** OTel span attribute defaults: 128 attributes per span (`_DEFAULT_OTEL_SPAN_ATTRIBUTE_COUNT_LIMIT`), no default value length limit. Excess attributes are silently dropped via `BoundedAttributes.popitem(last=False)` with `self.dropped` counter incremented — no log emitted. String value truncation (when `OTEL_SPAN_ATTRIBUTE_VALUE_LENGTH_LIMIT` is set) uses `value[:limit]` with no log. Source: OTel Python SDK `trace/__init__.py:567-714`; `attributes/__init__.py:239-323`.
- **(Round 21)** ADOT Extension warm invocation overhead is effectively zero on the hot path — span creation via `emit()` is non-blocking (appends to `deque`), and BSP export runs asynchronously on a worker thread every 1000ms. No per-invocation synchronous OTLP call occurs. The Extension is already resident on warm invocations. Source: OTel Python SDK BSP implementation; ADOT Extension lifecycle — Extension persists across warm invocations.
- **(Round 22)** PutTraceSegments default quota is 500 TPS per region (AWS Service Quotas L-AB6D2D9B). The ~2,500 value documented in Round 21 may represent an account-specific increase. Each new AWS account/region starts at 500 TPS. Source: AWS X-Ray Service Quotas page.
- **(Round 22)** OTel Python SDK `ReadableSpan.attributes` is immutable after `Span.end()` is called. The `on_end(span)` SpanProcessor callback receives a read-only view. Attribute mutation is only possible via `on_start(span)` or during active span lifetime. Source: OTel Python SDK source — `ReadableSpan` class definition.
- **(Round 22)** ADOT Lambda Extension collector configuration does NOT include OTel Collector contrib processors (e.g., `redaction` processor). The Extension ships a minimal collector binary. **CONFIRMED (Round 24)**: `aws-otel-lambda/adot/collector/lambdacomponents/default.go` confirms ZERO processors. Receivers: `otlpreceiver`. Exporters: `awsxrayexporter`, `awsemfexporter`, `prometheusremotewriteexporter`, `debugexporter`, `otlpexporter`, `otlphttpexporter`. Extensions: `sigv4authextension`. The upstream OTel Lambda layer includes 9 processors (including `attributesprocessor`, `filterprocessor`, `batchprocessor`) — ADOT's fork strips all of them.
- **(Round 22)** `aws lambda update-function-configuration` replaces ALL environment variables, not merge. Omitting existing variables from the API call deletes them. Source: AWS Lambda API Reference — UpdateFunctionConfiguration.
- **(Round 22)** ADOT Extension crash causes Lambda service to terminate the entire execution environment. Next invocation gets a completely new sandbox (full cold start). Extensions cannot be restarted in-place. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — extension lifecycle documentation.
- ~~**(Round 22)** ADOT Extension SHUTDOWN flush window default is 2 seconds, configurable to max 10 seconds via `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` environment variable. **UNVERIFIED** — the environment variable name and max value come from ADOT GitHub issues, not official AWS documentation.~~ **DENIED (Round 24)**: `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` does NOT EXIST in any ADOT or OTel Lambda source code (GitHub-wide code search returned zero results). The 2-second extension shutdown window is a Lambda platform constraint enforced via SIGKILL, not configurable by the extension. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API documentation — extension shutdown lifecycle. See FR-202.
