- **(Round 22)** X-Ray `GetTraceSummaries` has no `MaxResults` parameter — the service controls page size internally. The `Sampling` boolean parameter enables statistical result sampling. Source: AWS X-Ray API Reference — GetTraceSummaries.
- **(Round 22)** W3C Trace Context specification defines only one flag bit (`sampled`) in `traceparent`. There is NO standardized "synthetic" or "canary" flag. Source: W3C Trace Context Level 1 — Section 3.2.2.5 trace-flags.

**Corrected Assumption (Round 22):**
- PutTraceSegments TPS "~2,500 default" (Round 21) → CORRECTED to **500 TPS default**. The 2,500 figure may represent an account-specific Service Quotas increase. Default applies to new environments, regions, and accounts. This correction mirrors the BSP timeout correction pattern (Round 9: 200ms → 5000ms).

**Round 23 Assumptions:**
- **(Round 23)** `force_flush()` double-call within a single invocation is safe on OTel Python SDK v1.39.1. The BSP's `force_flush()` acquires a condition variable, drains the internal deque via `_export()`, and returns. A second call acquires the same lock, finds an empty deque, and returns immediately with no side effects. This is NOT a confirmed risk — it is a confirmed non-risk. Source: OTel Python SDK `BatchSpanProcessor.force_flush()` implementation — deque drain is idempotent.
- **(Round 23)** ADOT Extension partial startup race (Extension process alive but OTLP :4318 not yet listening) is a confirmed non-risk for Lambda. The Extensions API lifecycle guarantees that the Extension's INIT phase completes (including OTLP receiver startup) before the Lambda service sends the first INVOKE event to the runtime. The runtime cannot call the handler — and therefore cannot create spans — until after the Extension is fully initialized. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API — "Lambda waits for all extensions to report an INIT completion before sending the first INVOKE."
- **(Round 23)** SpanProcessor registration ordering in the OTel Python SDK's `TracerProvider` follows insertion order. `add_span_processor()` appends to an internal list, and callbacks (`on_start`, `on_end`) are invoked in that insertion order. FR-191's attribute allow-list SpanProcessor MUST be registered BEFORE `BatchSpanProcessor` to ensure `on_start()` filters attributes before BSP sees the span. Source: OTel Python SDK `ConcurrentMultiSpanProcessor` — iterates processors in registration order.
- ~~**(Round 23)** Go's `recover()` mechanism can catch panics in ADOT Extension goroutines without terminating the Extension process. A recovered panic in a non-critical goroutine (e.g., metrics reporting) leaves the Extension alive to the Lambda Runtime API but potentially in a degraded state (e.g., exporter goroutine dead while receiver goroutine still accepts spans). The Lambda service sees a healthy Extension (INIT succeeded, no crash signal). Source: Go language specification — `recover()` semantics; ADOT Collector source — goroutine structure.~~ **INVALIDATED in Round 24**: OTel Collector does NOT use `recover()` in pipeline goroutines. `exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go` has no `recover()` wrapper. Panics crash the entire Collector/Extension process. The "recovered panic" scenario is architecturally impossible. See FR-200.
- **(Round 23)** OTel Python SDK `BoundedAttributes` evicts the OLDEST attribute (by insertion order) when the configured limit is exceeded. This is a FIFO eviction policy, not LRU or priority-based. When X-Ray's 50-annotation limit is reached at the X-Ray service layer, the truncation order is UNDEFINED by AWS documentation. The interaction between SDK-side eviction and service-side truncation means annotation survival depends on both insertion order (SDK) and undocumented service behavior (X-Ray). Source: OTel Python SDK `BoundedAttributes` implementation — `__setitem__` with `maxlen` deque.

**Confirmed Non-Risks (Round 23):**
- `force_flush()` double-call: Safe — empty deque returns immediately (see assumption above).
- ADOT Extension partial startup race: Non-risk — Extensions API lifecycle prevents runtime-before-Extension ordering (see assumption above).

**Round 24 Assumptions:**
- **(Round 24)** OTel Collector pipeline goroutines (exporter workers in `async_queue.go`) do NOT use Go `recover()`. A panic in any pipeline goroutine crashes the entire Collector process. This INVALIDATES the Round 23 assumption about `recover()` catching panics in ADOT Extension goroutines. The `StatusRecoverableError` mechanism in OTel Collector is voluntary component-level status reporting, NOT panic recovery. Source: `opentelemetry-collector` `exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go` — zero `recover()` calls; `component/componentstatus/status.go` — `StatusRecoverableError` definition.
- **(Round 24)** ADOT Lambda Extension includes zero span processors. Receivers: `otlpreceiver`. Exporters: `awsxrayexporter`, `awsemfexporter`, `prometheusremotewriteexporter`, `debugexporter`, `otlpexporter`, `otlphttpexporter`. Extensions: `sigv4authextension`. Processors: none. Source: `aws-otel-lambda/adot/collector/lambdacomponents/default.go`.
- **(Round 24)** The Lambda platform's extension shutdown window is 2 seconds, enforced via SIGKILL. This is a platform constraint, not configurable by the extension or environment variables. The `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` environment variable referenced in Round 22 does NOT EXIST in any ADOT or OTel Lambda source code. Source: AWS Lambda Extensions API documentation — extension shutdown lifecycle.
- **(Round 24)** OTel Collector `exporterhelper` retries failed exports with exponential backoff and `max_elapsed_time` default of 300s. However, Lambda's 2s shutdown window truncates this to at most 2s of retry during shutdown. During invocation execution, the full retry budget is available but competes with Lambda timeout. Source: OTel Collector `exporterhelper` `retry_sender.go`.
- **(Round 24)** SendGrid Python SDK uses `python_http_client` → `urllib.request.build_opener().open()` → `http.client.HTTPSConnection`. AWS X-Ray SDK `patch(['httplib'])` instruments this path. OTel `URLLibInstrumentor` from `opentelemetry-instrumentation-urllib` also instruments this path. This RESOLVES the Round 15 uncertainty about SendGrid HTTP tracing. Source: `python_http_client/client.py:259` — `urllib.build_opener()`; `aws_xray_sdk/ext/httplib/patch.py` — wraps `http.client.HTTPConnection._send_request`.

**Confirmed Non-Risks (Round 24):**
- ADOT recovered panic as distinct span-loss vector: DENIED — panics crash the entire Extension process (no `recover()` in pipeline goroutines). Identical to span-loss vector #3 (crash). Not a distinct vector.
- SendGrid HTTP tracing uncertainty: RESOLVED — `httplib` patch captures SendGrid calls through the `urllib.request` → `http.client` call chain. No uncertainty remains.
- SNS cross-Lambda trace propagation: CONFIRMED AUTOMATIC — `AWSTraceHeader` system attribute carries trace context when Active Tracing is enabled on both Lambdas. Already documented in spec assumptions but confirmed via canonical AWS documentation. Caveat: `rawMessageDelivery: true` breaks propagation (already captured in FR-137).

## Success Criteria *(mandatory)*

### Measurable Outcomes

- **SC-001**: For any sampled user request, an operator can trace it from browser through API Gateway through Lambda through downstream services (DynamoDB, SNS, SendGrid) as a single continuous trace — with zero tool-switching required. Dev/preprod environments sample at 100%; production sampling is configured to balance cost with debuggability.
- **SC-002**: An operator can filter traces by error/fault status and immediately identify which specific operation failed (circuit breaker, audit trail, notification publish, fanout, self-healing) — without grepping logs.
- **SC-003**: 100% of Lambda functions (6 of 6) have auto-instrumented service call subsegments, up from current 5 of 6 (Metrics Lambda missing).
- **SC-004**: 100% of silent failure paths have X-Ray subsegments marked as error when the failure occurs. The 7 paths are: (1) circuit breaker load, (2) circuit breaker save, (3) audit trail persistence, (4) downstream notification SNS publish, (5) time-series fanout partial batch write, (6) self-healing item fetch, (7) parallel fetcher error aggregation.
- **SC-005**: SSE streaming latency and cache performance data is queryable via trace annotations — operators can filter traces by latency thresholds or cache hit rate directly, without separate log query tools.
- **SC-006**: The custom correlation ID system (`get_correlation_id`, `generate_correlation_id`) is fully removed, with zero remaining call sites.
- **SC-007**: The X-Ray canary detects simulated tracing ingestion failure within 2 consecutive canary intervals and fires a non-X-Ray alarm.
- **SC-008**: Cross-Lambda traces through SNS (Ingestion -> Analysis) appear under a single trace ID with the SNS hop visible as a connecting segment, enabling cross-service debugging without log correlation.
- **SC-009**: The system contains exactly one non-X-Ray tracing mechanism: the X-Ray canary. All custom tracing logs and custom correlation IDs previously identified in audit section 9.1 are consolidated onto X-Ray. Standard operational logging and CloudWatch metrics remain unchanged.
- **SC-010** [Round 3 — Revised]: SSE streaming operations (DynamoDB polls, event dispatch, CloudWatch metrics) that occur AFTER the Lambda handler returns the generator are captured in traced spans that appear in X-Ray linked to the original invocation trace ID. Zero orphaned subsegments, zero `SegmentNotFoundException` errors, zero silently discarded segments from `LambdaContext.put_segment()`. The tracing mechanism has an independent lifecycle that survives handler return.
- **SC-011** (Round 2): SendGrid email API calls in the Notification Lambda appear as explicitly instrumented subsegments with HTTP status and duration, not as untraced gaps in the service map.
- **SC-012** (Round 2): All non-streaming Lambda functions use a single, consistent tracing approach. Exceptions raised inside traced functions are automatically captured as subsegment errors. Zero Lambdas use dual/conflicting patching mechanisms. The SSE Lambda uses a distinct approach necessitated by the RESPONSE_STREAM lifecycle constraint, but its traces appear in the same X-Ray console.
- **SC-013** (Round 3): An X-Ray Group with error/fault filter generates CloudWatch metrics for errored traces. Operators can set alarms on error rates derived directly from trace data.
- **SC-014** (Round 3): The X-Ray canary detects partial trace data loss (throttling, daemon failure) by tracking the ratio of submitted-to-retrieved test traces. When data loss exceeds the configured threshold, a dedicated CloudWatch alarm fires.
- **SC-015** (Round 3): The frontend SSE client uses `fetch()` + `ReadableStream` with automatic reconnection logic, propagating `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` headers on every connection — matching or exceeding the reliability of the replaced `EventSource` implementation.
- **SC-016** (Round 3): X-Ray billing alarms fire when monthly costs exceed $10, $25, or $50 thresholds, preventing cost surprises from sampling configuration changes or traffic growth.
- **SC-017** (Round 4): 6/6 Lambda functions have both CloudWatch error alarms and CloudWatch latency alarms configured. Zero Lambda functions exist without operational alerting.
- **SC-018** (Round 4): All custom metrics previously emitted without alarms (7 metrics from audit Section 4.2) now have CloudWatch alarms with documented thresholds. Zero metrics exist in "emitted but unalarmed" state.
- **SC-019** (Round 4): All 7 silent failure paths emit both X-Ray subsegments (for trace context, per SC-004) and CloudWatch metrics (for 100% alarm coverage). An error on any silent failure path triggers both a trace annotation and a CloudWatch alarm — no silent failure is invisible to operators regardless of X-Ray sampling configuration.
- **SC-020** (Round 4): SSE reconnection traces are queryable by `session_id` annotation, returning all traces for a logical SSE session across reconnections. Operators can follow the reconnection chain via `previous_trace_id` annotations.
- **SC-021** (Round 4): The canary detects both X-Ray ingestion failure AND CloudWatch metric emission pipeline failure within 2 consecutive canary intervals. Meta-observability failures are reported via an out-of-band channel independent of CloudWatch alarms.
- **SC-022** (Round 4): The CloudWatch dashboard alarm status widget displays ALL configured alarms. Operators viewing the dashboard see complete alarm status without hidden blind spots.
- **SC-023** (Round 5): OTel spans created during SSE streaming phase carry the SAME trace ID as the Lambda runtime's X-Ray facade segment. Zero disconnected traces from trace ID mismatch. Zero orphaned OTel spans from sampling decision mismatch. Handler-phase subsegments (Powertools) and streaming-phase spans (OTel/ADOT) appear as a unified trace in the X-Ray console.
- **SC-024** (Round 5): The SSE Lambda's streaming generator calls `force_flush()` before the execution environment freezes. Zero spans are lost between invocations due to unflushed `BatchSpanProcessor` buffers. Zero stale spans from previous invocations appear in current invocation traces.
- **SC-025** (Round 5): All X-Ray subsegment/span metadata payloads are bounded. Zero segment documents are rejected by the 64KB `PutTraceSegments` limit. Error messages are truncated to 2,048 characters. No HTTP response bodies are attached as metadata.
- **SC-026** (Round 6): On warm invocations, all OTel streaming-phase spans link to the CURRENT invocation's trace ID — not a stale trace ID from a previous invocation. Verified by triggering 2+ sequential invocations on the same warm execution environment and confirming each invocation's spans carry distinct, correct trace IDs. Zero trace ID carryover between invocations.
- **SC-027** (Round 7): The SSE Lambda's OTel `TracerProvider` is instantiated exactly once per execution environment (at INIT). On 10+ consecutive warm invocations, no new `BatchSpanProcessor` daemon threads are created and memory usage remains stable (no monotonic growth). Zero `TracerProvider` instances are created inside the handler function.
- **SC-028** (Round 7): Streaming-phase DynamoDB and CloudWatch spans appear as correctly-typed subsegments in the X-Ray service map — DynamoDB calls render as DynamoDB nodes, CloudWatch calls render as CloudWatch nodes. Zero "unknown remote" or generic nodes from streaming-phase operations. Verified by querying the X-Ray service map API after a traced SSE streaming invocation with at least one DynamoDB query and one CloudWatch `put_metric_data` call.
- **SC-029** (Round 8): The SSE Lambda's container image includes the ADOT collector binary at `/opt/extensions/collector` and the default collector configuration at `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml`. The ADOT Extension process starts during Lambda INIT, registers with the Extensions API, and accepts OTLP spans on `localhost:4318`. Verified by inspecting the container image layers and confirming the Extension appears in Lambda INIT logs.
- **SC-030** (Round 8): The SSE Lambda appears as a correctly-named node in the X-Ray service map (matching `POWERTOOLS_SERVICE_NAME`). Zero `unknown_service` nodes exist in the service map for any environment where the SSE Lambda has been invoked. Verified by querying the X-Ray service map API and confirming the SSE Lambda node name matches the configured `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`.
- **SC-031** (Round 9): The ADOT Extension's collector pipeline includes the decouple processor. Verified by inspecting the collector configuration and confirming the pipeline order includes `decouple` as the last processor before the exporter.
- **SC-032** (Round 9): The SSE Lambda's `TracerProvider` is instantiated with `shutdown_on_exit=False`. Zero `RuntimeError` exceptions from `ConcurrentMultiSpanProcessor` shutdown race conditions on execution environment recycling. Verified by running 100+ invocations across multiple execution environment recycling events.
- **SC-033** (Round 9): Zero `BotocoreInstrumentor` imports or `.instrument()` calls exist in the SSE Lambda's codebase. Verified by code search.
- **SC-034** (Round 9): The X-Ray canary retries trace retrieval at least once with backoff (30s then 60s) before reporting trace loss. Verified by simulating X-Ray propagation delay >30s and confirming the canary does not false-alarm on the first query.
- **SC-035** (Round 9): The canary immediately escalates IAM/credential errors (`AccessDeniedException`, `NotAuthorized`) via out-of-band channel (FR-050) with zero retries. Transient errors (`ThrottlingException`, `InternalFailure`) are retried up to 3 times before escalation. Verified by simulating both error types and confirming differential handling.
- **SC-036** (Round 9): The SSE Lambda server either (a) checks `Last-Event-ID` header and resumes from that position, or (b) responds with `X-SSE-Resume-Supported: false` header. Zero scenarios exist where the client sends `Last-Event-ID` and the server silently ignores it.
- **SC-037** (Round 9): The SSE Lambda Function URL CORS configuration includes `x-amzn-trace-id` in `Access-Control-Expose-Headers`. Browser JavaScript can read the `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` response header for FR-048's `previous_trace_id` capture.
- **SC-038** (Round 9): The frontend SSE client reconnects with short delay (1-3s) on graceful server close and exponential backoff on network error. Zero instances of 30s+ reconnection delays after expected server-initiated closes (e.g., Lambda timeout).
- **SC-039** (Round 10): When an SSE Lambda streaming client disconnects mid-stream, OTel spans emitted after the disconnect carry `client.disconnected=true` annotation. Verified by disconnecting a client mid-stream and querying X-Ray for traces with the `client.disconnected` annotation. The span status is `OK` (not `ERROR`), confirming client disconnect is not misclassified as a server fault.
- **SC-040** (Round 10): The SSE Lambda's `BatchSpanProcessor` `max_queue_size` is >= 1,350 (2x expected span throughput of ~675 spans per 15-second invocation). Zero spans are silently dropped due to queue overflow during normal streaming operations (15 polls/second, 3 spans/poll). Verified by running a 15-second streaming session with `OTEL_LOG_LEVEL=WARNING` and confirming zero "Queue is full" log entries.
- **SC-041** (Round 10): The X-Ray canary reports partial traces (`IsPartial=true`) as degraded rather than successful. When a test trace has `IsPartial=true` after all retry attempts, the canary emits `canary.trace.partial` CloudWatch metric with value 1 and does NOT count the trace as a fully successful verification. Verified by simulating delayed ADOT span delivery and confirming the canary reports degraded status.
- **SC-042** (Round 10): The SSE Lambda emits `retry: 3000\n` as the first field in each SSE connection. The frontend client parses this value and uses 3000ms as the reconnection delay on graceful server close. Verified by inspecting SSE stream output and measuring client reconnection timing after Lambda timeout.
- **SC-043** (Round 10): The SSE Lambda is deployed WITHOUT VPC configuration — no `vpc_config` block in the Terraform `aws_lambda_function` resource. Verified by inspecting Terraform configuration and confirming zero `subnet_ids` or `security_group_ids` on the SSE Lambda.
- **SC-044** (Round 10): The custom ADOT collector YAML explicitly includes `decouple` in the `service.pipelines.traces.processors` list, in the order `[decouple, batch]`. Verified by inspecting the collector configuration file in the container image at `/opt/collector-config/config.yaml`.
- **SC-045** (Round 11): The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap reads `Lambda-Runtime-Trace-Id` from the Runtime API response and sets `os.environ['_X_AMZN_TRACE_ID']` before calling the handler on EVERY invocation. On 10+ consecutive warm invocations, each invocation's OTel spans carry the CURRENT invocation's trace ID (not the first invocation's). Verified by comparing trace IDs between the Runtime API response header and the OTel spans emitted during each invocation.
- **SC-046** (Round 11): The SSE Lambda's streaming generator calls `force_flush()` proactively when remaining Lambda execution time falls below 3000ms, BEFORE the Lambda timeout kills the process. On a Lambda invocation that times out, spans created up to the proactive flush point are exported to ADOT and appear in X-Ray. Zero span loss due to `finally` block non-execution on timeout. Verified by setting a short Lambda timeout (5s) and confirming spans from the first 2 seconds appear in X-Ray.
- **SC-047** (Round 11): The SSE Lambda's Terraform configuration includes `OPENTELEMETRY_COLLECTOR_CONFIG_FILE = "/opt/collector-config/config.yaml"` in the environment variables block. The ADOT Extension uses the custom config (not the embedded default). Verified by inspecting Lambda configuration in the AWS console and confirming the ADOT Extension logs reference the custom config file path on startup.
- **SC-048** (Round 11): The observability canary runs every 5 minutes via EventBridge scheduled rule. Detection latency for X-Ray or CloudWatch failures is <= 10 minutes (2 consecutive 5-minute intervals per FR-020). The canary Lambda timeout is 60 seconds. CloudWatch metric health checks use two-phase architecture (each invocation queries PREVIOUS invocation's test metric). Verified by checking EventBridge rule configuration and canary invocation logs.
- **SC-049** (Round 11): All FR-043 silent failure metrics use the `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` namespace with `FunctionName` and `FailurePath` dimensions. All 6 metrics are queryable in a single CloudWatch namespace. The `HighLatencyAlert` metric uses `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability` namespace. Verified by querying CloudWatch `list-metrics` for the namespace.
- **SC-050** (Round 11): The SSE Lambda's CloudWatch Log Group has a metric filter matching `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."`. The filter emits `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/ADOTExportFailure` metric. A CloudWatch alarm on this metric fires within 5 minutes of an ADOT export failure. Verified by simulating an export failure and confirming the alarm transitions to ALARM.
- **SC-051** (Round 11): The frontend SSE client uses `new TextDecoder('utf-8', {stream: true})` for ReadableStream chunk decoding. Multi-byte UTF-8 characters that span chunk boundaries are correctly reconstructed without U+FFFD replacement. Verified by sending SSE events containing multi-byte characters and confirming the client receives them intact.
- **SC-052** (Round 12): After the proactive flush (FR-093) fires, the streaming generator yields `event: deadline` and terminates normally. The Lambda invocation completes as a normal return (not a timeout). The ADOT Extension receives Shutdown with `shutdownReason: "spindown"` (not `"timeout"`). Verified by setting a short Lambda timeout (10s), streaming for 7+ seconds, confirming the `event: deadline` SSE event is received by the client, and confirming all spans up to the flush point appear in X-Ray.
- **SC-053** (Round 12): The SSE Lambda's requirements file pins OTel core packages to identical versions (e.g., `opentelemetry-api==1.39.1`, `opentelemetry-sdk==1.39.1`, `opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http==1.39.1`). `pip install` produces zero version-conflict warnings. Docker builds on different dates produce identical OTel package versions. Verified by running `pip check` and confirming zero incompatibilities.
- **SC-054** (Round 12): The SSE Lambda memory allocation is 1024MB. Cold start (including ADOT Extension + OTel SDK initialization) completes in < 1500ms. Memory utilization under normal 15-second streaming stays below 80% (< 820MB). Verified by inspecting Lambda `REPORT` log lines for `Init Duration` and `Max Memory Used`.
- **SC-055** (Round 12): The SSE Lambda's custom bootstrap reads `Lambda-Runtime-Deadline-Ms` from the Runtime API response and passes the deadline timestamp to the handler. The handler (or streaming generator) can compute remaining execution time as `deadline_ms - current_time_ms` without using the Lambda context object. Verified by logging the deadline value at handler entry and comparing with the actual Lambda timeout.
- **SC-056** (Round 12): All 6 Lambda functions have CloudWatch memory utilization alarms at 85% threshold. A Lambda invocation that uses > 85% of configured memory triggers the alarm. Verified by simulating high-memory workload and confirming alarm transition.
- **SC-057** (Round 12): FR-098's CloudWatch Logs metric filter matches both `"Exporting failed. Dropping data."` and `"Exporting failed. No more retries left. Dropping data."` log variants. Verified by injecting both log patterns and confirming the metric filter emits for both.
- **SC-058** (Round 13): Remediation tasks are deployed in phase order per FR-107: Phase 1 (IAM) → Phase 2 (Instrumentation) → Phase 3 (Frontend) → Phase 4 (Logging Removal, after 2-week verification per FR-109) → Phase 5 (Monitoring) → Phase 6 (Validation). Zero logging removal tasks (6/7/9) are deployed before instrumentation tasks (2-5) are verified. Zero canary deployments (Task 11) occur before at least one instrumentation task is live and emitting traces. Verified by deployment runbook checklist, PR merge timestamps, and canary health status.
- **SC-059** (Round 13): All ADOT-instrumented Lambda functions include `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=false` in their Terraform environment variables block. Setting `OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true` via Terraform and applying immediately disables all OTel span creation on the next execution environment initialization, with zero container rebuilds required. Reverting to `false` re-enables tracing. Verified by inspecting Terraform configuration and toggling the variable in a non-production environment.
- **SC-060** (Round 13): The SSE Lambda's ECR repository contains a tagged `pre-adot-baseline` image that matches the current production image without ADOT components. Reverting the Terraform `image_uri` to the `pre-adot-baseline` image and applying restores pre-ADOT behavior within 5 minutes. The rollback image passes all existing integration tests. Verified by deploying the rollback image in a test environment and confirming the Lambda functions normally without OTel traces.
- **SC-061** (Round 13): All X-Ray Groups created for this feature have `insights_configuration { insights_enabled = true }`. CloudWatch metrics derived from X-Ray Group filter expressions are visible in the CloudWatch Metrics console under the `AWS/XRay` namespace within 5 minutes of traced requests matching the Group filter. Verified by creating a Group with error filter, triggering an errored request, and confirming the `FaultCount` metric appears in CloudWatch.
- **SC-062** (Round 13): The canary EventBridge rule's Terraform resource includes explicit `depends_on` referencing the `aws_lambda_permission` resource. A fresh `terraform apply` from empty state creates the Lambda permission before the EventBridge rule activates. Zero `AccessDeniedException` invocation failures occur during initial deployment. Verified by `terraform plan` output ordering and monitoring the first canary invocation after deployment.
- **SC-063** (Round 13): The canary emits `canary.trace.completeness_ratio` metric on every invocation. Over a 1-hour window with 12 canary invocations (5-minute interval per FR-048), the completeness ratio stays >= 0.95 (at least 11 of 12 test traces fully verified). A simulated 20% systemic trace loss (e.g., by temporarily misconfiguring ADOT collector pipeline) triggers the completeness alarm within 30 minutes. Verified by querying the CloudWatch metric and simulating trace loss in a test environment.
- **SC-064** (Round 14, amended Round 17, **SUPERSEDED Round 20**): This SC has been split into SC-064a (port-unreachable) and SC-064b (hung Extension) in Round 20. The original SC tested two distinct failure modes with different code paths in a single success criterion, creating ambiguous pass/fail semantics. SC-064a verifies fast failure (ECONNREFUSED, < 100ms, no thread wrapper needed). SC-064b verifies hung failure (TCP accept, no response, FR-139 thread wrapper fires at 2500ms). The `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_TRACES_TIMEOUT=2` env var requirement remains in both sub-criteria.
- **SC-065** (Round 14): Every SSE event emitted during streaming includes a `trace_id` field in the JSON data payload in X-Ray format (`1-{hex_timestamp}-{24_hex_digits}`). An operator can paste this trace_id into the X-Ray console and retrieve the exact span that produced the event. Verified by receiving an SSE event, extracting trace_id, and querying X-Ray.
- **SC-066** (Round 14): CI includes an ADOT collector config validation step before Docker image build. A deliberately malformed config (invalid YAML, unknown component, broken pipeline) causes CI failure with clear error. Validation uses the ADOT-specific binary, not `otelcol-contrib`. Verified by introducing a config error and confirming CI rejection.
- **SC-067** (Round 14): FR-109's four verification gates are executable: gate (a) automated semantic trace comparison, gate (b) annotation key set diff, gate (c) X-Ray service map API query, gate (d) automated 100-trace spot-check. All produce pass/fail with detailed output. Daily spot-check results persisted to S3 for 2-week audit trail. Verified by running gate scripts in test environment.
- **SC-068** (Round 14): The frontend SSE client correctly classifies 4 error types: graceful close (sentinel) → immediate reconnect, abnormal termination (no sentinel) → short delay, network error (TypeError) → exponential backoff, intentional cancellation (AbortError) → no reconnect. SSE Lambda sends `event: done` before every intentional close. Verified by simulating each scenario and measuring reconnection behavior.
- **SC-069** (Round 14): All CORS configurations including `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` in Allow-Headers also set `Access-Control-Max-Age: 7200`. First fetch() triggers preflight; subsequent requests within 2 hours do not. Verified via browser DevTools Network tab.
- **SC-070** (Round 14): No OTel span on the SSE Lambda exceeds 25 annotations (half the 50-annotation X-Ray limit). Annotation budget is documented with 10 reserved slots. Verified by exporting traces and counting annotations per span.
- **SC-071** (Round 14): All canary/heartbeat alarms use `treat_missing_data = "breaching"`. All custom error metric filter alarms use `"breaching"`. AWS-native Lambda metric alarms use `"notBreaching"`. Simulated canary failure (no metric emission for 2 periods) triggers alarm. Verified by inspecting Terraform and simulating metric absence.
- **SC-072** (Round 14): Kill switch mitigation (`OTEL_SDK_DISABLED=true`) applies within 5 minutes. Full image rollback to `pre-adot-baseline` completes within 15 minutes. Post-rollback SSE Lambda error rate < 0.1%, cold start p99 < 1500ms within 5 minutes. Verified by rollback drill in preprod.
- **SC-073** (Round 14): SSE Lambda CloudWatch Log Group has metric filter for ADOT collector startup failures. Deliberately broken config triggers `ADOTCollectorStartupFailure` metric and alarm within first invocation. Verified by deploying malformed config to test environment.
- **SC-074**: All 5 identified silent failure paths (circuit breaker persistence, audit writes, notification delivery, self-healing fetch, fanout partial writes) emit a `SilentFailure/Count` metric with `FailurePath` dimension AND log a structured fallback line containing `metric_fallback: true` on metric emission failure.
- **SC-075**: Each Lambda log group has a CloudWatch Logs metric filter matching `{ $.metric_fallback = true }` that generates a backup metric, with an alarm using `treat_missing_data = "breaching"`.
- **SC-076**: The canary `EmissionHeartbeat` metric is included in the same `put_metric_data` API call as production metrics — not a separate call — and its alarm uses `treat_missing_data = "breaching"` with 3×60s evaluation periods.
- **SC-077**: All Lambda error alarms use percentage-based CloudWatch math expressions with a minimum invocation guard (>10); no Lambda error alarm uses absolute count thresholds.
- **SC-078**: Ingestion Lambda has P95 latency alarm < 48,000ms; Notification Lambda has P95 latency alarm < 24,000ms; SSE Streaming Lambda has P99 connection setup alarm < 5,000ms; Analysis Lambda has WARNING at 36,000ms and CRITICAL at 48,000ms.
- **SC-079**: CloudWatch dashboard displays all alarms across 3 severity-tiered widgets using alarm name prefix patterns (not ARN lists); a composite alarm aggregating all CRITICAL alarms is visible in the dashboard header.
- **SC-080**: An integration test confirms that a SendGrid API call produces an X-Ray subsegment or OTel span with destination URL containing `api.sendgrid.com`, verifying the httplib/urllib patching chain.
- **SC-081**: All CloudWatch alarms on application-emitted custom metrics use `treat_missing_data = "missing"`; canary/heartbeat alarms use `breaching`; only AWS-native metric alarms use `notBreaching`.
- **SC-082**: A validation check detects any FR present in the HL remediation checklist task table but absent from the corresponding fix-*.md work order file, with zero synchronization gaps.
- **SC-083**: Collision rate alarm evaluation periods are ≤2 periods for high collision and ≤3 periods for low collision; error rate alarm thresholds on all Lambdas are percentage-based.
- **SC-084** (Round 16): Every `FailurePath` dimension value of the `SilentFailure/Count` metric has an individual CloudWatch alarm. An aggregate composite alarm across all FailurePath-specific alarms is in the CRITICAL tier of the dashboard. Simulated silent failure (e.g., injected DynamoDB throttle on circuit breaker table) triggers the path-specific alarm within 1 evaluation period (1 minute).
- **SC-085** (Round 16): A Playwright test confirms `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header is present on outbound `fetch()` requests to API Gateway (same-origin) and Lambda Function URL SSE endpoint (cross-origin). The trace ID matches X-Ray format (`Root=1-{hex_timestamp}-{24_hex_digits}`). The test runs as a Phase 3 deployment gate and fails if any monitored fetch() call lacks the header.
- **SC-086** (Round 16): The canary publishes failure alerts to a cross-region SNS topic via direct `sns.publish()`. Simulated primary-region CloudWatch Metrics API degradation does NOT prevent the alert from reaching the SNS topic. The topic has at least one email and one webhook subscription confirmed by `sns:ListSubscriptionsByTopic`.
- **SC-087** (Round 16): A test trace from Ingestion Lambda through SNS to Analysis Lambda shows both Lambda segments and the SNS connecting segment under a single X-Ray trace ID in the service map. The verification gate is automated, uses retry-with-backoff (30s then 60s), and blocks Phase 2 deployment on failure.
- **SC-088** (Round 16): The API Gateway-fronted Dashboard Lambda has `IntegrationLatency` P99 alarms and `5XXError` rate alarms. The SSE Lambda has equivalent Lambda Function URL metric alarms (`Url5xxError`). Event-driven Lambdas (Ingestion, Analysis, Notification, Metrics) use Lambda-native metrics only (no HTTP interface). A simulated 6-second Lambda response triggers the IntegrationLatency alarm within 2 evaluation periods.
- **SC-089** (Round 16): `force_flush()` completes or aborts within 2,500ms regardless of ADOT Extension state. A hung Extension (TCP accept but no OTLP response) causes the flush to abort after 2,500ms — NOT block for 44+ seconds. The generator still yields `event: deadline` and terminates gracefully. Zero Lambda timeouts caused by runaway `force_flush()`.
- **SC-090** (Round 16): ADOT Extension unavailability during SSE streaming produces an `ADOTExtensionUnavailable` CloudWatch metric within the same Lambda invocation. Simulated Extension crash during streaming results in metric emission and alarm transition within 2 minutes — not waiting for the 10-minute canary cycle.
- **SC-091** (Round 16): X-Ray query `annotation.session_id = "{test_session_id}"` returns all traces for an SSE session across multiple reconnections. The `sse-reconnections` X-Ray Group generates a CloudWatch metric for reconnection frequency. Reconnection rate alarm fires when rate exceeds 10/minute system-wide.
- **SC-092** (Round 16): FR-124's `FailurePath` dimension has exactly 7 distinct values: `circuit_breaker_load`, `circuit_breaker_save`, `audit_trail`, `notification_delivery`, `self_healing_fetch`, `fanout_partial_write`, `parallel_fetcher_aggregate`. Each value produces a separate alarm (FR-134).
- **SC-093** (Round 16): The `metric_fallback` structured log line is JSON-formatted across all 6 Lambda functions. FR-125's CloudWatch Logs metric filter `{ $.metric_fallback = true }` matches fallback lines from every Lambda. Deliberately emitting a fallback line (by mocking `put_metric_data` to fail) in each Lambda's log group produces a metric filter match confirmed by `get-metric-data`.
- **SC-094** (Round 17): Every manually-created OTel span on the SSE Lambda that encounters an exception has BOTH `StatusCode.ERROR` set AND the exception recorded. An X-Ray query with `fault = true` on the error X-Ray Group (FR-034) returns spans from ALL error paths — including DynamoDB failures, internal processing errors, and BrokenPipeError disconnects (FR-085). Zero exceptions are invisible to X-Ray error filtering. Verified by triggering each of the 7 silent failure paths (SC-004) during streaming and confirming every resulting span has `fault=true` and populated `cause` field in the X-Ray segment document.
- **SC-095** (Round 17): The canary Lambda starts successfully and completes its health check cycle even when X-Ray SDK/OTel initialization fails. Simulated X-Ray service outage (ADOT Extension not running + X-Ray API returning 500) does NOT crash the canary. The canary emits `CanaryInitFailure` CloudWatch metric and still publishes to cross-region SNS (FR-136). Verified by deploying canary without ADOT Extension and confirming health check completes with degraded status.
- **SC-096** (Round 17): When X-Ray is healthy, the canary Lambda's own operations (X-Ray API calls, CloudWatch API calls, SNS publish) appear as traced subsegments in X-Ray. The canary's Powertools Tracer instrumentation produces the same trace structure as other non-streaming Lambdas. Verified by querying X-Ray for canary traces during normal operation.
- **SC-097** (Round 18): FR-124's inline text states "seven distinct silent failure paths" (not "five"). The 7 FailurePath dimension values match FR-142's enumeration and FR-134's alarm definitions exactly. Zero dangling alarms reference non-existent metrics. Verified by text inspection of FR-124 and cross-reference with FR-142 enumeration and FR-134 alarm ARN list.
- **SC-098** (Round 18): The frontend application does NOT issue any fetch() call to instrumented backend endpoints before CloudWatch RUM FetchPlugin initialization completes. A Playwright test simulates a cold page load with network throttling (Slow 3G) and verifies that the first outbound fetch() to the API carries `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` header. A second test simulates RUM CDN failure (blocked by CSP) and verifies the application proceeds after the 5-second timeout with a structured warning logged to the browser console.
- **SC-099** (Round 18): After FR-093's proactive flush fires, zero new OTel spans are created before the generator returns. A test triggers proactive flush by simulating remaining time <= 3000ms, then verifies the BSP queue is empty at generator return. Any span-creating code path executed after flush_fired=True logs via structured JSON instead. The test counts spans exported after the flush timestamp and asserts zero.
- **SC-100** (Round 18): Every caught exception in the SSE Lambda's 7 silent failure paths (FR-142 enumeration) has explicit `span.record_exception(exception)` AND `span.set_status(StatusCode.ERROR, str(exception))` as the first two statements in the except block. Code review gate: a grep-based CI check verifies that every `except` block within an OTel span context contains both calls. X-Ray query for `fault = true` on the error Group returns spans from ALL 7 failure paths when triggered.
- **SC-101** (Round 18): The canary Lambda attempts TracerProvider re-initialization on warm invocations when cold-start initialization failed. A test deploys the canary without ADOT Extension (causing cold-start failure per FR-145), invokes it twice (warm invocation), then starts ADOT Extension and invokes a third time. The third invocation's traces appear in X-Ray, confirming successful re-initialization. The `canary_reinit_attempt` structured log is emitted on each warm invocation while `_tracer_init_failed` is True.
- **SC-102** (Round 18): FR-117's automated trace validation script is the authoritative deployment gate for trace structure verification. The script defines minimum expected segment counts per Lambda function type and validates 100 traces per deployment. FR-109 gate (d) is documented as a one-time acceptance test. The automated script runs in FR-107 Phase 5 and blocks promotion on segment count violations.
- **SC-103** (Round 18): FR-018's scope statement explicitly names all covered Lambda functions and all exempted Lambda functions (with FR references). A new Lambda function added to the system without an explicit exemption FR defaults to fail-fast behavior. Verified by spec text inspection and by deploying a hypothetical 8th Lambda without FR-018 exemption — it crashes on X-Ray initialization failure.
- **SC-104** (Round 18): FR-132's staleness detection creates a GitHub issue within 1 hour of detecting HL document staleness. The next `/speckit.specify` round cannot proceed until the staleness issue is resolved or explicitly deferred. A test runs FR-132's audit against the current HL document and verifies the issue creation mechanism fires when gaps are detected. The issue body enumerates specific missing rounds, risk entries, and SC entries.
- **SC-105** (Round 18): Zero X-Ray span annotations or metadata contain PII (email, username, IP, sentiment text, API keys). A code review gate searches all `set_attribute()`, `add_annotation()`, and metadata assignment calls for variable names matching PII patterns (email, user, name, address, text, input, token, key, secret). X-Ray trace data from a production-like test run is queried and spot-checked for PII content. The PII check runs as part of FR-107 Phase 4 code review gate.
- **SC-064a** (Round 20, split from SC-064): Port-unreachable ADOT failure mode — stopping the ADOT Extension process causes `force_flush()` to fail fast (< 100ms) via ECONNREFUSED on localhost:4318. The SSE Lambda emits a structured log with `flush_timeout_cause: "extension_unavailable"` and `otlp_connection: "refused"`. FR-139's thread wrapper is NOT required for this code path — ECONNREFUSED returns immediately. Verified independently from SC-064b by killing the Extension process during a streaming invocation and measuring `force_flush()` duration.
- **SC-064b** (Round 20, split from SC-064, **amended Round 21**): Hung ADOT Extension failure mode — a mock TCP server on port 4318 that accepts connections but never sends an OTLP response causes `force_flush()` to hang until FR-139's 2500ms thread wrapper fires and aborts the call. The SSE Lambda emits a structured log with `flush_timeout_cause: "extension_hang"` and `otlp_connection: "established"` (label amended from `"bsp_or_extension_hang"` per FR-165 — BSP deadlock eliminated in SDK v1.33.0+). The generator yields `event: deadline` and terminates gracefully within 500ms of thread wrapper abort. Zero Lambda timeouts caused by this failure mode. Verified independently from SC-064a by deploying a mock TCP server during a streaming invocation.
- **SC-106** (Round 20, **amended Round 21**): Force flush completes or aborts within 2500ms (per FR-139) regardless of whether the timeout cause is ADOT Extension hang or any other blocking condition. BSP deadlock (opentelemetry-python#3886) is no longer a possible cause at SDK v1.39.1 (FR-165). When the flush times out, a structured log line differentiates the cause: `flush_timeout_cause` is `"extension_unavailable"` (ECONNREFUSED, fast failure) or `"extension_hang"` (connection established but no response). Verified by both SC-064a and SC-064b failure scenarios.
- **SC-107** (Round 20): A GitHub issue titled "HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18" exists in the repository, created as part of Round 20 acceptance. The issue enumerates: 9 missing FRs (FR-147 through FR-155), 9 missing SCs (SC-097 through SC-105), missing Round 18 Progress Log entry, and missing Round 18 Risk Assessment entries. The issue is labeled `doc-staleness` and `priority:high`. HL document synchronization MUST be completed before any task implementation begins.
- **SC-108** (Round 20): SSE Lambda cold start P95 latency is measured in preprod with the ADOT-embedded Docker image at 1024MB memory and is < 2000ms. The measurement is repeated after any ADOT version, OTel SDK version, or memory allocation change. The cold start measurement is documented in the HL document's Risk Assessment. If measured cold start exceeds 2000ms, the Lambda memory allocation is increased until the budget is met.
- **SC-109** (Round 20): The Lambda execution role for ADOT-instrumented Lambdas (SSE Lambda, canary Lambda) includes all 5 IAM actions: `xray:PutTraceSegments`, `xray:PutTelemetryRecords`, `xray:GetSamplingRules`, `xray:GetSamplingTargets`, `xray:GetSamplingStatisticSummaries`. A Terraform plan shows all 5 actions in the policy statement. ADOT Extension logs show `"Successfully fetched sampling rules"` on cold start, confirming centralized sampling is operational.
- **SC-110** (Round 20): A preprod test deploys the ADOT-instrumented SSE Lambda, initiates a 15-second streaming invocation, creates OTel spans at 1-second intervals throughout the streaming phase (14+ spans), and verifies ≥95% of streaming-phase spans appear in X-Ray within 60 seconds of invocation completion. The test runs 10 invocations and reports aggregate span retention rate. The test blocks FR-107 Phase 2 progression on failure.
- **SC-111** (Round 20): An X-Ray centralized sampling rule exists for the SSE Lambda Function URL with a configurable sampling rate (`FixedRate`). FR-038's cost alarms include a daily anomaly detection alarm that fires when X-Ray daily cost exceeds 200% of the trailing 7-day average. In dev/preprod, the sampling rule rate is 1.0 (100%). Production sampling rate is configurable via the X-Ray console without code deployment.
- **SC-112** (Round 20): Every CloudWatch alarm in the system has an explicit `treat_missing_data` value that matches the documented classification: `breaching` for canary heartbeat and `no_new_items` alarms; `missing` for all application metric alarms, Lambda error/latency alarms, and API Gateway alarms; `notBreaching` for cost/billing alarms only. A Terraform validation check confirms all `aws_cloudwatch_metric_alarm` resources have `treat_missing_data` explicitly set (not relying on provider defaults). Zero alarms omit the setting.
- **SC-113** (Round 20): An operational runbook section documents the manual X-Ray trace archival procedure: (a) identify incident time window, (b) estimate trace volume via `GetTraceSummaries` count, (c) export traces via `BatchGetTraces` to S3 bucket with 1-year retention, (d) record S3 path in post-mortem document. The procedure is cross-referenced from FR-122's rollback section. The procedure includes rate limit awareness (5 traces/request, 5 requests/sec) and estimated archival duration per trace volume.
- **SC-114** (Round 20): Every FR listed in the HL document's Work Order task table is present in the corresponding fix-*.md file with round annotation (e.g., "FR-100 (Round 12)"). FR-132's automated validation check reports zero synchronization gaps. Verified after the HL document synchronization mandated by FR-157, and re-verified after each subsequent specification round.
- **SC-115** (Round 21): FR-156's structured log label `"bsp_or_extension_hang"` is replaced with `"extension_hang"` across all code paths and documentation. The spec's catalogued span-loss vectors enumerate exactly TWO vectors: (1) ADOT Extension drop race (FR-074), (2) ADOT Extension hang (FR-139). FR-156's BSP deadlock vector is documented as RETIRED with the caveat that OTel SDK downgrade below v1.33.0 would re-expose it. Verified by text search for `"bsp_or_extension_hang"` in codebase and spec — zero occurrences remain.
- **SC-116** (Round 21): SC-040's verification of BSP queue non-overflow uses a span-count comparison method: a test `SpanProcessor` shim counts total `on_end()` calls (spans created), a test `SpanExporter` shim counts total `export()` spans received (spans exported), and the delta is zero during a standard 15-second streaming session. The old verification method ("confirming zero 'Queue is full' log entries") is documented as INVALID for SDK v1.39.1+. Verified by running a 15-second streaming session with the test shims and asserting created == exported.
- **SC-117** (Round 21): ADOT Extension crash during SSE streaming produces `ADOTExtensionUnavailable` CloudWatch metric (per FR-140) on the SAME invocation AND on ALL subsequent warm invocations on the same execution environment. A test kills the Extension process mid-stream, confirms metric emission on the current invocation, then triggers 3 additional warm invocations and confirms each emits the metric. Recovery occurs only on execution environment recycling (new cold start). Verified by monitoring Lambda invocation logs and CloudWatch metrics across warm invocations after Extension crash.
- **SC-118** (Round 21): An AWS Config rule or CloudTrail EventBridge rule monitors IAM policy changes on ADOT-instrumented Lambda execution roles. When any of the 5 required X-Ray IAM actions (FR-159) are removed from the role policy, a `SentimentAnalyzer/Reliability/IAMPolicyDrift` CloudWatch metric is emitted with `FunctionName` dimension within 15 minutes of the IAM change. A CloudWatch alarm fires on any non-zero value. Verified by removing `xray:GetSamplingRules` from the role and confirming the alarm transitions to ALARM state.
- **SC-119** (Round 21): The canary Lambda emits a heartbeat signal to an external monitoring endpoint (cross-region CloudWatch or third-party uptime service) on every successful invocation. Simulated double-failure (canary stops running + primary-region CloudWatch Alarms degraded) triggers the external heartbeat monitor's alert within 15 minutes. The external heartbeat is fire-and-forget — delivery failure does NOT affect canary execution. Verified by stopping the canary EventBridge rule and disabling primary-region alarm actions, then confirming the external monitor alerts.
- **SC-120** (Round 21): X-Ray PutTraceSegments TPS quota utilization is monitored. A CloudWatch alarm fires when `UnprocessedTraceSegments` count in PutTraceSegments API responses exceeds zero, indicating segments were permanently lost due to throttling. The alarm references AWS Service Quotas quota code `L-AB6D2D9B` with current region default (~2,500 TPS). Verified by inspecting Terraform alarm configuration and confirming the metric source.
- **SC-121** (Round 21): FR-163's trace archival runbook accounts for the 6-hour maximum `GetTraceSummaries` time window per request. The runbook includes a time estimation formula: `archival_minutes = ceil(incident_hours / 6) * (trace_count / 500) / 60 + trace_count / (5 * 5) / 60`. For a 24-hour incident with 100,000 traces, the estimated archival time is documented as ~70-90 minutes. Verified by runbook text inspection.
- **SC-122** (Round 21): Terraform configuration for X-Ray Groups and Sampling Rules includes a comment documenting current resource count against the 25-per-region quota. A CI validation check counts `aws_xray_group` and `aws_xray_sampling_rule` resources and warns when count exceeds 20 (80% of default quota). Verified by running the CI check and confirming the count is below threshold.
- **SC-123** (Round 21): The spec documents that X-Ray encryption at rest is active by default using an AWS-managed key. The operational runbook notes CMK configuration availability via `PutEncryptionConfig` for organizations requiring customer-controlled encryption. No action is required for default encryption — this SC is verified by AWS X-Ray documentation review.
- **SC-124** (Round 21, **CORRECTED Round 25 Clarification**): Centralized X-Ray sampling rules control root-span Lambdas: Function URL (SSE), EventBridge (Ingestion, Canary, Metrics, Notification), and SNS (Analysis). Only the Dashboard Lambda is API Gateway-fronted and inherits parent sampling decisions — centralized rules have NO effect on it. **CORRECTION**: R21 incorrectly listed Ingestion, Analysis, and Notification as API Gateway-fronted. Ground truth from Terraform: Ingestion=EventBridge, Analysis=SNS, Notification=EventBridge+SNS. Implementers can verify by changing the centralized rule rate in preprod and confirming all Lambda trace volumes change EXCEPT Dashboard.
- **SC-125** (Round 21): An ADOT version upgrade runbook exists, cross-referenced from FR-070 and FR-110. The runbook enumerates 8 verification gates (release notes review, Dockerfile update, CI config validation, cold start re-measurement, streaming span retention, trace validation, IAM verification, production deployment). The runbook mandates ADOT upgrades be deployed independently of application code changes. Verified by runbook text inspection and cross-reference check.
- **SC-126**: PutTraceSegments quota monitoring differentiates between AWS default (500 TPS) and account-applied quota, with deployment checklist requiring quota increase for new environments.
- **SC-127**: A sampling graduation document exists with 4 defined phases, traffic thresholds, sampler environment variable configurations, and CloudWatch alarm triggers for transitions.
- **SC-128**: A kill switch activation runbook exists documenting 5 threshold conditions with specific metrics/alarms and actions (sampling reduction before kill switch).
- **SC-129**: All 6 Lambda functions carry `deploy-sha` tag and `DEPLOYMENT_VERSION` environment variable, with post-apply CI check detecting cross-function version skew.
- **SC-130**: Span attribute allow-list defined per Lambda, enforced at creation time via `SpanProcessor.on_start()`, with CI validation that all `set_attribute()` calls use listed keys.
- **SC-131**: Canary traces carry `annotation.synthetic = true`, X-Ray Group `production-traces` excludes them, `synthetic` key absent from non-canary allow-lists.
- **SC-132**: Annotation budget documented allocating ≤50 per trace with per-component limits and CI tracking (warn >40, fail >50).
- **SC-133**: ADOT resource overhead budget documented: cold start ≤500ms, steady-state memory ≤70 MB, warm invocation ≤5ms.
- **SC-134**: GitHub issue "HL Document Staleness: Missing Round 18" exists in repository with FR-157/SC-107 cross-references.
- **SC-135** (Round 23): A CI static analysis gate scans all Python source files for `.set_attribute(` calls and verifies each call uses a key from the per-Lambda allow-list (FR-191). Any `.set_attribute()` call using a key not in the allow-list fails the CI check. A runtime audit `SpanProcessor` (registered last in the chain) logs violations in `on_end()` when span attributes contain keys not in the allow-list. A CloudWatch Logs metric filter on the violation log emits `AllowListViolation` metric. Verified by introducing a `.set_attribute("unlisted_key", value)` call and confirming CI rejection AND runtime metric emission.
- **SC-136** (Round 23): The `TracerProvider` registers SpanProcessors in this exact order: (1) FR-191 attribute allow-list `SpanProcessor`, (2) `BatchSpanProcessor`, (3) FR-191 runtime audit `SpanProcessor`. A unit test instantiates the `TracerProvider` and asserts `_active_span_processor._span_processors` list order matches this sequence. Verified by inspecting the TracerProvider initialization code path.
- **SC-137** (Round 23): X-Ray annotation budget allocation accounts for exception attributes. Each `record_exception()` call consumes up to 3 annotation slots (`exception.type`, `exception.message`, `exception.stacktrace`). The per-span budget documented in FR-193 reserves 3 slots for exception attributes, reducing the application-available budget from the per-component limit. A CI check counts maximum possible annotations per span (including exception paths) and warns at >40, fails at >50. Verified by triggering an exception in every silent failure path and confirming total annotation count stays within budget.
- **SC-138** (Round 23): An OTel Python SDK upgrade runbook exists, cross-referenced from FR-101 and FR-194. The runbook enumerates 7 verification gates: (1) changelog review for BSP behavior changes, (2) `BoundedAttributes` eviction policy verification, (3) `force_flush()` timeout behavior verification, (4) `SpanProcessor` callback contract verification, (5) requirements.txt pin update, (6) cold start re-measurement, (7) streaming span retention re-test. The runbook mandates SDK upgrades be deployed independently of application code changes. Verified by runbook text inspection.
- **SC-139** (Round 23): Powertools Tracer is pinned to a specific version range in `requirements.txt` (e.g., `aws-lambda-powertools>=2.x,<3.0`). The version constraint is documented in FR-195 with rationale. A `pip install` with the pinned constraint produces zero `auto_patch` behavior differences from the version tested during initial implementation. Verified by running integration tests with the pinned version.
- **SC-140** (Round 23): The canary detects ADOT Extension degraded state (alive but non-functional) by verifying not just that test traces are submitted but that they appear in X-Ray with expected segment structure. A test deploys a mock Extension that accepts OTLP spans on :4318 but silently discards them (simulating recovered panic in exporter goroutine). The canary detects zero retrievable traces despite zero connection errors and fires the alarm within 2 consecutive intervals. Verified by deploying mock Extension and confirming canary alarm fires.
- **SC-141** (Round 23): The spec documents canary detection latency as 5-15 minutes (1-3 consecutive 5-minute intervals depending on failure alignment). Brief X-Ray outages lasting less than 10 minutes may go undetected. This limitation is documented in the operational runbook with the rationale that reducing the canary interval below 5 minutes would increase X-Ray cost and Lambda invocation count disproportionately to the detection improvement. Verified by spec and runbook text inspection.
- **SC-142** (Round 23): Per-Lambda sampling configuration documents the architectural split: API Gateway Lambdas (Dashboard, Ingestion, Analysis, Notification) inherit parent sampling decisions from API Gateway and are NOT affected by X-Ray centralized sampling rules. Function URL Lambda (SSE) and EventBridge Lambdas (Canary, Metrics) are governed by centralized sampling rules. The sampling graduation plan (FR-198) defines per-Lambda phase transitions only for the centralized-rule-governed Lambdas. Verified by spec text inspection and preprod sampling rate change test (only SSE/Canary/Metrics trace volumes change).
- **SC-143** (Round 23): Deployment version skew tolerance window is documented as 15 minutes (FR-199). A CI post-apply check queries all Lambda function configurations and compares `DEPLOYMENT_VERSION` values. If any function has a version different from the deploying version AND the deployment started more than 15 minutes ago, the check fails. During the tolerance window, the check emits a WARNING. Verified by simulating a staggered deployment and confirming the check transitions from WARNING to FAIL after 15 minutes.
- **SC-144** (Round 24): OTel Collector source code (`exporter/exporterhelper/internal/queue/async_queue.go`) confirms zero `recover()` calls in pipeline consumer goroutines. Span-loss vector catalog updated: "ADOT recovered panic" reclassified from "NEW VECTOR CANDIDATE" to "RETIRED/DENIED". FR-196 amended from recovered-panic detection to exporter-backend-error detection. Verified by source code inspection and spec text update.
- **SC-145** (Round 24): Canary test validates detection of ADOT exporter backend error state. A test configures ADOT Extension with X-Ray endpoint returning persistent 429 responses (or mock endpoint). Canary detects sustained trace loss (zero retrievable traces despite non-zero submissions) and fires alarm within 2 consecutive intervals. Distinguished from drop race (vector #1) by sustained near-100% loss rate. Verified by deploying mock X-Ray backend and confirming canary alarm fires.
- **SC-146** (Round 24): All spec references to `ADOT_LAMBDA_FLUSH_TIMEOUT` environment variable are removed or corrected to reference the Lambda platform's 2-second extension shutdown window. No code, configuration, or documentation references a non-existent environment variable. Verified by full-text search of spec, HL checklist, and codebase.
- **SC-147** (Round 24): `aws-otel-lambda/adot/collector/lambdacomponents/default.go` confirms the ADOT Lambda Extension includes zero processors. Spec documents Python SDK as the sole span processing enforcement point. All PII filtering (FR-191), allow-listing, and annotation budgeting (FR-193) FRs reference Python SDK SpanProcessor chain, not ADOT-level processing. Verified by source code inspection and spec text review.
- **SC-148** (Round 24): Requirements checklist contains tracking rows for 100% of spec FRs (FR-001 through FR-204+) and SCs (SC-001 through SC-148+). Every row has a checkbox and description. Superseded FRs are annotated with `[SUPERSEDED by FR-NNN]`. Verified by counting checklist rows and comparing against spec FR/SC enumeration.

---

## Clarifications

### Session 2026-03-09

- Q: Has CloudFront been reintroduced to the architecture since Features 1203-1207, or does "CDN" refer to a different component? → A: CloudFront is NOT in the architecture (confirmed — removed in Features 1203-1209, replaced by Amplify). CDN-to-DB tracing is a **documented blind spot** — deferred intentionally. Future CloudFront tracing would be additive (~3-5 FRs), not a rearchitecture, because CloudFront supports Active Tracing natively and propagates `X-Amzn-Trace-Id` to origin. The existing line 1118 restriction note remains valid.
- Q: Should cache visibility be per-request boolean (`cache_hit`) or aggregate only (`cache_hit_rate`)? → A: Both (Option A). FR-007 amended to add per-lookup `cache_hit` boolean subsegment annotation alongside existing aggregate `cache_hit_rate` on the parent span. Enables `annotation.cache_hit = false` filtering for debugging emergent issues.
- Q: Should ingestion/bucket write traces use per-bucket subsegments (8x multiplier) or a single subsegment with counts? → A: Single subsegment with counts (Option B). FR-205 added: one subsegment per ingestion with `ticker_symbol`, `buckets_written`, `buckets_failed`, and `failed_buckets` string annotation for bucket-level failure identification without 8x subsegment overhead.
- Q: Should SDK-internal research findings (source file paths, retry formulas, Go code references) be extracted to a companion doc or kept inline? → A: Keep inline (Option A). Research evidence is load-bearing justification for constraints. Separating "what" from "why" risks drift and weakens spec persuasiveness. Single implementer workflow means full spec is loaded once.
- Q: Should ingestion subsegment include a latency threshold annotation (`is_slow` boolean) or raw duration only? → A: Raw `ingestion_duration_ms` only (Option B). Threshold judgment at query time avoids historical discontinuities when thresholds tighten. Operators filter with `annotation.ingestion_duration_ms > N` and adjust N without redeployment. FR-205 updated.
- Q: Should the canary validate subsegment completeness for API Gateway-fronted traces? → A: Yes (Option A). FR-207 added: canary sends synthetic request through API Gateway → Dashboard Lambda, validates trace contains both API Gateway segment and Lambda subsegments. Detects ADOT crash on Dashboard Lambda that API Gateway's own segment would mask.
- Q: FR-205 annotation cleanup — `buckets_failed` (int) and `failed_buckets` (string) are redundant; what constitutes "failed"? → A: Collapsed to single `failed_buckets` string (count derived from string). "Failed" means retries-exhausted only — data was NOT written. Retried-then-succeeded = success. Transient throttling visible via DynamoDB `ThrottledRequests` metric, not trace annotation. Also removed redundant `buckets_written` (implicit from 8 - failed count).
- Q: Should per-lookup `cache_hit` create new subsegments or annotate existing poll-cycle subsegments? → A: Annotate existing (Option B). `cache_hit` boolean added to the poll-cycle subsegment, not as a separate subsegment. Avoids ~180 additional subsegments per SSE invocation drowning the X-Ray waterfall. Same filtering capability (`annotation.cache_hit = false`). FR-007 updated.
- Q: Should `failed_buckets` distinguish DynamoDB failures from deadline-skipped buckets? → A: No extra variable (Option B). FR-206's `flush_reason = "deadline"` annotation already disambiguates. If `flush_reason` present + `failed_buckets` non-empty = skipped due to timeout. If `flush_reason` absent + `failed_buckets` non-empty = DynamoDB write failure. Two annotations cover both cases.
- Q: Should event-driven Lambdas get deadline-aware force_flush like the SSE Lambda (FR-093)? → A: Analysis Lambda only (Option B). It has the highest timeout risk: up to 32 sequential DynamoDB update_item calls per ticker × ticker count. Natural checkpoint between each of the 8 resolution iterations. Parallelization rejected — OTel threading.local() context breaks in worker threads. FR-206 added. Also corrected FR-205: bucket writes happen in Analysis Lambda, not Ingestion Lambda.
- Q: Are Ingestion, Analysis, and Notification Lambdas API Gateway-fronted? → A: **NO — spec error corrected.** Ground truth from Terraform: Ingestion=EventBridge (5min schedule), Analysis=SNS, Notification=EventBridge+SNS. Only Dashboard Lambda is API Gateway-fronted. SC-124, FR-094, FR-138, FR-161, FR-179, FR-198 corrected. This means centralized sampling rules apply to 6 of 7 Lambdas (all except Dashboard), significantly simplifying the sampling graduation plan. Also corrected: specs/427-fix-lambda-zip-packaging/spec.md line 16 (API Gateway→EventBridge). Also fixed: README.md mermaid.live badge URL regenerated from correct architecture.mmd (removed stale Auth Lambda diagram).
